# Miracles of Quran
*Source: KASHKOLE, Binder 35 (The Wise Reminder), Chapter 176. 11 topics. Language: ur.*

<!-- section 1 (id=5776, raw_sort=1): Is Quran Human Or Divine Speech -->
It is from the ettiquettes of our Islamic tradition to begin any religious conversation with the praise of Allah(Subhanhu Wa Ta'ala) and by sending blessings and salutations on his beloved messenger. So I'm going to recite this SALAAM which is in Arabic. So don't get scared and run away. The session is still going to be in English. Last time I did this, a bunch of kids freaked out and ran away hearing the Arabic of the Salaam :)

Is Quran human or divine speech (25 min)

One of our DAIs, Syedna Jaffar bin Mansoor AlYaman QR states in one of his books

⟪ar-quote:فجعلَ اللہُ لِکُلِّ أَوَّلِ مِنہُ آخَر⟫

For every beginning Allah has placed within it an end;

⟪ar-quote:وَلِکُلِّ آخِر مِنہُ غاَیَۃ⟫

and for every end there is a goal;

⟪ar-quote:وَلِکُلِّ غَایۃٌ نِّھَایَۃ لا یَبلُغُ أمْدَھاَ⟫

and every goal has a limit; the full extent of which cannot be achieved.

In other words, the purpose of every journey is its destination. So I thought I'd being by talking about the purpose and the goal of this sessions; and give you an idea of how we're going to travel along this path. My goal is to systematically analyze the Quran with you, in order to see if this is the word of God or not! We're told that every messenger was given a miracle as proof for their prophethood. MOOSA (AS) was given the staff; EISA (AS) could bring the dead back to life. Suleman AS could interpret the language of animals and birds. So every prophet was given some form of miracle to prove the authenticity of their prophethood. And Rasul Allah(Salallahu alayhi wa aalihee wa sallam) was given Quran as the ultiamte miracle, and a decisive proof of his prophethood; not just for the people of his tim but for all of humanity till the end of time.

So that is the question we will try to answer. Is Quran a miracle or not? And if it is, then what makes it a miracle. To me, this seems like a good first logical step. Because once I'm convinced that this book is divine, it organically answers other philosophical questions such as is there a God or not. Is there such a thing as heaven and hell. Are there angels? Are there messengers? 

Because in my opinion, the only "definitive" proof there is abou the existence of god is the Quran. So if the Quran is not good enough as that proof, then nothing really is; and nothing ever will be.

So we Aristotle's approach of questioning, the first real question is who claims the Quran to be a divine speech? That would be Rasul Allah(Salallahu alayhi wa aalihee wa sallam). He's the one who said that Jibraeel AS would inspire him with this divine message, before he would recite the verses that we have call the Quran today. So now either he was telling the truth, or he was lying about it (معاذ اللہ). If he was telling the truth, then problem solved, end of sessions - have a wonderful life! If he wasn't telling the truth, then what are the possibilities here? Either he was himself authoring this speech, or someone else was delivering it to him. Now historically there is no account of any contention over the Quran being the speech of someone else. The only argument that exists, is that is Quran the speech of Rasul Allah(Salallahu alayhi wa aalihee wa sallam); or is it the speech of God. Because if there were other parties involved, then someone would have stepped forward and taken credit for it, especially after the popularity this book achieved.

OK..... So maybe the prophet came up with this message himself and then somehow bluffed an entire nation into believing that this book is from god (معاذ اللہ). The problem with that argument is that the Quran is essentially a spoken text. It was not revealed as a written text. The compilation of the Quran in the book form that we see today, happened several decades after the death of the prophet (Salallahu alayhi wa aalihee wa sallam). But for many many years, the Quran remained purely a spoken text. And what's more interesting is that it is unanimously agreed that the Quran was an "extempore" speech. The prophet would be inspired with the divine message by Jibraeel (AS), and he would then begin reciting the words of the Quran. And once those words were spoken, there was no going back.  There could be no revision, no modification, no improvement on those words. You know how when we write a speech, we have mulitple drafts? And we keep revising it over and over again until it's finally ready? There's none of that with the Quran. Once the prophet recited the AYAATS of the Quran, that's it! They were set in stone. And we know that he was delivering the Quran in large public gatherings.

OK..... So maybe he came up with this speech in the privacy of his own home, and then revised and edited it over and over again, until it became perfect, and then the next morning when he was in a group, maybe he pretended to get revelation, and then delivered the speech that he had prepared last night, in front of that live audience. That's possible, right?

The problem with that theory, is that a major portion of the Quran was revealed as instant and direct responses to questions and comments of the disbelievers of Mecca. They would ask him a question, or pass a comment, or criticize him, and right there and then, JIBRAEEL AS would come down with answers or responses from Allah. And the prophet would begin reciting the AYAATS. So revelation was happening as a "live" show!

OK..... So maybe, this conspiracy runs deeper. Maybe, he bribed, threatened, or preped a bunch of people beforehand saying, "Listen! Tomorrow at such and such time, I'll be at that location. Come up to me and ask me this particular question, and then I'll respond with the verses of the Quran. And make sure you sound angry and hateful! Just so that it creates the right effect with the people there!"

Now the problem with that theory, is that history tells us that at the time these revelations were taking place, Rasul Allah did not have that kind of pull with the people of Mecca. He was pretty much a nobody at that time. He was not rich, so he had nothing to bribe people with. He was not in power, so he couldn't threaten anyone, or make future promises of glory or rewards. He was not formally educated in any school. He did not formally study with any teacher who might have taught him the historic events of past prophets that the Quran reveals. Nobody ever taught him the art of BALAGHA or eloquence, which was very much an acquired skill at that time. He never left MECCA for another city, so we could say he learnt all these things from someone else in different city or country. He was living right there in front of them his entire life. Also if he was taught by teachers, someone would have stepped forward saying, "I taught him that! Everything he knows, guess who taught him?". But there is no account of that happening historically. So these are some very solid arguments, defending him against the allegation that, he might have staged this entire process of revelation just to claim prophethood.

But let's just get really crazy here and say, that is what happened! He somehow prepped a bunch a people to ask him these questions before an audience (and BTW not a single person noticed that happening, nor did any of them turn around and snitch on him, over a period of 23 years). But let's say he somehow pulled that off.

Now the thing is, the majority of the people who were asking him these questions, that the Quran was responding to, were his sworn mortal enemies. People who hated him; who wanted him dead. People who battled him later; people who wanted to show him down, destroy him at any and every cost. And many of these people did not even convert to ISLAM. They actually died disbelievers. So if you think about that, that's not a very genius plan, is it? Hey! Ask me questions, I'll come up with this great response pretending its the Quran, but don't believe in me. Remain disbelievers! Ahhh..... I don't think so!

So all of this can only mean one thing. That the Quran was coming from Rasul Allah(Salallahu alayhi wa aalihee wa sallam) himself; and it was completely spontaneous and an unscripted speech, before a live audience. But this still doesn't mean that it is divine speech. It doesn't rule out the possibility that this still could be human speech. But at least we've now narrowed down the scope of arguments dramatically. We agree now that the Quran is an impromptu speech coming directly from Rasul Allah(Salallahu alayhi wa aalihee wa sallam). The only question that remains, is that is it divine or is it human speech! And this actually makes our lives so much easy. Because if we can somehow prove, that human beings *are* capable of such a magnificent speech that the Quran is, then that's it! Problem solved! Its not a miracle, and Muhammad (Salallahu alayhi wa aalihee wa sallam) is not a messenger of Allah; ISLAM is a false religion. End of story!

Because if this is human speech, it should be really easy to poke holes in it. Because as human beings, we know our weaknesses and shortcomings; especially when it comes to speech. Think about this! Rasul Allah(Salallahu alayhi wa aalihee wa sallam) is delivering this unscripted speech before a live audience, that is made up all sorts of people. Famil, friends, enemies, strangers, Christian priests, Jewish Rabi's, idol worshippers, all sorts of poeple. And he's delivering the Quran going through a slew of emotions. When he's happy Quran is being revealed. When he's sad Quran is being revealed. When he's in battle Quran is being revealed. When he's afraid, when he's anxious, when he's angry, when he's frustrated, when his son dies, when his daugther cries, when his grandsons are starving, when he wins a battle, when he loses a battle, the Quran is being revealed. And as human beings, we know what happens, when we speak under hightened emotions. We say things we don't mean! We fumble our words! We pretty much always say things, either in excess of what needed to be said; or we hold ourselves back, and not say what we really wanted to say. In other words, our mental and emotional states constantly influence our conversations. And then we have to go back and apologize for what we said. "That's not what I meant! I'm so sorry! I was just angry! Allow me to rephrase what I said! You are not a big fat bold potato", right? So if this is human speech, it should be really easy to poke holes in it. Because remember! Once he says it, that's it! There's no going back! There's no cut and paste! There's no spellcheck! There's no "Fix my grammer as I go" option here. You understand?

And so this is the subject of our conversation in the remainder of these sessions. You will see for yourself that it is simply "impossible" for impromptu speech, delivered under the influence of all sorts of emotions, over a period of 23 years (that's over 8000 days); before a live audience, who were masters of this language; who would tear you apart; who would destroy you if you made as much as a grammatical mistake. For the conditions and circumstances under which the Quran was revealed, you will see that it is absolutely impossible for this speech to be so incredibly amazing, and so insanely perfect.

And if at the end of the sessions you agree that YES! ABSOLUTELY! Without the shadow of the slightest doubt, this speech could not be human speech, then naturally you have to also accept, that this is divine speech. And if this is a divine speech, then there is a God! And if there is a God, then what he says about all the meta-physical realities in this book must also be true! Because we as human beings, we are forced to deny our own divinity, and the divinity of all other human beings by recognizing our weaknesses and our shortcoming, espeically when it comes to language and speech.

So I wanted to begin by setting the context of our conversation.

---

THINGS YOU MUST KNOW ABOUT THESE SESSIONS:(20 min)

I few things I want clarify before we begin these sessions. I use lots of material from various external sources. Everything I intend on sharing with you in these sessions is available on the internet, on websites, on YouTube, on Vimeo. Obviously this material is not something I came up with. I'm sharing the marvellous work of other scholars with you. And this became a huge issue in my previous sessions. He should not be sharing outside material! He's literally using the exact material word, for word from all these sites and videos. So that's why I wanted to bring this up right at the onset of these sessions, because I am! There is this misonception in our JAMAAT that we should not study anything that is outside the realm of our books. Anyone who's read CHAHAL SABAQ knows that it's not true. Because Syedna Ghulam Hussain Sahab QR clearly states in CHAHAL SABAQ that you should never hate the knowledge of others. In fact you should make an effort to learn from them if they have something good to offer. But he emphasises to understand our own theology first. Because there is a lot of good and bad concepts out there. So if you don't know your own theological principles you can end up straying from the path. But no true AALIM of our JAMAAT has ever hated or discarded external knowledge. I like to consider myself a student of truth, and I am happy to take it from anywhere I can find it. Maulana Ali says, ⟪ar:الحکمۃ ضال المؤمن⟫, Wisdom is the lost property of a believer. If you lose your phone, and you find it with someone else, You're not going to say, "Wait! Are you Sulemani?", Go take AHAD Shareef first so that I can have my phone back!..... Would you say that? NO! Hand it over brother! right?

Also there is a hadees of Rasul Allah(Salallahu alayhi wa aalihee wa sallam) in which he said, "Seek knowledge, even if you have to go to China!". Last time I checked, Confucius wasn't sulemani! I haven't heard of any Chinese Duaat, have you? Because what that HADEES means is, "Seek knowledge, even if you get it from outside". And the reason SULEMANIYAT is the ultimate truth, is because it is open to ALL truth! I like to believe I'm a member of the SULEMANI sect and not the SULEMANI cult.

But then there are people in the JAMAAT, who prefer not to hear a single word unless it is from our DAWAT books. And I completely respect that. To each his own! So that's why I want to share this with you right at the beginning, that if knowledge makes you uncomfortable just because it doesn't come from the DAWAT SHAREEF, then very respectfully you should not be in these sessions. Because I don't want you to go through these only to find out that some of this material was not from our books. 'Cause it's not! What I have done, is literally taken hundreds of hours of material and condensed it into 10-12 hours for you; so that *you* don't have to spend hundreds of hours understanding this. And InshaAllah nothing I share with you will conflict with our principles; in fact they complement them. That's the first thing I wanted to share.

My second concern is for the young adults in the group. The only reason you should be in these sessions, is because you want to learn about your religion; and because you're happy learning it. None of you should be here because your mom is making you sit through this, or your dad is making you sit through this. If your heart is not in it; if you feel you're not ready for it, then you should not be here. When you're ready for it, InshaAllah I'll do the sessions for you again later, if you want me to.

Also please do not record these sessions and forward it to other people. There are certain people who did that in my previous group and I ran into all sorts of trouble. What happens when you forward the sessions to others, is that you rob them of the opportunity to clarify their questions and concerns. So they end up with an inaccurate or misunderstood concept. And when that happens, guess who gets blamed? I get blamed; because it's my voice in the recording. For those attending the sessions, I've built a proper context for you over a period of time. But if someone randomly listens to one of the session, and doesn't have the context that goes along with it, then obviously they will misunderstand, and I will get into trouble.

Look..... These sessions are my sincere effort to share the beauty of our religion with young adults. In fact it's not even just me, there is a whole team that works behind the scenes to make these sessions possible. First and foremost is my teacher Mulla Javeed bhai. Whatever I am; and whatever I know is because of him. That's why he's a part of every whatsapp group I create. Because I want to have that accountability to him where he's aware of what I'm sharing and teaching, and how the group is responding to it. Also this group would not have been formed if it wasn't for the efforts of Kafia and Anees. Ayaz is administering the group. If you just look at the instructions he posted, you can tell how much thought and effort he put into it. Then there are people who supported me with their honest feedback and advise in how to make things easier and better for the kids to understand. I have amazing kids from my previous group who've supported me through these sessions like you won't believe. So these sessions are a major team effort. I end up getting the credit because I'm the one teaching it; but in reality none of this would have been possible without the support of certain family members and friends; all of which goes completely unnoticed. And none of us are getting anything out of this. So all I ask in return, on behalf of all of us, that you please don't do anything that would make things difficult for us.

Ask question! Ask as many questions as you like. Ask stupid questions! I LOVE stupid questions. I myself am the king of stupid questions. I wouldn't have acquired the knowledge I have today without my dumb questions. So please ask all you want. If the answer is not relevant to our sessions, or outside the scope of our sessions, I'll try to answer it privately on a one-on-one basis. If you feel anything I teach conflicts with your existing concepts, then let's talk it out. Maybe there is something I did not explain properly. Maybe there is something you misunderstood. We can sort it out. But please don't go complaining to other people. If I have a problem with you, I'll directly take it up with you. I won't go and complain to your parents, right? So show me the same courtesy.

These are some of my concerns that I wanted to bring to the table before we begin. Because I really want this to be an enjoyable and a great learning experience for all of us collectively as a group. But I can't do that if I have to constantly deal with all these problems on the side.

Now as for my teaching style, what I normally do is that I work with one kid per session. For example Ayaz and Kafia's daughter Fatera has agreed to work me on these sessions. What I will do is try to explain the material just to her and make sure she understands. And the idea is that through our back and forth, everyone in the group understands. I would really like more kids to participate, so if anyone else is interested please let me know. I'm not going to force anyone into doing something they're not happy to do.

I prefer the word "sessions" than "asbaaq". Because SABAQ has the implications of a learned scholar teaching the material (which I'm not), and it's supposed to be a very serious event. And I'm alergic to all kinds of seriousness. I crack jokes [obnoxious jokes mostly]; Sarcasim is definitely on the menu. Basically I like to have fun. This is definitely a very serious subject, but doesn't mean we can't enjoy the learning process, right?

---

MYTHS (30 min)

The next thing I want to do, is address certain fundamental misconceptions that become problematic in the study of Quran. There are too many misconceptions, to go over all of them. I'll only talk about a couple that are directly related to the topic we are discussing.

**MYTH: I can study the Quran all by myself!**

There are people who tell me that they studied the Quran, and then they give me a list of things they don't understand or have a problem with. Then when I ask, Who did you study the quran with? "Oh! I just studied it myself". Well my friend! That's your problem right there! You cannot study the Quran yourself and claim to understand this book; just as you cannot read a medical journal, or a book on surgery and become a brain surgeon. The notion that I studied the Quran by myself is absolutely ridiculous!

The first thing you're asked when you go for a job interview, is which school did you graduate from?  In other words, who did you study with? Now, if you need proper schooling for material sciences that you study in your own native language, it stands to reason that you would certainly need some level of schooling for a book that deals with meta-physical realities in a language that you don't even understand. Isn't that true? So just like any other subject, the study of Quran requires a serious commitment. It takes a lot of time and effort to properly study the Quran; under the guidance and supervision of a qualified teacher. You can't understand the Quran through a casual read while watching Netflix.

**Some of you are going..... Well why not?! I can read English! If I can understand Shakespere why can't I understand the Quran?**

[diagram: Orange heart cracked down the middle: left half labelled 'AYATS / Content', right half labelled 'Context / Circumstances surrounding revelation'.]
  (see ../images/001.png)
  *Note:* Pedagogical: every Quranic verse has both Content (text) and Context (circumstances of revelation, asbab al-nuzul).

The reason you can't is because all the Quran provides is "content". What it does not provide is "context"! None of the AYAATS in the Quran explain the context in which they're revealed. And we all know what happens, when we take content out of context, right? Look at everything that's happening around us in the name of ISLAM! This is what you get when you study the Quran yourself. When you take the content and leave out the context! Hey! Let's just take this one verse; leave out the surrounding verses; forget the specific circumstances and situations surrounding their revelation, and lets just blow up a bunch of innocent kids in the name of ISLAM. Or let's just oppress women, and degrade them in the name of ISLAM by taking all their rights away. Because look! it says right here in the Quran!

**Now why doesn't Quran provide the context?**

If I tell you, "You see that door, that has that big huge lock on it! Unlock it and go inside". What's going to be your obvious question? Where's the key? Who has the key? So Allah designed the Quran  this way - locking the content, with the lock of context. Why? So we are forced to find the one who has the key! The one who can provide the right context! Who is that?

Rasul Allah(Salallahu alayhi wa aalihee wa sallam) before he died, he said:
⟪ar-quote:إِنِّی تَارِکٌ فِیکُمُ الثَّقَلَیْنِ ..... مَا إِنْ تَمَسَّکْتُمْ بِهِمَا لَنْ تَضِلُّوا⟫

I am leaving among you two precious things۔ As long as you remain connected with both, you will never be misguided

⟪ar-quote:کِتَابَ اللَّهِ وَ عِتْرَتِی أَهْلَ بَیْتِی⟫

The book of Allah and my progeny (the Ahlul-Bait... the Imams that will come in my lineage). In other words, I'm leaving behind the lock and the key. I'm leaving behind this content, and the one who can provide its context.

⟪ar-quote:وَ إِنَّهُمَا لَنْ یَفْتَرِقَا⟫

Because without a doubt, these two will not separate from one another. What two? The Quran and the Imams; the content and the context. They will never separate from each other

⟪ar-quote:حَتَّى یَرِدَا عَلَیَّ الْحَوْضَ⟫

Until they both reunite with me at the fountain.

And so this deliberate "need to seek out the true Imam" is embedded directly with the structure of the Quran, and there are numerous AYATS within the Quran asking people to seek them out:
⟪ar-quote:فَسْـَٔلُوٓا۟ أَهْلَ ٱلذِّكْرِ إِن كُنتُمْ لَا تَعْلَمُونَ⟫

Ask the people of this book, if you do not have knowledge. And this is why we have this hierarchy of structured religion; where are our elders (our Duaat and Manaseeb); they provide us with the proper context for this content. And once you have both, there is no problem; there is no confusion.

**Why was it done this way? Wouldn't it be better to simply provide the content and the context?**

The content of the Quran are the principles and the fundamental teachings of the Quran, which are timeless. They are universal, they are timeless, and they are immutable. They never change! But their applications and their implementations change over time. If you deeply study the Quran, it specifically deals with one particular context, which is the Arabs of that time. That's why you find references of camels, and horeses and swords etc; all of which are very particular to that time period. But as time changes, as human intellect evolves, their environments, their challenges, and their needs change. In other words, the context changes over time. But what doesn't change? The content! The underlying principles of the Quran. And so now you need somone to explain and implement those exact same universal principles in the context of modern times. And only the IMAM of that particular time can do that. And InshaAllah I'll show you some good examples of this as we progress through the sessions.

**MYTH: Next one is that I can understand the Quran through a translation in any language other than Arabic**

I believe this is the greatest misconception of all! And it is essentially the root cause of all the other misconceptions. It is absolutely impossible to understand the true meanings of Quran by reading the translation of the verses. And this is something that will manifest itself to you as we go through these sessions that it is not a coincidence that the Quran was revealed in Arabic. Arabic is fundamental to the comprehension of quran. Allah says:
⟪ar-quote:إِنَّآ أَنزَلْنَهُ قُرْءَنًا عَرَبِيًّۭا لَّعَلَّكُمْ تَعْقِلُونَ⟫

We sent down an Arabic Quran so that you may think. In other words our ability to think about the Quran, is directly related to the Arabic of the Quran. He says
⟪ar-quote:بِلِسَانٍ عَرَبِىٍّۢ مُّبِينٍۢ ‎⟫

Arabic language that clarifies. In other words the language of Arabic that is used in the Quran is meant to clarify its meanings. So if you are trying to study the book in a different language you will get some of the meanings, but you will not get all of them. You will not get the actual meaning.

So you need to know Arabic to understand the Quran. When I began studying the Quran, I would hear people tell me, "OMG! Quran is so awesome! Its arabic is so amazing! No poets of that time could come up with anything in comparison to it!"; And I would get all excited..... "Oh WOW! Quran is so awesome!!!! Wait! Why is it awesome?" Oh because it's Arabic is awesome! Oh WOW! But wait! I don't know Arabic "Well too bad for you!! It's still awesome!! And you'll never know how awesome it is because you don't know Arabic!".

It's like I show you a door and I say, "You know behind this door is something *really* amazing! It's SO incredible! OMG, I can't even begin to tell you how amazing it is!!". And then you say, "Oh Really! Can I see it?" And I say, "NO you can't! Go learn Arabic first!".

And this is a problem; because practically speaking, nobody is going to invest 5 or 6 years of their lives, to learn Arabic first, just to understand the Quran. And ancient Arabic is an ocean. It's a monster! I've been studying it for 16 years now and I still hardly feel I know anything. And the fact o the matter is that the statement is actually true! You really cannot understand the Quran's nuances, without understanding ancient Arabic. Because the beauty of its essence is baked within the Arabic itself. 

I'll give you a few examples just so you can appreciate this.

Asiya asking for a house in Jannah

Allah says in the Quran: [**http://quran.com/66/11**]
⟪ar-quote:إِذْ قَالَتْ رَبِّ ٱبْنِ لِى عِندَكَ بَيْتًۭا فِى ٱلْجَنَّةِ⟫

This ayah is talking about ASIYA, the wife of FIRON. Asiya is stuck in the castle of the Pharaoh. She can't escape. She is married to this horribly evil guy. She can't report him to the government, because he kinda is the government. She can't go to the cops, because he owns the cops. She has nowhere to go. But she lives in this incredibly beautiful castle. If there was MTV back then, FIRON'S castle would be like the most hit episode ever! It's the greatest crib there is on the planet at that time. So she is living in the most luxurious castle on earth at the time. And she makes this prayer:
⟪ar:رَبِّ ٱبْنِ لِى عِندَكَ بَيْتًۭا فِى ٱلْجَنَّةِ⟫

Roughly translated, Master! build me a house in your company in heaven. That would be a decent translation. Except in the words of the AYAH, instead of ordering it in the sequence I just translated it for you, it uses a strange sequence of words. It says: My master, build for me - near You - a house in Paradise. It's like instead of saying, "Please bring me a glass of water", I say: "Please a glass of water bring me". You understand? And what this change in sequence does in Arabic linguistics, is that it makes the request specific. So what she is actually saying is, Master! Build "especially for me", a house that is near you in Jannah. Because I am living in a terrible house right now. What's captured in this change of sequence, is that the castle she's living in, means nothing to her because of the evil that goes on inside. So she is telling Allah, that "I" in particular need different housing.

And then the most important part to the AYAH is not even heaven; it's not even the type of house. The most important part of the AYAH is ⟪ar:عِندَكَ⟫. That's why its forcefully brought in the beginning. "I need to be close to you!" Build for me, really close to you, a house. In other words, whatever is close to you I will take it. I have absolutely no demands on what kind of housing you provide for me, as long as it is close to you. And then finally she mentions heaven. Like the heaven part was a later concern. Even the house was a later concern. Her primary concern was what? That I want to be close to you. All of that is captured in the sequencing of the words of this AYAH; all of which is completely lost in the English translation.

Allah responding to the call

The month of Ramadan comes. People who are not religious turn religious. Somebody decides, at least in this month I should stop doing what I'm doing; maybe even do a couple of prayers. At least for a few days, if not everyday in the month. And then they ask themselves, How should I ask Allah for anything. I am such a sinner, why would Allah answer my prayers? Why would he even respond to someone like me? Because this is the way human beings operate. The way we human beings deal with each other, is that if I make you upset, and then I ask you for something, you're not going to respond to me right away. You're not going to be eager to respond to me; that is if you respond at all. And even if you do respond, it's going to be a struggle for you. You're going to take your sweet time responding. I send you a text message, you don't respond. I leave you a voicemail, you don't call back. I send you an email you don't reply. And then eventually, when you cool off, I get an answer back saying, Yeah! I was upset, I did not want to talk to you! So you and I are not eager to talk to someone who upset us. That is natural human behavior. Allah says in the Quran:
**http://quran.com/2/186**
⟪ar-quote:أُجِيبُ دَعْوَةَ ٱلدَّاعِ إِذَا دَعَانِ.....  فَلْيَسْتَجِيبُوا۟ لِى⟫

I respond to the call, or the prayer of the one who calls upon me, whenever they call me. The word that I want to highlight here is the one Allah uses for "I resond". ⟪ar:أُجِيبُ⟫(I respond). In the traslation it says "I respond, so they should respond".

In the Arabic language, when you respond immediately you say ⟪ar:أُجِيبُ⟫. And in the Arabic language, if you want to take your sweet time responding, or respond partially you use the word ⟪ar:استجیبُ⟫. There is a difference. If you say ⟪ar:أُجِيبُ⟫, it means immediately, without any hesitation, and it is always a full response without holding anything back. It's a 100% response. If you say ⟪ar:استجیبُ⟫, it means you are attempting to respond; you are thinking about responding, or you are responding partially; and you're taking your sweet time in responding.

Allah says,
⟪ar-quote:أُجِيبُ دَعْوَةَ ٱلدَّاعِ إِذَا دَعَانِ⟫

It doesn't matter where you've; it doesn't matter what you've done, when you call upon me, don't ever think I am so mad at you that I will never respond to you. He says "I respond immediately, I respond complete and I respond without hesitation."

What is even more epic in this verse, is that first he says "I will respond to you immediately and completely"; but then in the same verse he uses the word respond again. But this time he uses ⟪ar:فَلْيَسْتَجِيبُوا۟ لِى⟫. That they should also respond to me. In other words, Allah is saying that when you call upon me, I will respond to you immediately, I will respond completely; without any hesitation; without holding anything back from you. But you should at least try to make some effort to respond to me, even if it is delayed, even if it is half-hearted, even if it is not immediate; even if you take your time; but at least make some effort towards me. He does not say, Give me everything right away! He doesn't put that burden on us SubhanAllah! And all of this captured in the usage of words أُجیب and استجیب. What does the English translation say, "I respond to the prayer of the one who calls upon me, so they should respond to me. The word "respond" comes up twice, but you lose the linguistic nuances that are associated with the response.

So I hope these examples give you some idea of why the Quran cannot be understood through the filter of translation. Because there is no other language in existence other than Arabic, that is powerful enough to capture the meanings of the Quran at the required level of precision. And you don't have to take my word for it. This is a fact that will manifest itself very clearly to you as we progress through these sessions. And I'm going to make this super-easy for you. You won't need to learn 6 years of Arabic to understand these sessions. I will InshaAllah teach you the necessary Arabic that you need to know, in order to appreciate the beauty of the Quran as we move along.

---

---

So InshaAllah that's what I will attempt to show you, why I personally believe that the Quran is a miracle. One good way to look at the miracles of Quran, is to think of it in terms of this example. Let's say you and your friends take a boat and go to the middle of the ocean. You all dive into the ocean and then come back up with pearls and metals of different shapes and sizes. You look at the pearl that you found and you say, "Let me tell you why this ocean is amazing! It's amazing because of this pearl right here! Just look at this guy!" Your friend says, "Phew..... you think the ocean is amazing because of that!! "No no no! Look at these pearls that I am holding! Look what I found! The ocean is awesome because of these". Another friend says "Forget about pearls! Look at what I found at the bottom of the ocean! The ocean is not awesome because of the pearls that you guys found, it's awesome because of what I found at the bottom. I don't even have a name for this thing yet!" All of you that dove into the ocean, is impressed and amazed by what you found, and every one of you thinks that the ocean is awesome because of what you found. But I'm not talking about an ocean. I am talking about the Quran!

I am bewildered and amazed by this book because of what I found in it to be a miracle. Somebody else who is a Jurist (someone who studies law; somebody who studies SHAREEAH) when he studies the Quran, he finds something entirely different and is amazed by it. A historian studies the Quran, and he is amazed by the historical facts this books talks about. A grammarian or a lignuist studies the book, and he is amazed by the eloquence and perfection of the language, and says this Quran is a linguistic miracle. Each and every one of them finds their own miracle in this book. One says this book is a miracle because of linguistics; the other says it is a miracle because of justice and law; another says this book is a miracle because of the authenticity of its historical events. No no no, the Quran is a miracle because of its scientific information; another says this book is a miracle because of TAJWEED, because of its rhyme structure. Another says No! Quran is a miracle because of..... because of..... because of......

Each and every person finds a miracle in this book based on what they are looking for. And so the Quran is a miracle for *all* of those reasons and *none* of those reasons. In other words, you and I cannot limit the miracle of Allah's word based on what we think of it. It is way bigger than that. When we say that the Quran is a miracle because of these five things, then we are limiting its scope. It is much more bigger than we can ever fathom.

Now the most amazing thing about the Quran, when you think about it in terms of miracles, is That you cannot limit it to any one dimension. The Quran is like this beautiful tree that stands alone in an open valley. People who look at this tree appreciate different aspects of it. Some look at the colors of the leaves and they say this tree is incredibly beautiful because of its leaves. Others look at the fruits and say this tree is amazing because of its fruits. Some look at the symmetric shape of its branches and say this is why I think this tree is incredible. So nobody can say that the tree is beautiful because of one particular aspect. It's beauty literally lies in the eyes of its beholder.

When a child studies this book, she is mesmerized by the illustrations of its stories. When a historian studies this book, he is amazed by the accuracy of the historical facts. When a Jurist studies this book, he is amazed by the perfection in the laws of SHAREEAH. When a linguist analyzes the words of each verse, he is captured by the linguistic perfection of the speech. When a poet reads this book he is enchanted by the rhyme scheme of the verses. So when it comes to the miracles of Quran, nobody can say that it is a miracle for one particular reason. It is a miracle for all of these and none of these reasons. In other words we cannot limit the miracles of this book to our intellectual capacities.

So all I can do in these sessions, is share with you why I personally believe this book to be a miracle and the word of Allah(Subhanhu Wa Ta'ala). You have to figure out why you find it miraculous! One particular dimension may appeal to me; but a completely different dimension may appeal to you; and a completely different dimension may appeal to your sister. And it's all good! Or you may not find any of these dimensions miraculous, and that's fine too! It will not change my conviction about this book in anyway. Sadly I've come across lots of people where nothing impresses them anymore. It's really sad! May Allah open their hearts.

And all that is required on your part to study the Quran is to think. That's the one consistent demand throughout the entire Quran.
⟪ar-quote:أَفَلَا يَتَدَبَّرُونَ ٱلْقُرْآنَ؟⟫

Why do you not reflect on the Quran?
⟪ar-quote:افلا تعقلون؟⟫

Why don't you use your intellects?
⟪ar-quote:كَذَلِكَ يُبَيِّنُ ٱللَّهُ لَكُمُ ٱلْآيَتِ لَعَلَّكُمْ تَتَفَكَّرُونَ⟫

This is how Allah reveals his signs for you so that you can think deeply about them; so you ponder over it; so you wonder and exhaust your minds over it? All Allah asks us to do is "think". What is the difference between thinking and knowing? When you know something you no longer have to think about it; because you already know it! When you think, you are actually struggling to reach a conclusion. Isn't that the case? What does the Quran ask us to do? To know, or to think? To think! Because at the end of the day, only Allah can truly claim to knows!
⟪ar-quote:سُبْحَنَكَ لَا عِلْمَ لَنَآ إِلَّا مَا عَلَّمْتَنَآ⟫
Glory be to you Oh Allah! We have no knowledge except what you have taught us.

⟪ar-quote:إِنَّكَ أَنتَ ٱلْعَلِيمُ ٱلْحَكِيمُ⟫

Indeed it is only you who is All-Knowing, and All-Wise

So the only demand the Quran makes of us is to think. Because the more you think and reflect on the verses of the Quran, the more you will find new incredible things to learn for it. Every time you dive into this ocean, you will find new pearls and jewels of wisdom; each more valuable than the previous. So hopefully these sessions will engage us all more with the Quran.

3 types of Arabic (3 min)

In the previous session we established that the quran is an extempore, unscripted speech, that was delivered by the prophet (Salallahu alayhi wa aalihee wa sallam) before a live audience comprising of friends and enemies. The only question that remains to be answered, is that "Is Quran the speech of the prophet, or is it the word of God? Is it human speech, or divine speech?". That's the goal of our sessions.

Today I want to address the topic of why we are unable to appreciate the Quran as a miracle. Indeed, the Quran is as much a miracle today, as it was back then; but not in the exact same way. Because even though the Quran was reavealed "for" us; it was not revealed "to" us. There is a huge distinction here that we need to be clear about. To us the Quran is a "book", but to the Arabs back then, it was not a book, it was "speech". And so the miracles of speech are very different from the miracles of the book. And this will become clear as we progress through these sesssions. For now, I just want you all to make a mental note of this fact, that the miracles related to speech are very different from the miracles related to the book. Because the Quran was revealed to the Arabs as speech; and it has been compiled and handed down to us as book.

So we're first going to look at the miracles of Quran related to speech before we look at the miracles related to the book. The speech of Quran was revealed to a nation that lived 1400 years ago; and so if we truly want to to experience the miracle of Quran, we have to go back in time [1400 years ago], and first experience what those people experienced in speech. Because if history teaches us anything about that time period, there was definitely something very intriguing about this message; that even the most staunch disbeliever would hear one single AYAH and accept ISLAM. So as rational human beings, we have to have atleast some curiosity about this. What was so incredible about this message that affectd and transformed these people instantly? What did they hear, that instantly convinced them that this could not be the speech of a human being? This is where I want to begin our journey. And in order to do that, we must first undestand that enivornment [that context] in which the Quran was being revealed. I'll give you a very simple example to illustrate my point.

Volunteer
I'm going to count from 1 to 10, but I will call out one number out of context, and then you tell me which number that is.

1, 2, 3, 5, 6, 4, 7, 8, 9, 10

What told you that the number 4 is out of context? The surrounding numbers, right? The sequence or the environment surrounding the number 4, revealed to you that it is out of context. Because if I counted: 1, 3, 5, 7, 9, - 2, 4, 6, 8, 10, the number 4 is no longer out of context. Why? Because it falls in place with its surrounding kind, right? So my point is that you cannot appreciate the miracle of Quran without first understanding the conditions and the culture of that time, in which this book was being revealed.

Miracle according to culture - Arabic (10 min)

Because when we study history, we find that Allah(Subhanhu Wa Ta'ala) supported his Prophets with miracles that were extraordinary events. But the events were of the same nature, that the people of that particular time excelled at. For instance, the people during the time of Moosa (AS) excelled at magic. So the miracle of Moosa (AS) was that he threw his staff and it turned to a serpent. Likewise, the people of EISA (AS) excelled at medicine. So Jesus cured the blind and the leper, and gave life to the dead by the permission of Allah(Subhanhu Wa Ta'ala). During the time of IBRAHEEM (AS), the practice was to burn criminals alive. So when IBRAHEEM (AS) was thrown into the fire, Allah turned into a bed of flowers. So every prophet was given a miracle that was way above and beyond the skillset, that the people of the time excelled in.

Now what was it that people excelled in at the time of our prophet Muhammad (Salallahu alayhi wa aalihee wa sallam)? They excelled at poetry [rhetoric; BALAGHA; elogquence]. And they excelled in this area to such a degree, that even their children were incredible poets. The Arabic language had reached its peak! So much so that there was no language in the world at that time that was more eloquent and more superior than Arabic. And this is why, the Quran was revealed as a "linguistic" miracle.

Which Arabic am I talking about? Today's Arabic? HELL NO! Let's first understand the different types of Arabic.

[Volunteer]
There are 3 types of Arabic. How many types? And you need to remember them in this order I tell you... There is Spoken Arabic, Proper Arabic and Ancient Arabic.

Spoken Arabic: Another word for spoken Arabic is busted arabic, ugly arabic, slang, twisted, demented, mutated Arabic. This is also called ⟪ar:عمِّیَّۃ⟫which means dialectic arabic. What this means is that Egyptians have their own dialect, Algerians have their own dialect, Kuwaits have their own dialect and Saudis have their own dialects. Think of it like the hip-hop version of Arabic [Instead of Hello Sir! How are you doing today - YO! WAZ UP!]. So can think of it in those terms. The Arabic is similar, but the dialect varies from country to country. If you've ever been to a middle eastern country and heard two Arabs talking, you want to stick a knife in your ears. HAMMANA HAMMANA HAMMANA. This is the Arabic that is spoken in the middle east today; which is a distorted version of pure Arabic.

[Then there is..... ]

Proper Arabic: Any Arabic newspaper that you read, or any Arabic news program that you watch on TV [for example AL-JAZEERA, that's] is all in proper Arabic. This Arabic is called ⟪ar:الفُصحَۃ⟫. If you ever take an Arabic course in college, they call it "Modern Standard Arabic". What they mean by that is ⟪ar:فصحۃ⟫. It is proper arabic that is enunciated correctly. It uses the grammatical rules of Arabic correctly. So when you are learning proper Arabic, you're actually learning correct Arabic. There is nothing wrong with it.

But what we really need to understand for the purpose of our sessions, is this third type of Arabic, which is what? Ancient Arabic!

Ancient Arabic: Ancient Arabic is the original, *pure* Arabic that was spoken in the land of Arabia. It is called ⟪ar:قدیم⟫or ⟪ar:بلاغۃ⟫  .This Arabic was far more sophisticated, far more eloquent, far more complex, far more advanced, far more involved, far more intricate, far more powerful, than proper modern standard arabic. This is something you really need to understand in order to appreciate the Quran; because Quran was revealed to the people who spoke Ancient Arabic.

If you go to Egypt today, and you study arabic for 5 years, and you return speaking the most perfect arabic, you're still speaking which Arabic? Proper Arabic! But that still doesn't mean you have an understanding of what? Ancient arabic! They are two completely different things. The subtelties, the nuances, and the minute details that the ancient Arabs could detect in a phrase, the proper arabs cannot. That's why even when the "proper" Arabs today hear the Quran, they do not hear what the ancient Arabs heard when they heard the exact same ayat. You understand? So this belief that the Arabs today actually understand the Quran, is absolutely wrong. Because when they hear the Quran, they listen with the ears of their dialectical Arabic. And even the best of them [let's say an Arab scholar who graduated from one of the most esteemed university, like AL-AZHAR], when he hears the Quran, he still hears it with the ears of proper Arabic. And so both, are unable to experience the true linguistic beauty of the Quran. Because the only way to experience the miracle of Quran, is through "Ancient Arabic".

And so, moving forward all my explanations and analaysis of the Quran will be based on this "ancient arabic"  in these sessions.

How did Arabic reach its linguistic heights? (20 min)

Now let's understand why Arabic reached such linguistic heights in that time period. Every country in this world today, has something called nationalism, or patriotism. You take something and say, we're the best at it. For example, one country makes the best baseball bats, or cricket bats. That becomes their national pride. They unite as a nation in the production of that one particular thing. Today, in the US, we even have something called "state pride". Every state has something they're very proud of. For example Florida is proud of the oranges they produce. Alaska takes pride in its natural beauty. I'm from NJ, we MashaAllah have the highest crime rate in the country! So each state [country] has something that they're extremely proud of.

So now let's jump back back in time to see what these Ancient Arabs took pride in! The year is 610 BC. Rasool Allah (PBUH) has been born and he is about 40 years old. And because we're from the future, we know that any day now the Quran is going to be revealed to him. But we're not planning on meeting Rasul Allah(Salallahu alayhi wa aalihee wa sallam) on this trip. The people we really interested in meeting, are the Arabs of this time. So now what do we see?

We see a bunch of Arabs hanging out in the desert. There are no buildings, no agriculture, not even much of a farming community. They haven't even discovered oil yet. All they have is "sand" and "dry heat". Their water parks is sand; their Disney world is sand; their recreation is sand; their commute to work is through sand; their scenic spots, their vacation homes, their picnic points are all sand.

We also see that their neighbours are the Persian empire, and the Roman empire. They're sandwiched between these two super powers of that time. Now if you know anything about empires, they are always trying to increase the size of their backyards. They're always trying to expand their territories. But we notice something very strange here. Do we see them marching into Arabia? No! Why not? because they're thinking, why should we send our soldiers to get BBQ'ed is the heat of the deserts? What are we going to get out of them anyway? They're useless to us! They have nothing! There is nothing we can take over. They have no monuments, no resources, no buildings, they have absolutely nothing. So there's no point going after them. Because "resources" are the motivation for invasions. Your country have something another country wants and so they want to take over. But Arabia and the Arabs had nothing but sand; and who wants that! So we see that they are just left alone.

And you know what happends when you're left alone? When you look outside your window and all you see is "nothing"; all you see is the empty dry desert, you know what develops as a result of that? A very powerful and a very vivid imagination. See today, we don't have much of an imagination. You know why? Because everything that we can think of, has already been visualized for us in SCI-FI movies. So if I ask you to imagine something, you'll just relate a different version of what you've seen or read before. But a good imagination is when one can imagine things nobody has seen before. And this became the Arab imagination. It became extremely active; it became wild! Why? Because they saw nothing! Did you know that historically some of the most [creative, poetic and philosophical], picturesque literature that's ever been written in any place in the world, was written in prisons? You'll find some of the most remarkable writings all over the world, that were actually written in prison. Why do you think that is? Because when you don't get to see, then your mind is the only thing that can paint a picture for you. So you become more creative than ever before.

And so the Arabs develop this incredibly picturesque language that is full of imagery; that is extermely visual. Why? Because they don't see beautiful oceans and rivers and trees. They can't see any beautiful sceneries around them, so they are froced to develop a language; they harness this language over the years, that can create the most beautiful; the most amazing sceneries in their minds using words. This is why ancient Arabic became so powerfully visual. Every language in the world has meanings and definitions for words. But Arabic actually has visual images. I'll give you an example, so you get a taste of what I'm talking about.

The Arabic word for the intellect is AL-AQL [ع ق ل ]. The verbal form AQALA actually means when you take a..... Have you seen these Arabs that wear a scarf on their head, and then they have this round rubber thing on top that holds it in place? Today that is called the GHUTRA, and it's used as a device, to protect their gear from flying away.

But what the ancient Arabs used was a rope, that they wrapped around their head. They called it ⟪ar:عِقال⟫. This rubber thing that the Arabs wear today on their heads, is just symbolic of that IQAAL. The original thing was actually a rope that they wrapped around their head. Why? Because they use to ride on camels and horses back in the day. So if they had to park their camel somewhere; their camels did not come with anti-lock brakes. So you can't just park it outside and go BEEP BEEP; and then just walk into the restaurant [or the tent]. You couldn't do that and expect the camel to still be parked outside when you come out. It's going to wander off. So you need some kind of a break device for the camel, and that device in those days was a rope. So they would take it off their head, tie the camel with it to a tree or something, and then go about their business. So you can think of ⟪ar:عِقال⟫ as a leash that they wrapped on their head.

So now two reasons why the Arabs would call the intellect AL-AQL, is because of the image of this rope that wraps around their brain. But the other reason is because what does a leash do? It restricts your movement. The camel just can't walk away whenever it wants once it's tied to this ⟪ar:عِقال⟫. It can only move within a limited amount of space. So the intellect is something that holds you back, or restrains you from doing stupid things. Intellect [AL-AQL] to them, became a leash that they would apply to themselves. Like for example if there is a fire, and I have this burning desire to just walk into it, the intellect says, that's a dumb idea! Stand back! So the intellect becomes a kind of what? A leash, for us not to do ridiculously dumb things. It keeps us within a boundary. It keeps us safe. So now whenever the Ancient Arabs throught of intellect, what picture would come in their head? Camel on a leash; horse on a leash. In any other language people would just say, brain is brain and mind is mind and intellect is intellect. No but for the ancient Arabs it had to be a picture; it had to be a image. Even verbs are associated with pictures. Now thinking becomes associated with putting the leash on something; "wrapping" the mind around it. Isn't that incredible? So now imagine having these incredible visualizations for the entire language. Everything they talked about, it had some kind of visual associated with it.

I'll give you another example that you might like. Does anybody know what a knife is called in Arabic? It's called SIKKEEN. The word for knife in Arabic is SIKKEEN, and it comes from the word SUKOON. SUKOON means a pause. Because for the Arabs, a knife is something that when you slaughter an animal with it, it stops moving. The blood drains, and the animal stops moving, so SIKKEEN is a device to stop things. And SUKOON also has the meaning of coolness in it. Because when the animal is slaughtered and a dies, what happens to its body? It becomes cold. So the device that brings stillness and coolness to the animal after it is slaughtered, is called SIKKEEN.  They don't just call it a knife or a sharp thing. They have this whole visual associated with. So this is the kind of language that these Arabs developed before ISLAM.

So the first reason Arabic became so powerful is because these Arabs lived in isolation. It forced their imagination to develop to incredible heights. But then there was also a second advantage their isolation proivded. There was no external influence on their language. You know what happens when there is no external influence on language? It gets refined! It's words becomes more and more pure with time. Words become perfect! Because external influences are what deteriorates languages. I'll give you a very good example. I work in New York city. New York is a place that has people from all over the world. They call it the melting pot. So the Indian, the Pakistani, the Bengali the Sudani, the Somali, the Turkish, the Greek, the Russians, you'll find people from every single country in New York City. Now do they all speak English as their first, or as their second language? So you hear every accent in the world in NY. Especially on the subway. I've seen some incredible things on the subway. I've seen Russian guy harassing a Bengali guy. "Hey! Sing some of that Indian song for me", and the poor Bengali guys going, "NO SAAAAR! I don't know any song SAAAR" - LOL - "Hey Why you no sing for me?" - LOL

So in New York City, you can clearly see all of these different cultures colliding. But guess what suffers in this collision? The one thing that suffers, is the English language. Even people who speak English as their first language, because they constantly have to deal with ESL's, such as myself around them, their English actually starts going down. So the worst English that you will hear in the entire United States is probably going to be in New York City. You have the worst English, the foulest language, all of it! English that is completely grammatically incoherent.

Aye! Wha choo doin? I own no! LOL - If you say, I don't know!, "Look achchoo Mr. English" LOL..... So when a city is multicultural and you have a lot of people visiting from all different parts of the world, its own language suffers. And the opposite of it is also true. If nobody from outside is coming; and there is no outside influences, what happens, is that language flourishes. It becomes more and more refined. Look at our own language, Urdu. We can see how heavily influenced it is by the English language. Urdu speakers today cannot actually say a single sentence, without incorporating an English word in it. I did this experiment with someone at work. His name is Anjum, he's also from Pakistan. I told him let's do an experiment. For the next hour we both will speak only in Urdu. And the condition is that neither of us can use a single word of English......  GO! And he goes.....

Yaar Asif! ye bara DIFFICULT kaam hai, BECAUSE boht saree VOCABULARY jo hai, wo COMPLICATED hotee hai aur us ke andar phir banda FORGET kar jata hai

So that is what you call foreign influence!

Anyway, so we see that these Arabs have no external influence on thier language; and so it starts getting more and more refined; it gets extremely pure, and their imaginations sky-rocket and now the Arabs start taking immense pride in it? Because what else can they take pride in? Is it their beautiful architecure? Is it the amazing structures that've built? Is it the beautiful gardens they have? Is it the amazing armies they command? NO! The only thing they have, that they could possible take pride in, is what? Language! That's the ONLY thing they have! And when you take pride in the ONLY thing you have, you REALLY REALLY REALLY take care of it. So the Arabic language became their national identiy! It became a matter of Arab identity to be focused on language from childhood! To excel in it, to drop everything else and focus on just this one thing. And so their Arabic language over time reaches a level of eloquence, that no other language in the world could compete with; even today!

Do you know what the opposite of ⟪ar:عرب⟫is? ⟪ar:العجم⟫. Do you know what ⟪ar:عجم⟫means? It means "dumb" or "mute" or "retarded". Someone who cannot speak properly. It sounds racist right? But just imagine the level of Arabic at that time; that if someone could not communicate with these arabs at the same level of sophistication that they spoke Arabic with, that's what they would call them! Mute! In other words, Dude! you may as well have been born dumb, mute, or retarded, because you're not even worthy of speaking with us. But this arragonce was based on something very substantial. They really did harness a language that was incredibly eloquent; and they were crazy about their eloquence! And what is the height and the summit of eloquence in any language? Poetry! So each and every Arab of this time, could recite incredibly amazing poetry, as naturally as you and I can have a conversation.  They would converse using the most eloquent poetry.

In fact, when they went to war, they would throw poetry at each other to intimidate them. Before they attacked them with swords, they attacked with words. Imagine that! Just think about this. Imagine you are about to fight an opponent with naked swords. You are facing death right now. Can you imagine what your mental state would be? I know I wouldn't even remember my name if you asked me! But these Arabs, they would recite poetry! And their poetry was so powerful, their words would literally shake their opponents to the core!
⟪ar-quote:المَوتُ أَحْلَ عِندَناَ مِنَ العَصَلِ⟫
⟪ar-quote:نَحنُ بَنُو ضَبَّۃَ أَصحَابُ الجَمَلِ⟫
⟪ar-quote:نحن بَنُو المَوتِ اِذَا المَوتُ نَزَلِ⟫

This is the poem that people of this tribe Banu Dabba would recite when facing their opponent. Death to us is sweeter than the taste of honey. We are the people of Banu Dabbah. We are the sons of death, and where we go death descends

In the battle of Khyber, Maulana Ali is facing Amr Ibn Abd Wud. This man was a monster! It is said that he alone was equivalent to 1000 soldiers. In the battle of Khyber, he challenged the prophet (Salallahu alayhi wa aalihee wa sallam) saying "Don't you have any men left amonst you to face me? Arent' you excited to go to heaven? Face me in battle and I'll send you to the destination you desire!".  And not a single person answered his call. But Maulana Ali stood up and said, Ya Rasul Allah, let me face him! And then he enteres the battle ground reciting
⟪ar-quote:أنا الَّذِی سَمَّتْنِی أُمِّی حَیدَرَا..... زَرْغَمُو عَجامٍ لَیسٌ قَصوَرَۃ⟫
⟪ar-quote:کَلِسَّرَا بَاطِلْ کَرِیہِ المَنظَرَا..... وَفِیھِمِی بِصَاعِ التَّیْلِ سَّندَرَا⟫

I am the one whose mother named him Hyder!

ٰI am the lion of the valley, that attacks his prey by chasing it

Evil trembles when it see me standing before it.

for my sword breaks open skulls with one strike!

So they would actually use poetry to intimidate and incite the anger of their opponents. And what would tool would they use for that? Poetry! Because psychologically when you intimidate an opponent, they either get scared, or they get enraged. In in both cases they would make mistakes. So the Arabs would break their opponents down psychologically with words, before they struck them down with swords.

But then they would also use poetry to encourage themselves. They would recite poems to themselves while in battle; to force themselves to move on; to not give up; to be strong.

⟪ar-quote:یاَ حَبَّ ذَالَجنَّۃُ وَقْتِرَابُھَا ،  طَیِّبَۃٌ وَ بَارِدٌ شَرَابُھَا⟫
⟪ar-quote:وَ الرُّومُ رَومُ قَدَّنیٰ عَذَابُھَا ، عَلَیَّ اِلاَّ قَیْطُھَا ضَرَابُھا⟫

These are the verses that Hazrat Jaffar Al-Tayyar recited when he was fighting in the battle of Moota.

My soul, don't you desire the blessings of Jannah? It's drink is sweet and cool. And this world is a torment in comparision to it. Is it for this world that you choose to be a coward?

⟪ar-quote:أقْسَمتُ یَا نَفسُ لَتَنْزِلِنَّا  ،  کارِھَۃً أَولیٰ تُطَابِعِنَّا⟫

These are the verses of Hazrat Abdullah iBn Rawaha when he was fighting in the battle of Moota.

I command you my soul! Do not become weak. The strike of the sword is far less painful than the disgrace of failure

So for the Arabs, their entire life was poetry! Battle was poetry, sports was poetry!

Arab sport of poetry (15)

---

It was so crazy that even their sports were developed around poetry! They used to have this ancient form of dissing competitions. You know how there is freestyle rapping today? They had their own version of it, except it wasn't slang. It was poetry in it's highest, purest and most eloquent form. Two tribes would select one man, the BEST man from their tribe; the *best* poet from among the poets, and they would then battle each other in poetry before a huge crowd. And the one who wins that competition, has successfully disgraced the other tribe for generations to come. And so the one who lost, their tribe would be so mad, that they would kill the poet. Because he did not just lose the competition, he lost the dignity of his tribe, for how long? a few days? a month? a year? No, for generations to come!!!!! Pretty much like India Pakistan cricket match.

So these guys took their poetry and their literature, VERY VERY VERY seriously. This was an extremely serious thing to them. And so now imagine people sitting around a bon-fires and these two poets spitting rhymes, dissing each other, and everyone going OOOOOOOHhhh SNAP! And what they would do is, they would take the verses of their opponents, and they will rip it apart; they would shred it to pieces; they would criticize it to the nth degree. And they would do all of this *with* poetry. They would recite poetry, to criticize the opponents poetry!  Because the best way to beat a poet is to attack his what? Not to attack his personality, but his poetry! Because poetry was how they identified themselves. So you attack his poetry and now you've actually got something. So to them, poetry was what the gladiators were to the Romans! I'll give you an example how sick they were when it came to their language, just so you can wrap your minds around it.

So there's this one poetry content going on. Huge crowds gathered to watch this slam. And so there is this guy from one tribe making poetry about how generous and how brave they are. So he made a poem about his tribe.

⟪ar-quote:لَنَا الجَفَنَاتُ الغُرْ.....  یَالمَعنٰی بِالضُّحیٰ⟫

⟪ar-quote:وَالأَسْیَافُنَا یَقطَرنَا مِن النَّجدَۃِ الدَّماً⟫

We have really shiny bowls, he begins. Now what has shiny bowls got to do with anything? I'll tell you what that means. The Arabs gave charity in bowls. They would put coins of gold and silver and precious metal in these bowls that they would then give in charity. He says the bowls in which we give charity, even they are shiny. So just imagine the stuff that we actually put inside! That is what he is saying..... ⟪ar:یَالمَعنٰی بِالضُّحیٰ⟫, Our bowls twinkle during the day. ⟪ar:وَالأَسیَفُنَا یَقطَرنَا⟫ ..... And our swords keep dripping drops of blood. Because we keep going on these impossible rescue missions. Like when one member of our tribe gets captured, we go with a team of three or four guys, and we take on the entire tribe. We have these covert operations, winters cell, assassin's Creed style; we keep going on these impossible rescue missions risking our lives, so much so, that our swards don't even get a chance to become dry. They keep dripping drops of blood.

So the first line was about how generous they are with their shiny bowls; and the second was about how brave and courageous they are. So you can see that these are some seriously epic lines that he dropped here. This is a good example of the Arab imagination at work here.

But then this lady from the other tribe, comes to him and says, "You know, that was pretty epic. I have some comments though. You said ⟪ar:الجَفَنَاتُ⟫..... JAFANAT is a kind a plural that is weak in Arabic. The Arabs have a stronger plural ⟪ar:جِفَان⟫. Had you used JIFAAN it would have meant you have a lot of bowls. But since you used JAFANAAT it means that you only have like 9 or less bowls. So you're really not that rich! Then you used the word ⟪ar:الغُر⟫, You said ⟪ar:الغُرْ یَالمَعنٰی بِالضُّحیٰ⟫..... You said that the bowls are shiny. Anything, a rock could be shiny. You should have said ⟪ar:البِیضْ⟫, so shiny that they look white! You used the wrong word, it wasn't strong enough. Then you said ⟪ar:یَالمَعنٰی بِالضُّحیٰ⟫..... They twinkle during the day! Frogs twinkle during the day too. That's no big deal. If something sparkles during the night, then that is something! And reflecting light is different than giving off light! If your bowls are so shiny as you claim to be, then it it shouldn't be reflecting light, it should be giving off light. You should have said ⟪ar:یُشرِقْنا بالَّیالی⟫ ; they give off light during the night time. If your bowls were really so awesome, they would have become a source of light. Thats how epic your bowls would have been, had you been generous". So she said, "that was kind of lame what you said which kind shows how lame your generosity is".

Then she said, you used the word ⟪ar:اسیافُنا⟫for swords, that's a weak plural like you have 9 or less swords. What you should have said is ⟪ar:سُیُفُنا⟫that you have many many swords. Then you said

⟪ar:یَقطَرنا بالدَّماً⟫، , what the hell is that? What are you cutting chickens? Are you giving paper cuts to your enemies? What is it that you guys are cutting? You should have said ⟪ar:یَجْرِینَا⟫, they flow. Then you said ⟪ar:الدَّماً⟫, which are like drops of blood. What is that dude? What did you give the enemies, a nose bleed? You should have said ⟪ar:الدَّمَاءً⟫, rivers of blood. Come on dude! make some poetry here! What is this? LOL.....

She destroyed him! And this is what they love doing. This was in their blood. Even in regular conversations, one guy would say something, and the other guy instead of responding, he'd say, this is what you said, you could have said it better this way. Imagine talking to an Arab who instead of having a conversation, keeps correcting your Arabic. Dude! What are you my mom? Can I just finish what I'm saying for once? But this is how they used to operate! They would take apart every single word in every single sentence, and then criticize it to the nth degree!

---

Quran comes as a challenge

Now the Quran comes to these people; and does it come in the form of a book or just words? Just words! Arabic words. And the Arabs are really really good at Arabic. And Quran comes in a poetic form; and if there's one thing that the Arabs love to compete in, is what? Poetry. And this is why you find historically that they accused the Quran of being poetry. One of the accusations against the Quran is that it is poetry. So Allah says in the Quran, Fine! If you think this is poetry then let's have a poetry slam. Why don't you produce something that can defeat the Quran? Go ahead. Allah challenges them in the Quran:

⟪ar-quote:وَإِن كُنتُمْ فِى رَيْبٍۢ مِّمَّا نَزَّلْنَا عَلَىٰ عَبْدِنَا فَأْتُوا۟ بِسُورَةٍۢ مِّن مِّثْلِهِۦ⟫

And if you are in doubt about this message that has been sent down to Our slave, then produce a single *Surah* of its kind.

⟪ar-quote:وَٱدْعُوا۟ شُهَدَآءَكُم مِّن دُونِ ٱللَّهِ إِن كُنتُمْ صَدِقِينَ⟫

And then call your own witnesses for the final verdict. You don't even have to come to us. Get your own groups; form your own committess; put together your own board of analysts and review what you've come up against the Quran. SubhanAllah!

One time Rasul Allah(Salallahu alayhi wa aalihee wa sallam) without telling the Arabs, that this is actually from the Quran, he had SURAH AL-KAUSAR enter a poetry contest. It's the shortest SURAH of the Quran. All these poets are coming with long poems and QASEEDAs, and they're dropping it before this huge crowd. And the finals; the national championships use to happen in Mecca. It used to happen right in front of the KAABA. And the trophy was, that if your poetry wins, we will hang it on the wall of the KAABA. That was the ultimate prize. If you win this competition your poetry gets hung on the wall of the KAABA. The prophet says enter SURAH ALKAUSAR into the contest. He doesn't tell anybody that this is Quran; and it has been entered into the contest. Now everybody is spitting their rhymes, and everyone's rhymes are like 100 lines. SURAH ALKAUSAUR comes down with what? 3 lines. And all of these poets, and everyone in the crowd [who BTW themselves are all poets]. So they're all sitting there and one of the poet goes:

⟪ar-quote:إِنَّآ أَعْطَيْنَكَ ٱلْكَوْثَرَ..... فَصَلِّ لِرَبِّكَ وَٱنْحَرْ..... إِنَّ شَانِئَكَ هُوَ ٱلْأَبْتَرُ⟫

And the entire crowd roars in one single voice

⟪ar-quote:ما ھذا قول البشر⟫

This cannot be the words of a human being. They actually added another line on the same rhyme scheme. That this cannot be the word of a human being. The entire crowd said this! And this 3 line SURAH won the competition and they hung SURAH ALKAUSAR on the wall of the KAABA. They didn't even know that this is QURAN. When they found out that this is actually verses from the Koran they took it down. SubhanAllah!

So now imagine verses upon verses of Quran coming down. Over 6000 verses in the Quran. I showed you the example of one verse from a poem. Look what that lady did to that verse. She crushed every single word in that single verse. She dismantled it; she destroyed it. Now this 600 pages of Quran is coming down. What do you think their first reaction is going to be?  Critique it, right?

"You said that, should have been this! You said that, could have been this!" Isn't it?

They don't do it? They're unable to do it. Over 6000 verses, and they can't change one single word, one single letter in it. They just can't do it. They're baffled. And it's not like a poetry slam, where you have two weeks to prepare. This Quran is coming down as unscripted extempore speech before them. And they cannot critique one single AYAH. And to this day nobody has been able to! I mean what are we going to produce with our distorted and deteriorated languages in this day and age? Our language is dumb mute and retarded even by standards set a 100 years ago. Shakespere would call us AJAM.  So forget us coming up with something comparable to the Quran. But even those people, who were the ultimate masters of the most picturisque, the most visual language that existed on earth; even they were completely baffled by it. 

So the Quran is revealed and they find no way to attack it. So now who do they attack? If you can't defeat the Quran, might as well accuse who? The messenger! You know when you lose a debate of ideas, you then start attacking personality! Right? It's very common. If there is a debate on an issue, and your opponent cannot beat you on the issue, what does he do? He starts attacking your personality. Isn't that what happens in debats? Your mama so fat!.....  It's called character assasination. So this is what they came down to. They started attacking his personality.

They started calling him a ⟪ar:شاعر⟫ (A poet). But when their best poets went to challenge the messenger of Allah (PBUH), they came back swearing, Wallahi! This is not what? It's not poetry! Because they knew the rules of poetry, and the Quran wasn't fitting in with those rules. Because the Quran is prose, in a poetic form. So the poets were completely baffled.

So then they said, the prophet was a mind reader (⟪ar:کاہن⟫). Because the Quran was making predictions about the future. But in those days when fortune tellers spoke they, talked in mumbo jumbo. They spoke this gibberish and it was supposed to have some sort of a magical effects. They used words nobody could understand. And they would say this guy is casting a spell. But did the words of Quran make perfect sense? They did! So it was clearly not the words of a fortune teller.

So then they called him insane [مجنون]. They said he's insane; or posessed by a JINN, so these are magical words. First of all as soon as you say this is magic, you are acknowledging that this is not normal, it is para-normal. So just by alleging that the Quran is magic, they were accepting its power. But then Quran speaks words of wisdom, which an insane person cannot do. So even that blame didn't stick.

And so now they can't even attack the prophet. They can't attack the message and they can't attack the messenger. So what do they do? They start battling and killing the Muslims. Now you tell me, what is a SURAH made up of? Words! All they had to do was come up with some words, and the problem of ISLAM is solved. The Quran is finished. All they had to do was come up with some words. Words in a language that they were masters of! But for those Arabs, shedding blood, killing and getting killed; going to war against their own tribe people; was easier to do, than to come with words to match the Quran.  How in the world is that possible? I'm just introducing to you the historical arguments about the Quran. We're going to go beyond that. But I want to share with you why do we have this kind of confidence in the Quran. Why were the sahaba converting left and right when they heard these verses? What was it about these verses that were SO perfect; that muted these linguistic gurus of the time?

⟪ar-quote:طلع البد علینا⟫

A man comes to Naseeruddin Tusi... who was an scholar, and asks him Will the love of Ali matter on the day of judgment? Now If someone asks you or me this question. What would we say? Sure! Absolutely! Of course! Right? That's the best we would come up with.... This is what he replies.. I'm going to recite the poem first, and then I'll explain what it says, OK?
⟪ar-quote:لو أن عـبداً أتى بالصـالحـات غداً⟫
⟪ar-quote:وود كـــلّ نـّــبي مـرســـــل وولي⟫
⟪ar-quote:وصام مـا صام صـوّاماً بلا ضجرِ⟫
⟪ar-quote:وقام ما قـام قـــوّامـاً بـــــلا مـــلل⟫
⟪ar-quote:وحجَ ما حجَ من فـرضٍ ومن سننِ⟫

⟪ar-quote:ما كان يوم الحشـر عند الله منتفعاً⟫
⟪ar-quote:إلَّا بحـــب أميــر المـــؤمنين عليّ⟫
