Metaphore of Quran with Tree (5 min 145w/m)

I'm going to use a metaphore to explain how people have approached the Quran. I want you all to imagine that this Quran, is like a huge towering tree in the center of a valley. We all have just entered that valley from all different directions, and we're walking towards this tree. As we walk towards it, each one of us notices different things about it. Some of us notice the wonderous  leaves of the tree. Some notice its massive trunk. Some of us are impressed by the towering height of the tree. Some admire the symmetry of its branches. Some see the majesty and beauty of this tree. Some of us will look at the shade that the tree provides to those who sit under it. Some are taken by the beauty of its flower, some by their fragrance. Some admire the extraordinary nature of its fruits. In other words, as we all walk towards this tree, we all notice certain specific aspects of this tree. But none of us can say, that this this tree is marvellous because of this *one* particular aspect, that I am impressed with.  NO! It's beautiful and its marvellous in every aspect.

Some of our Scholars have looked at Quran as a legal miracle. They spent their lives examining the legal aspects of this book; its exalted judgments; its highly esteemed rules that Allah(Subhanhu Wa Ta'ala) has placed within it. Some have been taken by the incredible mercy of the Quran. Some looked at the "spiritual aspects" of the quran. They admired the unseen meta-physical realities that it reveals. Some have looked at the wisdoms behind the moral teachings of the Quran. The idea of spending, the idea of charity, the idea of helping others in need. Some have been amazed by how this book, once it takes root in the hearts of a man, he no longer needs a policeman to guard him. There is no longer a need for someone to be constantly over him, threatening him with the sword of the law. They're amazed by how this book turns him into someone who is able to guard his own soul, and restrain himself from doing wrong, simply by his awareness of his lord, in conscience. Some have studied the linguistic eloquence of this book. They've analyzed the profundity, the linguistic depths that the Quran  reaches, which is beyond the reach of human capacity. 

And so each and every scholar has looked at a particular dimension of the Quran and considered it a miracle based on that particular dimension. But the Quran is a miracle in *all* of those dimensions and it is a miracle in *none* of those dimension. Because as time passes, there will be other dimensions that will reveal themselves to mankind, that we today have absolutely no knowledge about.

The reason I'm sharing this with you, is because in these sessions, I will share with you the mircalces of Quran in several dimensions. Each one of us may find it miraculous in a particular dimension. But none of us can say that the Quran's miracle is limited to that one specific dimension. It is a miracule in all dimensions.

Also, I want to make clear that in these sessions, we are not going to look at the wisdom behind any of the moral teachings of the Quran. That's beyond the scope of these sessions!

So continuing with the metaphore of the tree, all I intende to do, is show you the external beauty of this tree. If you even take one single aspect of this tree, let's say a leaf. There is beauty in the external appearance of a leaf; and there is beauty in the internal functions of the leaf. So we can appreciate it's symmetry, it's shape, its color; or we could appreciate how it functions; and it's role and purpose within the structure of the tree. So in these sessions we will only look at the outward aspects of this tree; not the inward aspects. InshaAllah if you're interested we will look at the wisdom of the Quran in a separate group.

<!-- section 3 (id=5780, raw_sort=3): What is a miracle -->
Recap

So far we've established that the Quran is an unscripted, imprompty speech, delivered before a live audience comprising of friends, family and mortal enemies. The question we're looking to answer is, "Is Quran the word of God, or is it the word of the prophet (Salallahu alayhi wa aalihee wa sallam)".

In the previous session I explained to you the 3 different types of Arabic: Spoken Arabic [which is dialectical Arabic], Proper Arabic [grammatically correct Arabic] and Ancient Arabic [which is Arabic in its purest form]. We then travelled back in time to understand the environment in which the Quran was revealed. We looked at why and how Arabic reached its linguistic peak. We saw how this language drew its power from images. Every single word in ancient Arabic was based off an image, which made the language extremely picturesque, extremely poetic. And this is why the people of that time excelled at poetry. Poetry was extremely important to them. Everything revolved around eloquence for these people. Every word of every sentence was critiqued, and criticized, and refined until it achieved absolute perfection. And because language is all the Arabs had, they took immense pride in it. They were so proud of it, that they were willing to sacrifice their lives for it. I told you that when they would have these poetry slams, the one who lost would end up getting killed. What's interesting is that these poets knew that going into the competition; but they were still OK with it. Because to them, if someone defeats them in language, in eloquence, there is no point in living any more anyway. So these people were seriously crazy about language.

And now the Quran comes down to these Arabs as an unscripted, inpromptu voluminous (veloo-menes) speech, with over 6000 verses, and they are unable to critique or criticize even a single verse; nor can they come up with something even remotely close to it in eloquence. So when they cannot attack the Quran, they start attacking the prophet by calling him a poet; by calling him a fortune teller; by calling him insane. But again, even though the Quran has a poetic form, it does not follow the rules of poetry. Even though it predicts the future, its words are not mumbo-jumbo; and Quran is a book of profound wisdoms which rules out insanity. And so now the only option the Arabs see, is to go to war with the Muslims and try to eliminate them. All they had to do, was to come up with a few words; in a language that they were masters of. All they needed was one single AYAH, to simply match the Quran, not even defeat it; but failing to do that, they choose to go to war with the Muslims. They choose to kill and be killed! Such was the power of this Quran.

What is a miracle

Now the first thing I want to do before we move any further, is define the word miracle! What does the word miracle mean? And what is the difference between a miracle and a magic trick? If I pull a rabbit out of a hat, is that a magic trick or did I just perform a miracle? Why are prophets given miracles? And why was Quran revealed as a linguistic miracle, instead of something that could be perceived? So there are quite a few questions we want to answer today surrounding this word "miracle".

So let's begin with the word miracle itself.

What does the word miracle mean? In common language, not in the context of religion, but in our day to day life, when do we use or hear the word miracle?

Doctors use the word miracle when patient unexpectedly recovers

It's used in sports, in cricket for example, when they hit a six on the last ball

You tank an exam, and then find out you got a 97!

You see a dream and it comes true

So the word miracle is thrown around all the time in normal conversations. Anytime we witness something extra-ordinary happening, that we believe was not possible, we use the word miracle to describe that event.

How would you define a magic trick? Because magic tricks are also things which are extra-oridinary. We saw that the hat was empty, the magician showed it to us; and then instantly he pulled out a rabbit from it. What was that? Magic or miracle?

In our general conversations, miracle is used for something that is highly unlikely, but not impossible. But the greatest difference between a miracle and a magic trick is that a magic trick is "perceived", whereas a miracle is "experienced"; it is something you feel in the heart. A miracle is not something I can give to you, or teach you. It is a very personal experience. In other words, a miracle is not something that can be proven by scientific facts, or guaged in scientific terms. This is why in a scientific context, a miracle is irrelevant. Why? Because the scientific community in general, when they study a phenomenon, what is their attempt? Do they attempt to prove that the event is a miracle, or are they always trying to figure out if there is a scientific explanation behind it? What is their attempt always?  To find a scientific explanation! So "scientifically" speaking, there is no such thing as a miracle. Everything has to have some scientific explanation. That's today's post modern thought. Therefore, miracle could be a "language" thing, or it could be a "religious" thing or it could be a "faith" thing. But what it certainly **cannot**be, is what? A scientific thing. You understand? Because science is something you can perceive with the 5 senses! And when you're talking about a miracle, you're definitely asking people to go beyond the 5 senses. right?

So whenever science doesn't have an answer, their response is that we don't know why this happend. We don't have an answer yet, but we're sure there is a scientific explanation behind it. There is no leap of faith in science. This is why science can tell us how the big bang happened. But what science cannot tell us, is why it happened! And if you ask them why? They'll say that is not a scientific quesiton, that is a philosophical question or religious question.

But in this day and age, if we were to believe in a miracle, then we have to see something beyond science. Something that just cannot be explained otherwise. Only something like that will make a believer out of you and I. Because we're living in a highly intellectual, extremely scientific age. And the reality today is, that we are much bigger believers in science, than we are believers in religion, even when we are religious people. So there is absolutely nothing wrong with it. Because we live in an age of questioning, and challenging, and seeking intellectual answers. Faith is great! But it needs to be backed up with rational and empirical evidence right?

Linguistic meaning of Miracle

Let's begin by understand the linguistic meaning of the word Miracle. Generally people think that a miracle means "something amazing or incredible". Most of you would be quite surprised to learn, that that is not what the word miracle means in Arabic. The word for miracle in arabic is ⟪ar:معجزۃ⟫ . It is a derivative of the word ⟪ar:أعجاز⟫, which in turn come from the root word ⟪ar:عِجزْ⟫. And what this word means, is to bring someone to his knees, in a way that the person cannot rise again. It means to incapacitate or overpower the opponent. To make one incapable of any kind of response. I'll give you an example:

[diagram: Etymology diagram of the Arabic root '-j-z. Three-step vertical chain: مُعجزۃ (Subject — miracle) → أَعجاز (Experience — incapacitation) → عَجز (the bare root), with English glosses listing four shades of meaning.]
  (see ../images/002.png)
  *Arabic labels in image:* ⟪ar:مُعجزۃ → أَعجاز → عَجز⟫
  *Note:* Pedagogical Arabic morphology — the noun 'mu'jiza' (miracle) literally means 'that which incapacitates'.

Imagine there is a truck is speeding down a road. and I'm crossing that road completely consumed in my thoughts. I don't even look at the truck that is speeding right towards me. When do I notice the truck? When it's one foot away from me. Now there is no time for me to move out of the way. There is no time for that truck to stop, even if the driver slams the brakes, or tries to steer away. In other words I realize it's too late. I'm done! Now if you can imagine what I would feel in that moment; that feeling is called ⟪ar:عِجزْ⟫.  That helplessness I feel in that moment, just before turning into pancake, that feeling is what's called ⟪ar:أعجاز⟫.

Now what I just went through, was it something I experienced? Or was it something that was taught to me? Right before the truck hit me, did someone hit the pause button, and come to me and say, "OK! So let me tell you like it is! Let me keep it real for you! Things aren't looking too good for you! You don't have time to get out of the way. It's too late for the driver to hit the brakes. There's no way you're walking out of this alive. So how do I put this delicately to you? Dude! you dead! And then he hits the play button..... LOL

In that moment, did anyone explain or teach all of this to me, or was it something I experienced? I experienced all of it. And so the word for that "experience" of feeling completely incapacitated and completely overpowered is called ⟪ar:أعجاز⟫; and the thing that generates that experience is called ⟪ar:معجزۃ⟫. You understand? So in this case the truck caused the ⟪ar:معجزۃ⟫, my experience of feeling completely incapacitated is called ⟪ar:أعجاز⟫; and my state would be called ⟪ar:عاجاز⟫.

The point is that a miracles is a thing to be "experienced", not "studied". Let's try something. Let's all of us take a journey back in time again. This time we're going 2000 years before the time of the prophet. We're now in the time of MOOSA (AS). We just got dropped among a bunch of people running for their lives. We learn that the army of FIRON is chasing them; and getting caught means certain death. So we start running along with the group until we reach the bank of this huge river, and we find ourselves completely trapped. We see MOOSA (AS) standing at the bank of the river holding his staff. We see some people blaming him for the situation they're in. They're saying Moosa! We are now trapped, all because of you! You led us to our doom! How are you a prophet? You said you would deliver us from FIRON, and now here we are completely trapped all because of you. But then..... we see MOOSA (AS) lift his staff, make a prayer and then strike it on water, and right before our very eyes, we see that the water begins to split. We see the water begins rising on both sides, and start forming huge wall..... ⟪ar:كَٱلطَّوْدِ ٱلْعَظِيمِ⟫ as the Quran says. We see "water" standing up like walls, creating a pathway for everyone to walk through. Now imagine walking through this river; imagine watching these walls made of water on both sides. You can touch it, you can feel it, you can hear it. It's still water, and yet it's not behaving like water. You are "experiencing" this miracle first hand. As you walk through this path, could there be the slightest doubt in your heart about MOOSA (AS) being the true messenger of Allah? Absolutely not! So you see, what you're feeling right now, this is what the experience of miracle feels like. Would you ever be able to describe it in words even if you tried?

Now think about this. Is Quran the miracle of our prophet? But is this the state of our hearts when we recite the Quran? Or when we hear it being recited to us? It's not! Because we see the Quran at best, as a book of religious text, but not as a miracle. But you know what the ancient Arabs "experienced" when they heard these verses recited to them? They felt exactly what you just experienced walking through the river with MOOSA (AS); every single time! For them Quran didn't begin as a book of religious teachings. To them it was a miraculous experience every single time. This is why it had such a strong impact on their hearts.

Now I want you to remember this feeling as I move this discussion forward.

Criteria for Miracle

I'm going to give you 5 criteria for something to be a miracle. If it's a miracle it needs to meet these 5 conditions:

[diagram: Slide titled 'CRITERIA FOR MIRACLE' listing five numbered criteria in purple-bordered boxes; the fifth ('IS A CHALLENGE') is highlighted in yellow.]
  (see ../images/003.png)
  *Note:* Five-point definition used to argue why the Qur'an meets the criteria of mu'jiza.

**1. A miracle should be impossible for human beings to perform.** A miracle is not a skill. It is not a trick, it is not technology. It cannot originate from a human being. For example if you see a human being floating in air, that is not something a human being can do without a device. Or a new born baby speaking perfectly; and not just speaking, but speaking eloquently. That's not something human beings can do. From the beginning of time, there is no evidence of such a thing happening, except through miracle. This is why one of the miracles of Eisa (AS), was addressing the people in the most eloquent language, when he's one day old.
**2. It breaks the laws of nature.** There are certain patterns and laws of nature which we observe on a daily basis, and we take for granted. Like for example, fire burns! We know this historically. You get thrown into a burning fire, you turn into KABAAB. That's law of nature. Yet here we have Ibrahim (AS) thrown in the middle of buring fire, and it doesn't burn him. Why? Fire is supposed to burn! And that fire was not set by an assistant (like magicians have these assistants that work with them to fool an audience). That fire was set by NAMROOD, his worst enemy. You understand? So the second criteria is that a miracle should break the laws of nature.
**3. It cannot be duplicated:**

Now people like Hoodini and David Copperfield have done the most incredible illusions. But why are those considered magic tricks or illusions and not miracles? Because it can be duplicated. Somebody else can perform the same illusion, the same magic, the same trick. And more than one person can do it. So the third rule is that it cannot be duplicated.
**4. It can ONLY be done by somone claiming to be the messanger of Allah.**

There was this guy named Musailema (AlKazzab) during the time of the prophet. When he found out that Rasul Allah (PBUH) declared himself a prophet and gained so much popularity; he thought, "Hey I should do the same and become popular!". This guy lived in a different town from the prophet. One day the prophet was taken to a well that had completely dried up. He was requested to pray to Allah that the well recovers, because the town was suffering because of it. Rasul Allah (Salallahu alayhi wa aalihee wa sallam) made a prayer and spit into the well, and it began overflowing with water as the narration goes. Now, in Musaliema AlKazzab's town, there was also a well that was half dry. It wasn't completely dry, but its supply had become short. So the people of his town came to him and said, "Why don't you do the same thing! After all, you're Allah's prophet too. Don't worry! you got this!". So he prayed and spit in the well, and it completely dried up. So a miracle can only be performed by a true prophet. If someone else tries to do it he will fail.
**5. The final criteria, and the most important of all, is that the entire purpose of a miracle is to challenge mankind 3x.**

Since the beginning of time, the point of giving a miracle to any prophet has always been, to challenge the people of their time. A challenge that if you think I'm lying, if you think I'm crazy, If you think I'm insane, then you do what I'm showing you. And if you cannot do it; if no one amonst you can do it; if you as in individual cannot do it; and if all of you collectively as a group cannot do it; then you must believe, that what I have been given can only be from Allah. Therefore when I tell you I'm the prophet, I speak the truth.

Nooh (AS) challenged his ummah with the flood. Ibrahim (AS) challenged his Umma with the fire. Moosa (AS) challenged Firaon with the staff turning into a snake, by parting the water. Eisa (AS) challenged his umma by curing the lepor and bring the dead back to life. Because no one from during that time was able to do the things, these prophets were able to do. So the purpose of a miracle is always to challenge mankind.

Prophet Suleman (AS) could speak with Jinns and animals, right? But that's not considered his miracle. Why? Because he did not challenge the poeple of his time with it! His miracle was what? the thrown of queen Sheebah (بلقیس کا تخت). He transported it from her kingdom to his. That was his miracle, because he challenged someone with that. Rasul Allah(Salallahu alayhi wa aalihee wa sallam) spit in the well and it started overflowing. That's pretty epic! Nobody can do that! So then why is that not the miracle of our prophet? Because he didn't challenge his nation with that? What did he challenge his nation with? The language and the eloquence of the Quran. And that's why Quran is considered his miracle.

Does everyone agree with these criteria?

So now let's first put Quran to the test for these ancient Arabs and and see if it fits the criteria.

1. Was any human being in Ancient Arabia able to match the eloquence of Quran? NO! So it was impossible for them to perform the same miracle

2. Did the Quran break the law of nature? It did! Because an unscripted impromptu speech should be flawed. Because as human beings we know we are not perfect, especially when it comes to conversations under hightened emotions. And Rasul Allah(Salallahu alayhi wa aalihee wa sallam) was delivering this message under all sorts of emotions. And if it's not full of flaws, it should have atleast some linguistic flaws! At least one flaw, right? But the ancient arabs could not find a single flaw in it. So it broke the law of human nature of speech.

3. Has the eloquence and perfection of Quran been duplicated? To this day, nobody has not been able to duplicate the perfection and eloquence of Quran.

4. Was it done by the only one claiming to be a messenger of Allah? Yes! So it fits the fourth criteria as well.

Now the most important one!

5. Was the Quran presented as a linguistic challenge to the ancient Arabs? It certainly was! And no one was able to answer this challenge. Is the Quran still a challenge to humanity? It absolutely is! Have linguists from our time come up with something better or even comparable? NO!

So the Quran fits all 5 criteria of miracle. Do you still remember the experience of miracle I showed you earlier? Now I want you to combine that experience of  أعجاز  with the criteria. Now imagine you are this hot-shot poet in ancient arabia! You are the best of the best! You are the "bomb" when it comes to Arabic poetry. People call you "the destroyer", "the crusher" because whoever you battle in poetry, you curst them! you destroy them! Poets are afraid to challenge you! They run the other way when they find out you've entered a poetry competition! And when someone does challenge you, you laugh in their face! Because you know they are so beneath you in eloquence. How dare you challenge me? Don't you know who I am? I am [Name] the "destroyer". You think you can take me on?

Now imagine a nobody like Rasul Allah(Salallahu alayhi wa aalihee wa sallam) coming to you with the verses of Quran. And I call him a "no body", because that is exactly what he was at the time. He was the definition of "nobody". He was an orphan; he was poor; he had no power; he had no status; he was not trained in poetry or eloquence, the one thing that Arabs took pride in. Now imagine, he comes to you with the verses of the Quran. Who are you? You're "the crusher"! You're "the destroyer". And the messenger (Salallahu alayhi wa aalihee wa sallam) comes to you and recites the verses of the Quran; and now imagine feeling, what I felt in that moment right before the truck hit me. Imagine listening to the words of the Quran and feeling completely helpless, completely incapacitated, completely overpowered; feeling down on your knees.

This was the miracle, the ⟪ar:أعجاز⟫of Quran. This is why the Quran is called ⟪ar:معجزۃ⟫, because when it challenges, the one being challenged becomes ⟪ar:عاجز⟫. He's forced to surrender. He cecomes incapacitated to the point that he canot even attempt a response. That's ⟪ar:معجزۃ⟫!

---

Why do prophets need miracles?

Volunteer

I want you to imagine something with me. Imagine you're sitting in your living room doing your thing, and there is a knock on the door. You open the door and you see your neighbour standing outside. He says "AsSalaamAlaykum", you say "WalaykumAsSalaam". But instead of saying "Can I borrow some sugar",  he says "Last night an angel came to me, and he told me that Allah has chosen me as his messenger. And now Allah has commanded me to deliver His message to all mankind. I already tried to invite my family, but they have all rejected me. Since you're my neighbour, and I care about you, I'm now delivering his message to you. I am Allah's messenger! and everything that I say from this point on, is not from me, it is from Allah himself. So obeying what I say is obeying Allah, and disobeying me is actually disobeying Allah".

So this is what your neighbour just hit you with. What's going through your mind right now? How would you resond to him? "Sorry! I no speak the ancient arabic!", right? Or "Are you OK? What did you have for dinner last night?" Or someone like me, would be like, "Oh the angel came to you too? Dude! He was here like 10 minutes ago and he said the same thing to me!" LOL

But seriously, would you believe him? Absolutely not! You'll say, "You've been my neighbour for so many years! I've seen you all my life, and now all of a sudden you want me to believe that an angel comes to you and Allah speaks to you through that angel? And then on top of that you're telling me that your own family has rejected you, they're calling you insane, but you want me to listen to you? Follow you? Obey you? You want me to change my entire life based on what you're saying? Everybody already thinks you're insane! What's going to happen if I follow you? What will they call me?

Aaah... No thank you! And you shut the door.

Think about this for a minute! We so easily condemn the disbelievers, "Oh these damn kuffar! They rejected the prophet, they called him insane! They should all go to hell", right? But put yourself in their shoes for a moment. What Rasul Allah was asking them, was not an easy thing to believe in. This bridge, from disbelief to faith, was not an easy bridge to cross. You see, today it's very easy for us to talk about Islam, and preach Islam, because it's been going on for thousands of years.

Just take these sessions as an example. I said I'm planning to begin these sessions on Quran, and you all just came. I didn't have to make any effort to invite you to these sessions (Kafia and Anees had to LOL). Why? Because you're already Muslims. You've already accepted Islam even if on the basis of faith. But you're all already somewhat sold into the idea of ISLAM. But this was not the case for the Arabs of that time! This was the very first time it was happening. It was a very difficult task that was being asked of them. Do you understand? So if your neighbour came to your doorstep and claimed to be a prophet, of course you will think he is insane!!!

Now tell me, why would you not believe him?

Do you know why? Statistics! Because you have never seen that happen before in your life. Believing in one God is not that far fetched. Believing in a hereafter - maybe possible. But what is absolutely impossible to believe? What you just cannot see happening is what? You just cannot see a man, who you've known all your life, pretty much as a nobody, suddenly being spoken to by an angel. That just goes beyond your wildest imagination. Right? Why you! Why not me? I have more money, more power than you! I'm more eloquent than you! I'm better than you in every single way! What's so special about you? So even if there was such a thing as revelation happening, logically it should happen to me, not to you!!

So I want you to first appreciate the state of mind of these Arabs when Rasul Allah(Salallahu alayhi wa aalihee wa sallam) was approaching them with the message. They were not bad people; they were not evil people. What was being asked of them was EXTREMELY difficult. When in the entire city, you are the only one holding a particular idea, a particular faith, that is different from everyone else's faith, what does that makes you? Crazy! It makes you insane! And what does it make the next person in line believing you? Just as insane! So before we write these people off as evil, and KUFFAR, put yourself in their shoes for a second.  How easy is it to accept when no one around you believes? The message of Rasul Allah (PBUH) was a VERY VERY VERY difficult thing to believe for the people in the city of Mecca. It was not easy. Faith was an EXTREMELY expensive, extremely dangeous commodity at that time. Do you understand?

---

OK, so now if you can appreciate that, now I want you to imagine something else. The person that the angel brought the message of prophethood to, is no one else, but YOU! Now it is YOU who has to go and knock on your neighbours door, and deliver this message to him. How would you feel about that? Would you be scared to do it? You would! And you would be absoulutely justified in begin scared. Forget your neighbour, if you told this to your own parents, you'll be sitting in a psychiatrist's office within the hour. So now imagine having to stand before a group of strangers, and promoting this novel idea, that goes, not only against all their existing beliefs, but also against the beliefs of their forefathers before them. How would you feel about delivering this message?

What would be some of the things you'd be afraid of?

Would you be afraid of ridicule? Of being called insane? Would you accept this task? Of course not! It's just too difficult. But Rasool Allah did it. He accepted the responsibility! Why? Was this his ticket to Jannah? No! He was already from the Jannah! Jannah was created for him! He already owned it! Then why would he accept such a difficult and painful responsibility?? You know why? He did it for me! He did it for you! So that you and I could be rescued from the slavery of our souls. So that you and I could have an actual shot at entering jannah. He said, if I don't take this step, how will the people of my ummah be free? How will they be guided? He did this for me! He did you this for you! He did this for all of us. Now that is love! That is mercy! That is a true blessing!

So now hopefully you can appreciate the enormous difficulty of this task, that Rasul Allah(Salallahu alayhi wa aalihee wa sallam) and all prophets before him had to take. So in order to make this delivery possible, Allah gave his prophets certain miracles as proof of their prophethood. These miracles were given to facilitate the decision of the people they were calling. The purpose was, that if you think I'm crazy! then let me show you, let me "challenge" you with what Allah gave me, and then you tell me if anyone besides Allah could have given this to me. If not, then this miracle is my proof to you, that I am speaking the truth. And if you're still not going to believe me, then it's only because you're arrogant and obstinate. But you can no longer deny that I am Allah's messenger.

That is why prophets are given miracles, so that they can challenge their nations in order to prove their truthfulness. When the nation of Moos (AS) saw the water parting; the staff turning into a serpent. When the nation of EISA (AS) saw the dead man coming to life, birds made from clay coming to life and flying, they were incapacitated; they were overpowered; all their arguments against them being the messengers of Allah, were instantly defeated. It brought them to their knees. And once you're on your knees, you have two choices. You can either surrender and fall into SAJDA; or you become arrogant and stand back up and choose to disbelieve. At that point it becomes a personal choice.

<!-- section 4 (id=5781, raw_sort=4): Speaker Content Style -->
We looked at the meaning of the word "miracle". The Arabic word for miracle is ⟪ar:معجزۃ⟫which comes from the root word ⟪ar:أعجاز⟫. And it means to bring someone down to his knees. It means to incapacitate; to overpower; to render someone incapable of a response. Then I explained that by definition, a miracle is not a scientific fact. Because it is not informational or instructional in nature. It cannot be taught or learnt. A miracle can only be experienced, and it is only real to the one experiencing it. Then we looked at the 5 conditions the ⟪ar:معجزۃ⟫should meet، in order to qualify as a miracle:

- It must be impossible for human beings to perform

- It must break the laws of nature

- It cannot be duplicated by anyone

- It can only be done by a prophet

- The most important of all; a miracle is used to challenge a nation. If something is not presented as a challenge, then no matter how incredible it is, it cannot be considered a miracle.

Then I explained why prophets were given miracles. It is because they are burdened with the most challenging and the most difficult of all tasks; which is to call people to abandon their ignorant ways of life and return to their creator. And so Allah gives his prophets certain miracles as proof of their prophethood. Miracles were given to facilitate the decision of the people that were being called, by challenging them with something that would be completely impossible for them to duplicate.

Why has the form of the miracle changed?

The next thing I want to talk to you about, is why Allah changed the form of his miracles when it came to our prophet (Salallahu alayhi wa aalihee wa sallam). I was reading the story of prophets to my daughter Erum when she was 6 years old. I went through all the prophets and their miracles one by one. When I reached Rasul Allah and told her about the miracle of Quran, she got really upset! She said "That's not fair Babu! Everyone else got such cool miracles! And all our prophet got was a book!! Now that sounds blasphemous, but she has a point. How come every other prophet got such cool miracles? And how come the best of the best just got a book? MOOSA (AS) got to turn a staff into serpent; EISA (AS) got to bring the dead back to life; Suleman AS could understand the speech of birds and animals. He had this cool teleportation device; DAWOOD AS could bend steel with his melody, birds would stop flying and hover in mid-air, just to hear his melody. So all previous prophets got these amazing X-MEN kinda miracles, and all our prophet got was a book! So she was right. She had a valid point. So I asked her, why do you think the other miracles were so cool? She said because if I could see them! But the miracle of Quran is not something I can see!

And that is absolutely correct. Quran was not for the eyes to see, it was for what? It was a speech for the ears. And Allah himself says this in the Quran:

⟪ar-quote:قُلْ أُوحِىَ إِلَىَّ أَنَّهُ ٱسْتَمَعَ نَفَرٌۭ مِّنَ ٱلْجِنِّ فَقَالُوٓا۟ إِنَّا سَمِعْنَا قُرْآنًا عَجَبًۭا⟫

Say we have heard someone reciting this incredible Quran
⟪ar-quote:قَالُوا۟ يَقَوْمَنَآ إِنَّا سَمِعْنَا كِتَبًا أُنزِلَ مِنۢ بَعْدِ مُوسَىٰ⟫

They said we heard this book that was revealed after MOOSA
⟪ar-quote:يَٓأَيُّهَا ٱلنَّاسُ ضُرِبَ مَثَلٌۭ فَٱسْتَمِعُوا۟ لَهُ⟫

Listen! Listen! Listen! Oh people! I'm giving you examples, so you can listen!

So it was a speech for the ancient arabs and it is a book for us.
⟪ar-quote:ذَلِكَ ٱلْكِتَبُ لَا رَيْبَ ۛ فِيهِ ۛ هُدًۭى لِّلْمُتَّقِينَ⟫

A book that has no ambiguity in it
⟪ar-quote:وَلَمَّا جَآءَهُمْ كِتَبٌۭ مِّنْ عِندِ ٱللَّهِ مُصَدِّقٌۭ لِّمَا مَعَهُمْ⟫

And when there came to them a "book" from Allah confirming what they already knew.

So when it came the Quran, the form of the miracle changed. Speech for them; book for us! Why did Allah all of a sudden change his format? Why did he switch from video to audio? Cause that sounds like a step down, doesn't it? The reason he changed the format is, because when you cannot see something, what are you forced to do? You are forced to imagine! Is imagination more powerful or is sight more powerful? Isn't this why movies turn out to be such a disappointment when you've read the book first? Because the movie cannot match up to your imagination. What were the Arabs so big on? What did they take so much pride in? Their ability to imagine and paint that imagination in words! They believed that there couldn't possibly be a greater imagination than the Arab imagination. And no one could express that super imagination better than them. But the Quran, with its mesmerizing words, created the ultimate imagination for them! An imagination that was way superior than the Arab imagination; using words that were so precise, so perfect, so eloquent, so mesmerizing, that it brought them to their knees. It incapacitated them. This is why the Quran became a miracle to them.

OK! So good for them! We're happy for them! But how does this relate to us? Let's talk about that.

Are all the previous miracles of prophets alive today? Or are they dead? Is the water that MOOSA (AS) parted, still separated or has it joined back? Are dead men still coming to life? Does fire still turn into a bed of flowers? No! These miracles occurred in a particular instance, and then it was all over. But is the Quran still alive? Is its ability to challenge the imagination still alive? Let's say, for the sake of argument, if we were actually able to experience the miracle of Quran, then could we repeat that experience for us as many times as we wanted? Could we experience its miracle over and over and over again? Yes We could!

See! When the people of MOOSA (AS) were standing at the bank of the river, and they saw it split in two, they experienced a miracle. Then they narrated that incident to their children. A father when to his son and said, "Look this is what happened! I was standing right there! I saw it with my own eyes!!" Then the child when he grows up, narrates it to his child, "My dad was there when it happened!". Then his child narrates it to his children, that my grandfather was there when it happend. And this goes on an on for thousands of years, until the story finally reaches us. But when we narrate the story of MOOSA (AS) to our kids, it's more like (yawn) yeah there was something about MOOSA and the river parting or something. Why? Because to us it is just a story! A story that we have accepted on faith. But that man who narrated this story the first time, for him, was it just a story? No, it was a miracle to him! You understand the difference?

What created this difference? Why is it a miracle to that man and a story to us? Because the miracle is over! It happened once in the history of time, and never again. The river will never split again. Bird made of clay will not come to life and fly off ever again. Anything that is seen with the eye, has a short life span. You see it and then it's over and it becomes a story. So all these miracles that took place in the times of the previous prophets, could have been miracles to them. But for us, they're just stories that we accept on faith.

And this is why, when an athiest comes to a Jew or Christian, and he asks, "Hey! Is it true that Jesus, brough the dead back to life?" They say of course! He asks, how do you know that? The Christian says, because it's in the bible. He says, Did you actually see that miracle with your own eyes? Were you there? No! So then how do you know it happened? Did anybody record it? Is it on YouTube? The Christian says because I believe in it! So the athiest says, then don't tell me that story, because that's just your belief! And anyone can believe anything! I can only believe what I see and experience! I'm not going to believe just based on a story.

Now when the same athiest comes to us Muslims and asks, "Is Quran the message of Allah?" We say of course! He asks, "Did you see Jibraeel (AS) descend from the heavens with the message?" We say No! So then how do you know this is the message of Allah? Our response is, "Let me show you!! Let's study this book together, and let me show you why this can't be from a human being. And then you be the judge of it. You decide for yourself, if this could be human speech". You see the difference?

You see, our response to that athiest, when we said, "Let me show you!", this is the part that these sessions are all about. After the last sessions a bunch of you asked, "Why isn't there a miracle happening today? Wouldn't it be awesome if we could experience a miracle too?". Well, there is a miracle happening today; there is a miracle happening every single moment of every single day; and that miracle is still the Quran. But the problem is when you think of miracle, what sense are thinking in terms of? Sight! And what sense is the Quran for? Hearing! So we all need to begin by shifting our paradigm; or the way we look at this Quran as a miracle. It is a miracle for the ears, for the intellect, and not for the sight. Why? Because sight is temporary and its experience is not repeatable! Hearing and comprehension is permanent and it is infinitely repeatable.

---

3 components of effective communication

**https://quran.com/14/52** --- ***This site has such terrible translation BTW. So ignore the translation, just look at the AYAH***

So with that said, today I want to talk to you about the Quran in light of it being an impromptu, unscripted speech. Because originally that's what the Quran is. It is a conversation. It is communication.
⟪ar:هَذَا بَلَغٌۭ⟫This is a message, a communication ⟪ar:لِّلنَّاسِ⟫  Who is this message for? for all mankind - not just muslims or believers, but for all mankind in general. What's its purpose? ⟪ar:وَلِيُنذَرُوا۟ بِهِ⟫ so they could be warned ? Of what? ⟪ar:وَلِيَعْلَمُوٓا۟ أَنَّمَا هُوَ إِلَهٌۭ وَحِدٌۭ⟫ So that they become aware that their lord is only one! And who is it for? Who are the audience of the Quran?  ⟪ar:وَلِيَذَّكَّرَ أُو۟لُوا۟ ٱلْأَلْبَبِ⟫ ۔ . And so the people of sound intellect may take heed from it. So Allah calls the Quran a communication, for a particular audience the ⟪ar:أُو۟لُوا۟ ٱلْأَلْبَبِ⟫. People of sound intellects. That's all you need in order to understand this message. An intellect!

[diagram: Two stick figures speaking via tin-can telephones; a large purple 'INFLUENCE' arrow runs left-to-right between them; checklist below lists CONTENT, SPEAKER, STYLE as the three elements of effective communication.]
  (see ../images/004.png)
  *Note:* Pedagogical communication model — the speaker, the content, and the style together produce influence.

When we communiate, there are essentially 3 components to an effective communication. Notice these are two separate words - "effective" and "communication". We'll first talk about the components of a good communication, and then discuss what makes it effective. Any seminar today on communication will tell you that there are 3 components to an effective conversation:

1- Content

2- Speaker

3- Style

So now let's talk about these components individually:

### Content

The first is "content". What is content? It is the stuff that you are going to say! A good communication or a powerful conversation is something that has a purpose; it is something that is truthful; it is something that is relatable; something that is beneficial to someone. We live in a world today where a *lot* is said and heard; but at the end of it, nothing substantial is actually said. Most of our conversations today is just "noise".

I'll give you an example. You may have certain friends (or you may know of people) that talk a lot, but they don't actually say anything meaningful in their conversations. At the end of 2 hours of listening to them, when you aks yourself, what was the conversation about? You have absolutely no idea. So for instance your friend calls you up to discuss homework. But instead of talking about homework, she begins by telling you how when she was a child, her favorite lolipop was red, and she had a swing in her backyard; and how her brother was.... the hind part of a certain animal when they were growing up.... And she ends up talking to you for an hour about everything on the planet, except homework. And then she says, "Sorry I'm getting another call and she hangs up". And now you're left there thinking what was that entire conversation about?! What was the point of that whole conversation?! Why? Because that conversation had no content!  And so good content is the first key to an effective communication.

**### Speaker**

The second component is the speaker. When we see someone speaking, even before the person opens his mouth, just by the way he is dressed, the way he looks, his age, his body language, based on these things, we've already made a judgment about this person. We've already formed an opinion. Think about it this way...

You have an important science question that you know is going to be on the exam. You need help understanding a certain concept. So you walk into your professors office for guidance. When you enter the room you see some kid, who looks much younger than you, wearing a P-cap backwards, sitting next to the professor talking to him. You walk up to the professor and say, "Sir! Can you please explain to me again, how the process of photosynthesis works?" As soon as you ask the question, the kid jumps up and says, "Hey! I can explain it to you!" And then without your permission, he begins responding to your question. Now would you take his answer seriously? Or would you prefer that the professor explain it to you?

Why? Not because what the kid said was wrong. Maybe he explained everything correctly, but it's coming from a source that you don't really acknowledge to be the expert for that content. But when the professor gives you the exact same answer, it holds lot more value for you! So who did you take into consideration there? The speaker!  So the credentials and the qualifications of the speaker are extremely important for communication to be effective.

Repeat

### **Style**

The third ingredient of a powerful communication is the style. It is not just what is being said; or who's saying it; it is also the "style", the "way" in which it is being said. I'll give you a personal example. We all go to MAJALIS and religious gatherings from time to time. And in almost all of these gatherings, the speaker is talking about something from the QURAN or from the AHADEES of Rasul Allah(Salallahu alayhi wa aalihee wa sallam). Isn't that true? Which means that there is nothing wrong with the "content". The content is powerful! But some speakers will deliver that content in such a boring, such a monotonous way, that it can put the entire audience to sleep. I have had the pleasure of attending some of these MAJALIS as a teenager, where I could literally see the speaker releasing sleeping gas from his mouth when he's talking. I have had some of the BEST sleep of my life during some of these gatherings. And then feeling my dad's elbow in my ribs whispering, "UTH JAA KAMBAKHT! ZALEEL KARWA RAHA HAI SAB K SAAMNEY". LOL

So what is the problem this time? It can't be the content because it is verses from the Quran. The content is divine! It can't be the speaker because he is a religious scholar; he's a very learned man. What is the problem now? It's the style. The way in which the content is being presented. You have to have a style which keeps people awake.

And this is not just about public speaking. It applies even inside our homes. There are different ways of presenting the same content. My wife comes home from work and decides to cook my favorite meal. She puts a lot of effort into it. She has it on the table before I even get there. I sit down to eat and notice that it has a little less salt than I'm used to. The food could use a little bit more salt. So what I want to say, is that I want more salt. But there are different styles of saying that.

I could say, This is the most amazing dinner I have ever had! This food tastes like it was sent down from heaven. If there was a bit more salt in it, it would taste like it was from the 7th level of heaven. Can I have some salt please? That's one way of doing it!

Another way of doing it is, "Woman! Is the economy so bad, that you couldn't put some more salt in this food? And BTW I hate your mother. Every time she visits etc. etc.".... LOL. I'm saying the same thing that the food needs salt, but there are different ways of saying it. Same content, different style. One style makes my life easy; the second makes me sleep on the couch - hungry. So style is extremely important.

### Audience

So these are the three essential components to an good communication. But the communication we're trying to understand is not just any communication, but "effective" communication. There is a difference between powerful communication and an effective communication. I could give an extremely powerful speech on how to bring about a change in "economy" to a bunch of nursery kids; and put them to sleep. Why? Because even though the communication is extremely powerful, the kids are not the right audience for it. So in order for even a powerful communication to be "effective", we must know who we are talking to. We need to tailor the message to the level of the audience we are speaking to.

The way I talk to my child is not the way I talk to my father. Even if I tell them the exact same thing. If I want to invite my dad to these sessions, the way in which I would go about inviting him will be very different, than the way I would invite my daughter. Even though I'm inviting both to the exact same session. You understand? The content is the same; the speaker is the same; but depending on who I'm talking to (my audience), my conversation changes to make it more effective.

Think about a classroom. Your teacher does not talk to all the students the same way. There are some students who are brilliant and they understand things immediately; but then there are others like me, who take a while to understand things. So my teachers had to adjust their styles to suit my level of intellect. This is why they mostly spoke to me using a very different kind of language that included hands and feets and sticks and chairs and anything else they could get their hands on. And they used very affectionate words to address me, which wouldn't be appropriate to share in this group.

Now how would you measure effective communication? What scale would you use to guage if a conversation was "effective" or not. Because all forms of communications can be subjective. You like a book! I don't! I love a conversation! You don't! It's based on personal opinion. So then how can we judge an effective conversation? What is the measuring stick?

The measurint stick (the scale) is, what influence does it have on the audience! What kind of an impact it has on the world. What change does it bring? How does it influence behavior? How does that conversation command and rule over people? That would be a practical measure and proof of an "effective" communication. When people heard the speech, did it change their lives? Or did they just call it a "wonderful speech", give the speaker a standing ovation and then returned to their business? That is what measures effectiveness.

Now Quran is an incredibly powerful speech! Because its speaker is "incredibly" powerful; its content is "incredibly" powerful; its "style" is incredibly powerful! What does that make the message? this communication of Quran? It makes it incredibly powerful. Yes? So we agree that the Quran, despite being an improptu, unscripted message, is an incredibly powerful message. But the real question is, is the Quran also an incredibly effective message or not?

You see there are many famous people who brought about revolutions through their speeches. The world has seen many revolutions that changed the world. But whenever you have a "revolution", those changes are either political in nature; or they are economic in nature, or they they bring out a military change. But the way people live on a day to day basis, that does not change. If a new government comes into power, it doesn't change the way children interact with their parents; or how husbands treat to their wives. All of that still remains the same.

There were people like Ghandi with and many others like him, that revolutionized a nation and moved them towards an incredible freedom movement. There were people like Martin Luther King who brought about changes in the civil rights of black people. He gave that famous "I have a dream" speech that was a very effective communication, because it inspired a positive change towards racial equalities. But did it change the way people behaved with each other in their household? Did it change the way people went to their jobs? Did it change what people ate for dinner? It did not! These people were effective in bringing out change in one particular aspect in society. And as effective as their speeches were, were they unscipted? were they unprepared? extemporaneous speeches? NO! They were pre-written, pre-prepared speeches; and yet they brought about changes in one particular area of peoples lives.

And did these people bring about the revolution all by themselves? Or were there other people doing the same work with them on the same platform at the same time? There were always a group of people bringing about this change? Gandhi wasn't alone! Martin Luther King wasn't the only one working for civil rights. Those of you who are in high school have studied the French Revolution in Europe. That revolution was brought about by people who read the works of philosophers, that they left behind decades ago. Look at the Russian Revolution, the communist revolution. Do you know who the author of  of the communist revolution was? It's Karl Marx. Do you know where Karl Marx was from? He was from Germany, and he died 60 years before the Russian Revolution began. The guy was a librarian; he was a writer. He was a philosopher, sitting in a quite room 60 years back, writing about all of this stuff. It wasn't even in his wildest dreams that people will be killing each other over this one day. And 60 years after his death, there are people revolutionizing  a country based on his works, right?

You see there is this historical formula! The philosopher of an idea, is never himself on the battlefield. Never! And the philosopher of an idea is not a revolutionist himself. He is simply a philosopher. He's not going out there to convince people to make a change. All he's doing is writing and presenting ideas completely disconnected from the reality of the actual work.

In the case of our prophet Muhammad (Salallahu alayhi wa aalihee wa sallam)  who's presenting the idea? who's delivering the message? And who is on the battlefield? And not just in the battlefield, who is in the front of the battlefield? Who's delivering the message and being boycotted for it? Who is being forced to hide in a cave? Who is being expelled from his own house? from his own city? He's not just standing behind some podium, telling "other people" to march forward. He is the first to march forward, even when there is no one standing behind him. This has never before happened in the history of mankind! Ever! Ask your political science professor! Ask your history professor.

So all other forms of effective communications that this world has seen, were brought about by a bunch of philosophers and a group of activits, collectively. And the change they brought about was limited to on particular dimension of society.  And all of this was based on pre-prepared, scripted speeches.

Now let's look at the change the Quran brought! If you study this fact historically, no society went through such transformation based on a single text, the way in which the muslims went through with which communication? The Quran! No other society in history! And in how many years did that society get transformed? Just 23 years! Even orientalists agree to this! The first Ayat is revealed at the age of 40, and it stops at the age of 63. Just 23 years. In these 23 years, this man begins the unscripted speech of Quran; *single handedly* mind you; and by the end of these 23 years let's see what change these words, and this speaker, and this content, and this style of speaking bring about. What change did the Quran influence in its audience?

Did it change the way in which people eat? Did it change what people ate and what they didn't? Did it change the way people sleep? Did it change the direction in which people pray? Did it change the way in which they prayed? Did it change the way people deal with their families? Did it change the way husbands treat their wives? Did it change the way parents treat their children; the way children behave with their parents? Did it change the rules of inheritance? Did it change how people scheduled their day? Did it change the way people spoke to each other? Did it change the way people greet one another? Did it change the way people do their business? Did it change the way people give and take loans? Did it change the way people dress? Did it change the way people married? Did it change the way people got divorced? Did it change the way rich treated the poor? Did it inspire change at a societal level? Did it inspire change at a personal level? Did it influence a change in physical hygene? Did it change the way we go to the bathroom? The way we brush our teeth?  Did it influence spiritual matters? Did it influence changes at a constitutional level? social level? political level? Judicial level? economic level? moral level? civil level? societal level? educational level? The question isn't what changed! You know what the right question is? What didn't change?

Everything changed! Every single aspect of human existence changed. Everything, from the very individual level, to the collective level and every spectrum in between changed. This speech completely changed things at a micro level as well as a macro leve. This in itself is the evidence of the unparallel power of the Quran. This was the unparalleled "effectiveness", of this impromptu message, delivered single handedly by one man - Muhammad Mustafa (Salallahu alayhi wa aalihee wa sallam) in a period of only 23 years. SubhanAllah!!

You give me one example in human history, from the beginning of time, that brought about a change of this magnitude in every single aspect of human life. You can't! And when you can't; when you cannot even begin to give an example; because none of us are even going to bother researching this. Because we know, that there is not a single unscripted communication [single impromptu conversation, single extempore speech] in human existence, other than the Quran, that brought about a change of this magnitude. And the fact that we are so incapacitated; so overpowered; completely defeated to come up with a response, *is* the very definition of ⟪ar:أعجاز⟫. That is the very definition of a miracle. Because a miracle is that which incapacitates and leaves one incapable of a response. So if you just experienced this feeling of defeat with me, then by definition, you just experienced the first first miracle of Quran InshaAllah .

<!-- section 5 (id=5782, raw_sort=5): Effectiveness of style on 3 people -->
Recap:

What have we learnt so far? We've established that the Quran is an unscripted, impromptu speech that was delivered by Rasul Allah(Salallahu alayhi wa aalihee wa sallam) before a live audience comprising of not just family and friends, but also his mortal enemies. What we're trying to understand is that if Quran is the message of Allah; or is it the message of the prophet. In order to do that, we studied the word "miracle" to understand what it means. The word ⟪ar:معجزۃ⟫I told you comes from the word ⟪ar:اعجاز⟫or ⟪ar:عجز⟫which means to incapacitate or overpower someone. To render someone incapable of a response. To completely defeat someone and bring someone down to his knees. So if two wrestlers are fighting, and one wrestler defeats the other in such a clear way, that he cannot even attempt to get up, that would be a good example of being ⟪ar:عاجز⟫.

Another thing we learnt about miracles is that its nature is that of an experience. It is not something scientific or informational that can be taught and learnt. It is something that can only be experienced. And the reason prophets are given miracles by Allah(Subhanhu Wa Ta'ala), is firstly, to prove the authenticity of the prophets; and secondly "challenge" the nation they are you calling. Because one of the most important criteria of a miracle is that it challenges people. In other words, if you think I'm lying! If you think I'm making this up; if you believe I am not the true messenger of Allah, then you do what I'm doing. And so Allah gives prophets these miracles, that are extraordinary events of the same nature, that the people of the time excel in. And so when the time of the prophet (Salallahu alayhi wa aalihee wa sallam) came, Arabs excelled in language! And we looked at the factors that led to the creation of the Arab's powerful imagination, and their ability to articulate that imagination in the most poetic form. We saw how these people were crazy about language, and how seriously they took it; and how they were willing to die for it. And then Quran comes to these extremely eloquent people, and they are completely dumb-founded. Even the most articulate Arab, is unable to speak; he has nothing to say when presented with the verses of Quran! Talk about being defeated at ones own game!

In the previous session we looked at Quran as a communication from Allah. Every form of communication has 3 components: It has a "speaker", it has a "content" and it has a "style". And together these three elements create what's called a powerful or eloquent conversation. But powerful communication may not always be effective communication. So we also looked at what makes a conversation effective. Effectiveness is measured by the influence it has on its audience; in the way it changes their lives. And so based on historical facts, we see that the Quran was an extremely powerful communication, because its speaker was extremely powerful! it's content was extremely powerful! and it's style was extremely powerful! But what proved its effectiveness, is the exceptional, and unparalled change it brought in the lives of the people. How it took the most barbaric nation on the face of this earth and turned them into angelic beings. You know how you were told these bed time stories about this guy who would turn rocks into pure gold? Rasul Allah(Salallahu alayhi wa aalihee wa sallam) actually did it. He took these uncivilized, cruel, barbaric people who were worthless like stones, and turned them into precious role-models for generations to come, to the point that we do not even mention their name without saying (⟪ar:رحمۃ اللہ علیہ⟫). And he did this single handedly in only a period of 23 years through this incredible message. These are simply historict facts that are undeniable.

So I want to move this conversation forward. Today what I want to focus on, is not the first dimesnion of the Quran, which is the speaker; not the second one, which is the content; but the third, which is its style! In other words, I don't want to focus on the fact that Allah is the one speaking through the Quran; nor do I want to focus on what he's saying, which is the content; I want to focus on the style! I want to focus on "How" he says it. This is where the Quran is truly unique and effective, in the "way" it communicates.

And this component of style is something that is really important for us to understand. In the very first session, I showed you guys how things are completely lost in translation. You see..... the Quran when it's translated, you already know who the message is from. Now maybe, just maybe; you might get the content; you might get some portion of "what" Allah says. But what is it that you will *definitely* not get? You'll not get "how" he said it! That is completely, 100% lost in translation. Because how he said it, exists in which language? In Arabic. And so, even if you try to explain it to someone in Arabic; in your own Arabic; it will still be "you" saying it, but it will definitely not be how "Allah" said it. So the creative beauty, the unique elegance, the unparalleled majesty of Allah's words, simply cannot be translated. Something from its meaning can be translated. But the ***impact*** that the original words have, nothing else can have. And this creates a gap! Now if you want to understand the distance of this gap, just think of the distance between Allah and his creation! That should give you a good idea of the distance between Allah's words and man's translations. Because Quran is from Allah, and the translation is from his creation; and mans translation, can NEVER be a substitue for Allah's words. It's just impossible. So this is something we need to appreciate even in our times.

But let's talk about why this component of style was so important to the ancient arabs. We as Muslims, who do we believe is the ultimate speaker of this communication? Who is this message from? It's from Allah! We as Muslims just believe this! But when a non-muslim or a disbeliever hears this communication, who does he see delivering the message? Who does he believe to be the speaker? He believes the message is from Rasul Allah(Salallahu alayhi wa aalihee wa sallam). This is very important to understand. To you and I, this is the message of Allah, but to the disbeliever, it's not the message of Allah, because he does not believe in Allah. If he did, that would make him what? A muslim! So a KAFIR believes that this is message of Rasool Allah, correct?

What are the 3 components of communication again? Speaker, content, style! So now if you think about it rationally, this Quran, based on the components of speaker and content alone, it could be a miracle to the Muslims; but it could never be a miracle to the disbeliever. You understand? Because they do not believe in the speaker. And when you don't believe in the speaker, you don't even want to listen to the content. Isn't that true?

So the question we now have to ask is, if the ancient arab did not experience a miracle in the "speaker"; if they did not experience a miracle in the "content"; what did they experience a miracle in? What was it that mesmerized these people? What was it that every time the messenger of Allah (Salallahu alayhi wa aalihee wa sallam) opened his mouth, they would be dumbfound. They wouldn't know what to say? It was it's incredible style! You understand? It was the style, the beautiful way in which it was being said, that made this message a miracle to the disbelievers. And this is something we completely lose when we study the Quran through the filter of translation.

---

I'll give you an example:

**http://quran.com/3/37**

⟪ar-quote:فَتَقَبَّلَهَا رَبُّهَا بِقَبُولٍ حَسَنٍۢ.....  وَأَنۢبَتَهَا نَبَاتًا حَسَنًۭا وَكَفَّلَهَا زَكَرِيَّ⟫

So her Lord accepted her with good acceptance, and caused her to grow in a good manner, and put her in the care of Zakariya. And just right there, you can see that this translation is not at all eloquent even by English standards. So even without explaining this AYAH, you can witness the degradation that takes place in translation. Now what is this verse talking about?

This verse is talking about prophet Zakariya raising Mariam SA. To describe how he raised her, Allah used the words of cultivating a plant ⟪ar:وَأَنۢبَتَهَا نَبَاتًا⟫. He raised her like a delicate plant, that you water; you make sure that it gets enough sun, you make sure the soil does not get contaminated, or get any kind of infestations. This is called ⟪ar:أِنبَات⟫. Planting something and allowing it to grow. So Allah says

⟪ar-quote:أَنۢبَتَهَا نَبَاتًا حَسَنًۭا⟫

He cultivated her; he allowed her to grow in the most beautiful way; and the word used are: ⟪ar:نَبَاتًا حَسَنًۭا⟫. Which is horribly translated here as: caused her to grow in a good manner. But to the ancient Arab, the expected word, grammatically, should have been ⟪ar:أِنبَاتاً⟫. If they were to say this, they would have said:

⟪ar-quote:أَنۢبَتَهَا أِنبَاتاً حَسَنًۭا⟫

So what's the difference? The first one ⟪ar:أَنۢبَتَهَا⟫, suggests that Zakariya took care of raising this child. He provided good environment for her; he provided her with nourishment; he provided her with good education; good mannerisms, ettiquettes, proper behavior; he gradually developed her spiritually. This is all part of Zakriya doing his part in raising Mariam. The AYAH is giving Zakariya for a job well done. Now we see in life, that parents do their best in terms of trying to raise their children. But sometimes the children when they grow up, they choose a completely different path, which is not the path their parents wanted for them. They don't turn out as the parents hoped. So if Allah had used the word ⟪ar:أِنبَاتاً⟫, (which the ancient Arab would have used) that would mean that ZAKARIYA did his part in raising MARIAM; but it would not necessarily mean that Mariam too, took in all of that development, internalized it for herself and benefitted from it. Had Allah said ⟪ar:أِنبَاتاً⟫, then all of the credit would go *only* to Zakriya. But Allah instead said ⟪ar:نَبَاتًا⟫, which linguistically suggests that she reciprocated; and also grew in the most beautiful way. In other words, this verse, simply by the usage of the word ⟪ar:نَبَاتًا⟫,  gives credit not only to ZAKARIYA for doing a marvelous job of raising MARIAM, but also gives credit to MARIAM, for taking advantage of that great development and training, that her uncle ZAKARIYA provided for her. What it's saying is that she too realized that training in the form of the highest of character. So Allah is actually complementing both of them through the use of this one single word. But in translation you only end up giving credit to ZAKARIYA and not MARIAM.

And this style is what got to the Ancient Arabs. Because to them using two words, where one word could have been used was a major flaw [defect] in language. And Rasul Allah(Salallahu alayhi wa aalihee wa sallam) using such "perfect" language in an unscripted, impromptu speech, was completely astonishing to them. Because they realized that human beings cannot speak with this kind of perfection - consistently.

Salaam of Ibraheem and angels

[**http://quran.com/51/25**]

That is a story in the Quran in which the Angels came to the house of prophet IBRAHEEM (AS), and they knock on the door and the Arabic says:

⟪ar-quote:إِذْ دَخَلُوا۟ عَلَيْهِ فَقَالُوا۟ سَلَمًۭا.....  قَالَ سَلَمٌۭ⟫

The English translation says, When they entered the house, they said, "peace." He answered, "peace". You are strangers to me.

Now we know that when we greet someone in the Islamic tradition, we greet them by saying AsSalaamAlaykum, which means "may peace and safety be with you". And so the Quran says, that the Angels said "peace" and Ibraheem (AS) also responded with "peace". Except when the angels said peace, they said ⟪ar:سَلَمًۭا⟫. The word SALAAM ends with ⟪ar:مًۭا⟫. But when IBRAHEEM AS responds, he says with ⟪ar:سَلَمٌۭ⟫. In other words the way in which the Angels offered peace is different than the way IBRAHEEM (AS) responded with peace.

What's the difference? When the angels said ⟪ar:سَلَمًۭا⟫, what they actually said was, "You will not receive any harm from us! you will remain at peace and you will remain safe!". Now in the ISLAMIC tradition, a gift is always returned with a greater or equal gift. That's why when someone says AsSalaamAlaykum to us, we respond with ⟪ar:وعلیکم السلام و رحمۃ اللہ و برکاتہ⟫ . And may peace and safety be with you as well and may Allah shower his blessings and create abundance for you! So IBRAHEEM (AS) responds with ⟪ar:سَلَمٌۭ⟫, which means "that may you be surrounded with "eternal" peace! Not just peace and safety for now, but with everlasting peace and safety. And not just peace from me, but from everyone else around you. But then IBRAHEEM (AS) isn't sure that if these strangers will keep their word or not. So embedded within the ⟪ar:سَلَمٌۭ⟫ is also a prayer for himself. That Oh Allah! keep me safe from any harm!

All of that is captured within the MUN of the SALAAM. SubhanAllah! What does the English translation says? They said "peace"; he said "peace", and all the linguistic nuances of the word are the style of presentation is lost. So I hope these examples help you appreciate the fact that how much is actually lost in translation. And what is it that we're losing? We still know this message is from Allah; we still get "some" of the content - atleast we understand that they're both exchanging peace or greeting each other. But what's completely lost? The style! The beauty of IBRAHEEM (AS) response is completely lost in translation.

---

So this was the influence that Quran's unique style had on these Ancient Arabs. They never heard anyone speak like this before! With such incredible perfection! And specially not someone who was considered nobody; had no formal training in eloquence; and now he is speaking extemporaneously; without any preparation, with such incredible perfection. And this is how the speech of Quran became a miracle to these people; not so much by virtue of the speaker or the content; but by virtue of its style. They were defeated by it; they were incapacitated by it; and their intellects forced them to believe, that indeed these cannot be the words of a man. And once they believed this message is from God, only then the content and the speaker became valuable to them. You understand?

I'm going to share with you 3 stories today to highlight the *effect* that the "style" of Quran had on some of the people of that time. In the previous session I talked about the general or global impact the Quran had on the lives of people. Today, we're going to zoom in, and look at very speicific examples of how it affected people at an individual level. This way we'll be able to appreciate both realities InshaAllah. What I do hope you will experience, is the kind of profound effect the style of Quran had on some of the most staunch disbelievers of that time.

---

### Tufail bin A'amir Al-Dausi

He was the leader of his tribe. In those days, the best man in the group would be chosen as the leader of the tribe. And what was the measuring stick of true virtue for the Arabs of that time? Language! So if Tufail bin Amir was chosen as the leader of his tribe, that implies what? That he was above the rest in what? Language! He was the best poet of his tribe! Remember that they're all incredible poets! But he's the best of the best! Now I want you to imagine a person of his position. Would you imagine he'd be easily impressed by another poet? Obviously not!

He goes to Makka to perform tawaaf of the Ka'aba (as the Arabs used to do during that time). The leaders of Quraish find out that he's coming. They get worried that he might hear the prophet reciting Quran; and if that happens, he might get enchanted. So they meet him at the out-skirts of the city, and they try to dissuade him about the prophet. They say to him, "Listen! There is a man in the city, who says these words, and puts a spell on people. He turns sons against their fathers, brother against brother, husband against wife. He creates disunity in tribes. Our people are being posessed by deamons when he speaks to them. We think you're an important figure for your tribe. We believe that your integrity is going to be compromised if he casts his spells on you". And as they're saying this they hand him ear plugs. They say, in order to be safe, just plug your ears so that you do not listen to what he says.

Imagine that! They hand him ear-plugs! Now why did they do that? Because what happens to a tribe when a leader becomes Muslim? The tribe members follow! So they had to take care of business!

Tufail Ibn A'amir goes to the Ka'ab and does his tawaaf. The messanger of Allah is sitting there reciting Quran. He hears the sweetness of the words, and realizes this is the man they were warning him about. So what does he do? He plug his ears and he dashes the other way. He starts running away from the prophet. But as he's running, he says to himself, What am I doing? I am the leader of my tribe! I am the pride of my people! There is not a single poet who can stand against me in eloquence. I am the most skillful poets in all of arabia. Just a few words are going to overpower me? That's ridiculous! I can take this! So he unplugs his ears and goes back to the messenger of Allah. He sits next to him and says:
⟪ar-quote:یا محمد! ما عندک؟⟫

Oh Muhammad tell me what you have! So Rasul Allah turns to him and says:
⟪ar-quote:أِنَّ الحَمدَ لِی اللہَ ؛ أحمَدَہُ ، وَ أستَعِینَہُ ، وَ أُومِنُ بِہِ ، وَ أتَوَکَّلُ عَلَیہِ ۔۔۔۔ مَن یَّھدِہِ اللہُ فَلاَ مُضِلَّ لَہ ؛ وَ مَن ⟪ar-quote:یُضلِلہُ⟫فَلاَ ھَادِیَ لَہ⟫
That's it! That's all he says!

⟪ar-quote:أِنَّ الحَمدَ لِی اللہَ⟫

All praise is for Allah!

⟪ar-quote:أحمَدَہُ ، وَ أستَعِینَہُ ، وَ أُومِنُ بِہِ ، وَ أتَوَکَّلُ عَلَیہِ⟫

I praise Him, and I seek his help in all matters, and I seek safety through Him, and I rely completely upon Him,

⟪ar-quote:مَن یَّھدِہِ اللہُ فَلاَ مُضِلَّ لَہ ؛ وَ مَن یُضلِلہُ فَلاَ ھَادِیَ لَہ⟫

For the one He guides can never stray; and the one he misleads, can never find guidance.

This is all he says! Tufail Ibn Amir hears this one sentence, and he's stunned! He is mesmerized! and he says to the prophet:

⟪ar-quote:أُعِد أُعِد! فَقَد بَلَغنَ قَامُوس البَحر⟫

Repeat it ! Repeat it! Indeed this one sentence contains with in the depth of 7 oceans! What mesmerized him? The profoundness and the depth of this one short verse. Because to the Arabs the more concise and the more precise the words are, the more eloquent the speech is. And so what he experiences in that one sentence, is the depth of 7 oceans! And so he begs the prophet to repeat it again for him. And Rasul Allah(Salallahu alayhi wa aalihee wa sallam) again says:
⟪ar-quote:أِنَّ الحَمدَ لِی اللہَ ؛ أحمَدَہُ ، وَ أستَعِینَہُ ، وَ أُومِنُ بِہِ ، وَ أتَوَکَّلُ عَلَیہِ ۔۔۔۔ مَن یَّھدِہِ اللہُ فَلاَ مُضِلَّ لَہ ؛ وَ مَن ⟪ar-quote:یُضلِلہُ⟫فَلاَ ھَادِیَ لَہ⟫
And Tufail bin Amir begins crying. With tears in his eyes, he puts his hands in the hand of the prophet and says. I submit! Make me a muslim! He recites the SHAHADAH (⟪ar:لا الہ الا اللہ⟫) right there and then. One Ayah! Just one short Ayah! Rasul Allah(Salallahu alayhi wa aalihee wa sallam) did not give him a page long speech. Just one short sentence, and this is not just any poet! He is the BEST of the best poets of his tribe! And he is immediately converts. This is the experience of miracle. This is defeat! This is incapacitation! This is being overpowered!

He takes the SHAHADAH, returns back to his tribe and then narrates the entire story to them; which gets recorded in history and this is how we know about it.

### 3 Kuffar

There are three 3 infamous disbelievers: ABU JAHAL, ABU SUFIYAN and AKHNAS BIN SHURAIQ. These were the 3 leaders; the 3 elders of Quraish at that time. They were the think-tank. But they were also the greatest haters of Rasul Allah (Salallahu alayhi wa aalihee wa sallam). But you know what they would do? They would sneak in the middle of the night and put their ears on the walls of the prophets (PBUH) home, and listen to him all night reciting the Quran.
