And then in the morning they would sneak back to their homes. And so what happens is, that one night, they all run into each other. None of them knew that the other was there. So the first guys goes, What are you doing here? and he says what are you doing here? LOL

But they all knew what they were doing there, didn't they? So they swear they will never ever return! But then they all catch each other again the next night! Again they swear that they won't come back. They catch each other again the third night. Just imagine that! The helplessness of not being able to stop oneself from listening to the Quran. To swear and then break their oath 3 times in a row! Can you imagine how powerful this Quran must have been to them? SubhanAllah! Anyway..., so this time they swear by their mothers, their fathers their gods, their donkeys, their lives, that they will never come back again. And they don't come back!

But AKHNAS is curious. He goes to Abu Sufyan and he says to him, "We have been listening to the Quran for 3 days. What do you think? Is this the truth? ABU SUFIYAN says to him "Of course it's the truth! What else can it be?". OK! So let's talk to ABU JAHAL! He's been listening too right? So they both go to ABU JAHAL and they ask him, "What do you think?". "Of course it's the truth", he says! Wait a minute! ABU JAHAL says, "Ofcourse it's the truth"????  The greatest enemy of Islam, the greatest hater of Rasul Allah says it's the truth?? They're completely shocked! But then ABU JAHAL explains. He says, "You see..... we're Banu Aa'mir, and Muhammad is Banu Hashim!".

Right there! Before I tell you anymore, what did he take into consideration? The speech or the speaker? The speaker! The rejection of the disbeliever came at the fact that these words, as powerful as they are, as true as they are, as flawless as the content is, as mesmerizing as the style is, We are not willing to accept "this" person at any cost! Why? Because when Banu Hashim gives charity, we match them! When Banu Hashim recites poetry, we match them! When Banu Hashim  shows bravery in battle, we match them! But when one of them comes up with these words, we can NEVER match them! So they have won forever! and we cannot let that happen!".  This was the reason! This was the reason they rejected Rasul Allah(Salallahu alayhi wa aalihee wa sallam) and the Quran. Not because they didn't experience the miracle! They experienced it to the point that they could not keep themselves away from it. 3 nights they stand with their ears to the walls of the prophets home. They break their oaths 3 times in a row. So they didn't reject the Quran because they didn't experience its miracle. They rejected him because of tribal pride and arrogance! They rejected ISLAM not because of the content or the style, but because of the speaker.

SubhanAllah! It's a completely different take on history. Even those who hated the prophet (Salallahu alayhi wa aalihee wa sallam), were mesmerized by the Quran.

Last stroy

---

### Uthbah Ibn Rabeea'ah

Think of this guy as the "mafia boss" when it came to language. Expert debator! Very insulting to those who opposed him in public discourse! He was a negotiator on behalf of conflicting tribes. You can think of him as a consultant. He was hired for these kinds of jobs. When somebody needed to be destroyed by language, UTBAH was the go-to man. He would go in, make demands in such a language, that they would have no choice but to accept defeat. In other words, he was the guy to get the job done!

So these leaders of Quraish get together and say, "We're losing this war of words! There's none among us who can stand up to the speech of Muhammad! So it's time we bring out the big guns! We have someone who's really good at words! Someone really good at debates; at discussion and negotiation. We need to get him involved.

So they hire UTBAH. They say UTBAH! We want you to go to Muhammad (PBUH). He is sitting right there. You talk to him! Make some demands of him, figure out what he wants. Humiliate him! Destroy him! We'll watch from a distance.

You know how today we gather in groups to watch cricket or basketball games? This was their sport. They enjoyed watching such debates. So they're all excited about this match that's about to take place. They get the popcorn and the soda ready! I'm kidding... Probably they get their dates and olives ready.

Anyway! So UTBAH goes to the prophet; and in an exteremely rude, extermely condascending manner, he says...

⟪ar-quote:یا محمد! فَرَّقتَ دِینِنَا، وَ شَطَنتَ آلِھَتِنَا، وَ عَبدْتَ دِینِنِا، وَ فَرَّقتَ أِخوَانِنا⟫

Oh Muhammad! You've torn apart our religions; you've humiliated our gods; you've disgraced our religion, and you've separated brothers from brothers.

Now it's difficult for me to show you that from a linguistic perspective, how rude and condascending these words are to an Ancient Arab. From an Arab perspective, his tone was basically on the lines of, "What the hell is your problem? (نعوذباللہ) What's wrong with you? What the hell is it that you want from us?" This is the kind of tone these words translate to. He says...

⟪ar-quote:أِنَّما أِن کُنتَ تُرِیدُ بِہِ مُلکاً، مَلَّکناَ عَلی رُؤُسِنَا⟫

Is it authority that you desire? Fine! We make you our leader. We give you complete control of our posessions

⟪ar-quote:أِن کُنتَ تُرِیدُ بِہِ الشَّرَف، لا نَقطَعُ أَمراً دُونَک⟫

Is it honor that you want? Fine! We will not make a single move without your blessing and permission

⟪ar-quote:أِن کُنتَ تُرِیدُ بِہِ البآءَ، جَمَعنَا لَکَ نِساَءَ قُرَیشً فَخطَ أَیُّ نِساَءَ قُرَیشً فَنُزَوِّجْکَ عَشَرا⟫

Is it women that you desire? Fine! We'll stand before you all the women of Quraish! Any and every woman that you point to, we will give to you in marriage

⟪ar-quote:أِن کُنتَ تُرِیدُ بِہِ المال، جمعنا لک أَموَالَناَ حَتّٰی تَکُونُ أَغنٰی قُرِیشً مالا⟫

Is it wealth you desire? Fine we will put all the wealth of Quraish and put it before you. We will make you the richest man of Quraish

Tell us what you want? Make your demands!

He literally barks at the messenger like a dog! And Rasul Allah is listening to his hurtful and insulting words quietly; patiently. And when he's done, in a very soft tone, the messenger says to him.... ⟪ar-quote:أَفَرغْتَ یا ابا ولید؟⟫ Are you done?

UTBAH says, Fine! Your turn!

And righat at the moment Jibraeel comes to Rasul Allah(Salallahu alayhi wa aalihee wa sallam) with verses of the Quran, and he begins reciting the Ayats of Surah Fussilat.. He says

⟪ar-quote:بسم اللہ الرحمن الرحیم

حمٓ۔ تَنزِيلٌۭ مِّنَ ٱلرَّحْمَنِ ٱلرَّحِيمِ۔⟫

The first thing he says, and this is my rough translation. Of course I can't match what Allah says. The verses go...

In the name of Allah, the intensely merciful, the constantly merciful! HA MEEM! This message has been sent down by the exceedingly merciful, the constantly merciful.

You see, when the attack came from UTBAH, the accusation was, this is *your* message with a hidden agenda! And you're just trying to get smething out of it. The first thing Quran says in response is what? This is not the prophet's message. Where are they from? It's from Allah! You are not negotiating with my prophet! Who are you debating right now? You're debating Allah. You're not fighting the prophet, you're fighting Allah. I have sent down this message to my prophet

⟪ar-quote:‏كِتَبٌۭ فُصِّلَتْ آيَتُهُۥ قُرْآنًا عَرَبِيًّۭا لِّقَوْمٍۢ يَعْلَمُونَ۔⟫

It's a message, whose demands have been made absolutely clear in the Arabic language (your language)

Remember, UTBAH asked the prophet to make his demand? Allah, is responding to his demands. Allah says, I'll tell you what those demands are! And I'll tell you in plain Arabic, so all of you can clearly understand! You wanna know what my demands are? Here they are...

⟪ar-quote:‏بَشِيرًۭا وَنَذِيرًۭا فَأَعْرَضَ أَكْثَرُهُمْ فَهُمْ لَا يَسْمَعُونَ۔⟫

This Quran has 2 functions. Give good news; and a warning, a threat! But most of you ignore it on purpose. ⟪ar:اعراض⟫is to ignore something on purpose! Allah says, you are deliberately not listening to what I'm telling you. It's not that you don't understand! It's that you understand and still reject my message. So now Allah is revealing his demands to UTBAH, through the Ayat of the Quran. And as the ayats are being revealed, people are watching in the distance. And the prophet continues:

⟪ar-quote:وَقَالُوا۟ قُلُوبُنَا فِىٓ أَكِنَّةٍۢ مِّمَّا تَدْعُونَآ إِلَيْهِ وَفِىٓ آذَانِنَا وَقْرٌۭ ۔   وَمِنۢ بَيْنِنَا وَبَيْنِكَ حِجَابٌۭ ۔ فَٱعْمَلْ إِنَّنَا عَمِلُونَ۔ ‏

قُلْ إِنَّمَآ أَنَا۠ بَشَرٌۭ مِّثْلُكُمْ ۔  يُوحَىٰٓ إِلَىَّ أَنَّمَآ إِلَهُكُمْ إِلَهٌۭ وَحِدٌۭ ۔ فَٱسْتَقِيمُوٓا۟ إِلَيْهِ وَٱسْتَغْفِرُوهُ ۗ

وَيْلٌۭ لِّلْمُشْرِكِينَ ‏۔ ٱلَّذِينَ لَا يُؤْتُونَ ٱلزَّكَوٰةَ وَهُم بِٱلْآخِرَةِ هُمْ كَفِرُونَ۔ ‏إِنَّ ٱلَّذِينَ آمَنُوا۟ وَعَمِلُوا۟ ٱلصَّلِحَتِ لَهُمْ أَجْرٌ غَيْرُ مَمْنُونٍۢ۔

قُلْ أَئِنَّكُمْ لَتَكْفُرُونَ بِٱلَّذِى خَلَقَ ٱلْأَرْضَ فِى يَوْمَيْنِ وَتَجْعَلُونَ لَهُ أَندَادًۭا ۚ۔ ذَلِكَ رَبُّ ٱلْعَلَمِينَ۔⟫

Now as these ayats are being recited, people see that UTBA's expressions begin to change. He was comfortably and proudly sitting, and now his face is changing as Allah is presenting his demands. And then as the verses continue, they notice that he starts crying! UTBAH beings crying! Their expert negotiator, KAFIR, hater of Islam, insultor of Rasul Allah (PBUH), لعنۃ اللہ علیہ. He is listening to the Quran, and he begins crying. As the ayats go on, his emotions start more and more intense, and his crying becomes louder and louder. And the AYATS continue...

⟪ar-quote:‏وَجَعَلَ فِيهَا رَوَسِىَ مِن فَوْقِهَا وَبَرَكَ فِيهَا وَقَدَّرَ فِيهَآ أَقْوَتَهَا فِىٓ أَرْبَعَةِ أَيَّامٍۢ سَوَآءًۭ لِّلسَّآئِلِينَ۔

ثُمَّ ٱسْتَوَىٰٓ إِلَى ٱلسَّمَآءِ وَهِىَ دُخَانٌۭ فَقَالَ لَهَا وَلِلْأَرْضِ ٱئْتِيَا طَوْعًا أَوْ كَرْهًۭا قَالَتَآ أَتَيْنَا طَآئِعِينَ۔

‏فَقَضَىٰهُنَّ سَبْعَ سَمَوَاتٍۢ فِى يَوْمَيْنِ وَأَوْحَىٰ فِى كُلِّ سَمَآءٍ أَمْرَهَا ۚ وَزَيَّنَّا ٱلسَّمَآءَ ٱلدُّنْيَا بِمَصَبِيحَ وَحِفْظًۭا ۚ.....  ذَلِكَ تَقْدِيرُ ٱلْعَزِيزِ ٱلْعَلِيمِ۔⟫

⟪ar-quote:أَعْرَضُوا۟ فَقُلْ أَنذَرْتُكُمْ صَعِقَةًۭ مِّثْلَ صَعِقَةِ عَادٍۢ وَثَمُودَ⟫

So Allah begins telling him about himself! Of how he created the universe. And how everything in creation obeyed his command. He says I commanded the heaven and the earth to obey me willingly or unwillingly, and they both said, we come to you willingly oh great master! In other words, the heavens and the earth didn't refuse me, and you people dare to refuse and reject me? And so Allah goes on an on about his majesty, and then says...
⟪ar-quote:أَعْرَضُوا۟ فَقُلْ أَنذَرْتُكُمْ صَعِقَةًۭ مِّثْلَ صَعِقَةِ عَادٍۢ وَثَمُودَ⟫

And if they continue to ignore deliberately, then you tell them! Now who's you? Who is Allah talking to? Muhammad (PBUH). So just by the words he realizes, that he is not talking to Rasul Allah anymore; he is in direct conversation with Allah(Subhanhu Wa Ta'ala)  right now. And Allah is not even dignifying UTBAH. He is his messenger to tell him. Allah could have said ⟪ar-quote:أَنذَرْتُكُمْ⟫ I am warning you! But he said  ⟪ar-quote:فَقُلْ أَنذَرْتُكُمْ⟫ YOU warn them! Warn them of what? Explosions! ⟪ar-quote:صَعِقَةًۭ مِّثْلَ صَعِقَةِ عَادٍۢ وَثَمُودَ⟫ Just like the explosions that occurred with the tribes of Aa'd and Samud. And this was something that the Arabs knew about. They knew this had happened in the past. And now Utbah sitting there realizes, that he has been issued a direct threat from Allah himself. He was gets completely overpowered. You know what he does? He jumps forwards, and puts both his hands on the mouth of the prophet! and says! Stop! Please Stop! Please do not recite another word!

He then gets up and returns to the people who sent them. This expert debator, who they had hired to quiet the messenger of Allah; who was their last hope. When they see his face, they say, "The Utbah that is now returning, is not the one who left from here! This is not the face you went with". Utbah says, Whatever this man says will one day become an enormous event.  ⟪ar:سیکون نبأ عظیما⟫ he says!

I suggest you take him seriously, because you all know that Muhammad has never lies. And they say to him ⟪ar:سحَّرَک⟫He has done his magic on you too! UTBAH says, Believe what you will! But it's not magic! It is indeed the word of God,  but I'm not going to talk about this anymore and he leaves.

---

So I hope you can appreciate the incredible effect the style of this Quran had on these disbelievers. We cannot appreciate it because of our language handicap. But what we can at least appreciate the kind of effect it had upon these people who were masters of their language!

But at the same time, I also want to tell you, that sadly we are the ones who have handicapped ourselves when it comes to Quran. There's no reason why we can't learn the Quran in the context of Ancient Arabia. You kids learn all sorts of languages in school. Why not Arabic? And this is why I wanted to share these stories with you, because I wanted to show you a tragedy. The tragedy is that the disbelievers at the time of the prophet (Salallahu alayhi wa aalihee wa sallam); and the believers shared one thing. They had one thing in common. They were both over powered by what? The Quran! They were both overpowered by the Quran. But we as believers, as muslims and the momineen of this time, we have no affect on us when we listen to the Quran. It's a tragedy that we don't appreciate the power of the Quran. We are not stunned, or mesmerized, or overwhelmed by the words of Allah! And that's a shame! That's a real tragedy. This miraculous effect that Quran is capable of, is something that is completely lost in our time. And it's lost to the point, where poeple actually can criticise the Quran today. Why does it say this, why does it say that. Quran no longer speaks to our hearts, because we've completely given up on the effort of learning it.

<!-- section 6 (id=5784, raw_sort=6): Miracle - Order and Choice of words -->
We're trying to establish whether the Quran is human speech or divine speech. So far we've studied the word "miracle" in depth to understand what it means. To do a quick recap,  ⟪ar:معجزۃ⟫comes from the word ⟪ar:أعجاز⟫which means to incapacitate or overpower somone; to make someone incapable of a response; to bring someone down on his knees; to defeat someone conclusively - these are all meanings of the word ⟪ar:اعجاز⟫.  And in light of that definition, we've already seen some of the miraculous effects that this improptu, unscripted speech had, on the ancient arabs of the time.

We saw its effectiveness in the public sense - in the way it drastically influenced and changed the lives of people, in every single dimension of human behaviour. And in the previous session I showed you how people were profoundly affected by the incredible and mesmerizing style of this message at a very personal level. We saw that even the worst enemies of Rasul Allah(Salallahu alayhi wa aalihee wa sallam) - people like ABU JAHAL and ABU SUFIYAN could not keep themselves away from listening to the mesmerizing style of the Quran. They would spend all night with their ears against the wall of the prophet's home listening to the Quran. We saw how UTBAH IBN RABEEAH was completely overwhelmed and overpowered by the AYAATS of Surah Al-Fussilat; which came down in response to his questions. And how he was defeated to the point where he began crying, and then finally physically tried to stop the prophet from speaking, by putting both his hands on the prophet's mouth. We saw how TUFAIL IBN AMR - one of *the* greatest poet of that time, converted to ISLAM, after listening to just one statement from the prophet (Salallahu alayhi wa aalihee wa sallam), and converted instantly.

This is something I find incredible! The fact that these people converted on the spot. Because accepting a new religion is not a small thing. For things that are a lot less significant, we take a much longer time to first think about it. When we make purchases; when shopping, when buying clothes or furniture; when ordering at a restaurant, we take time to think! And why do we do that? To make sure we don't make the wrong decision. So it really amazes me, that what was it that these people heard in the Quran, that moved them so much, that they just had to convert instantly. Because, TUFAIL did not go back home to think about it! He didn't say, "Wait, you know what? this is pretty heavy stuff! Let me just take this back home and think about it! Let me go over it with the wife; discuss it with my tribe members. Let me make a pros and cons list! I'll get back to you with my decision next week. NO! He accepted ISLAM instantly! Because he saw the truth in that message! There was not a fraction of doubt left in his mind about this message being from God!

If someone gives me a million dollars, with no strings attached, I'm not going to think about it. I'll be like, "Thank Ya, See Ya!" before he gets a chance to change his mind, right? Or will I say, "Hmmm..... its not a bad offer; let me think about it; let me discuss it with my family; let me see if this is something I need in my life right now! Hell No! I'll take the money and split before the guy has a chance to change his mind! Why?  Because he just made me an offer I can't refuse. So what was it that these Arabs heard in these ayats, that made them an offer they simply could not refuse? That's what I'm going to begin showing today InshaAllah. And BTW, this was not one isolated event. There are hundreds upon hundreds of such narrations, where people heard the prophet speak and accepted ISLAM instantly.

Story of Christian priest converting to Islam

There was a Christian priest that comes to Rasul Allah, with the intention of debating him, and arguing with him on the topic of ISLAM. He wanted to prove to Rasul Allah (SA) that ISLAM cannot be the true religion of God, because obviously Christianity is the true religion of God. Now when a person comes with the intention to debate or argue, is he ever in the mood to listen? NO! A person never really listens to what is being said in a debate. Because the intention is never to understand and learn, right? The only goal of a debate is what? To crush the opponent; to humilate him. And so even if one does listen, the only reason for that is to come up with a counter argument. So if you say "The sky is blue",  I'll say "Well! not when it's sunset! Not when its midnight! Ha! Gotcah! You don't know what you're talking about! Why? Because I have only one goal in my mind - to prove you wrong! Isn't that true?

So this Christian priest comes to Rasul Allah (SA) with the intention of this debate on ISLAM, and he says: ⟪ar:یا محمد! ما الاسلام؟⟫Oh Muhammad! What is Islam? And Rasul Allah(Salallahu alayhi wa aalihee wa sallam) says:

⟪ar-quote:الاسلام..... طيب الكلام ؛ ⟪ar-quote:وَأَفْشُوا السَّلامَ⟫؛  و إطعام الطعام ؛  وَصَلُّوا بِاللَّيْلِ وَالنَّاسُ نِيَامٌ⟫

That's it! That's all he says! What is ISLAM? He says ⟪ar:الاسلامُ طيب الكلام⟫ ISLAM is beautiful speech; ⟪ar:وَأَفْشُوا السَّلامَ⟫  ISLAM is spreading peace and safety, ⟪ar:و إطعام الطعام⟫ ISLAM is feeding the needy and ⟪ar:وَصَلُّوا بِاللَّيْلِ وَالنَّاسُ نِيَامٌ⟫  ISLAM is praying in the night when the world is sleeping - in other words sincerity. He summarizes the entire essence, the entire beauty of ISLAM in 4 simple things. That's it! And the priest is dumb-founded. Because how do you ague with that? Who can argue against a religion that is a beautiful speech, that has the mission of peace and safety; that calls for the spirit of brotherhood - taking care of the needy; and that demands sincerity with God. It was everything that Christ taught as well! Except Rasul Allah(Salallahu alayhi wa aalihee wa sallam) condensed it into 4 simple things. How do you argue with that? All his arguments got defeated even before he could begin; and he recites the SHAHADAH right there! That is just INCREDIBLE!

And look what we've reduced ISLAM to in this day and age! It was described as something extremely beautiful by Rasul Allah(Salallahu alayhi wa aalihee wa sallam) and look what Mulsims have made it today. We've turned it into something ugly and despicable. ASTAGHFIRULLAH

---

So today I want to start taking a look at some specific examples from the Quran. In order to do that, let's first get ourselves into the mindset of the Ancient Arab. There was a criteria by which the ancient Arabs judged the eloquence of a speech. In fact, they had two criteria for eloquence.

[diagram: Diagram titled 'ELOQUENCE' with two boxes: PRECISE (accurately deliver intent) and CONCISE (as few words as possible). PRECISE branches downward to Order of words and Choice of words.]
  (see ../images/005.png)
  *Note:* Pedagogical: the two pillars of eloquence — precision and concision.

The first was that an eloquent speech must be "precise"; and second, that it should be "concise". Precise, meant that it should deliver the intent of the conversation completely; and "concise" meant it should be done using as few words as possible. That is how these people measured eloquence. Now think about this for a second. Is this an easy thing to do or a difficult thing to do? It's actually a very very difficult thing to do. Because if you and I want to be extremely clear, and precise, in conveying our thoughts; we need to use more and more words. Because we want to make sure nothing is left to the imagination, right? But to them, that was a big "no no". Their criteria for eloquence was: Use as few words as possible, and still be extremely precise. They actually liked their imaginations to be challenged. But when we leave things to the imagination, is there a chance that people can misunderstand? Of course! But not to them. Their criteria was challenge my imagination with as few words as possible, and at the same time be so precise in those words, that there is no way I can misunderstand you. Crazy right?

Now to top that off, within precision, they again had 2 more criteria. They judged precision in two ways:

Precision in the **order**of words - in how you structure and sequence the words in a sentence

Precision in the **choice**of words - what word you use to articulate your thought. If a better word exists than the one you used, then you just lost the battle of eloquence.

This is why, in ancient Arabic, for any given word, we find dozens of synonyms. In fact several dozens of synonyms; each with a slight difference in meaning. It's like a gradient. If you've every bought paint for your house, you must have seen these color swatches. In those swatches, for every single color, you'll find many many gradients; each with a slightly different shade, and with its on unique name right? Ancient Arabic is exactly the same way. Instead of a definition for a word, it has a variety of images, each having a slight variation in meaning of the original entity.

So if you just take, for example, a lion; there are over 300 words to describe a lion in ancient Arabic. And each word describes a very precise meaning about the lion. So when a lion is sitting in its den with its front legs folded, it is called ⟪ar:أسد⟫. But when it comes out of its den and begins walking around casually, it's called "**Zargham**". When it begins focusing on a prey; when it targets a prey for its hunt, its called **Ghazanfar**. When it roars to intimidate its prey, it is called **Zaigham**. When it pounces on its prey, with extreme precision, it is called **Hamza**. When it catches and takes control of its prey, such that the prey is now unable to escape its grip, it is called **Abbas**; and finally when it starts ripping through its prey, and begins to disintegrate it into pieces, it's called **Haider**. Over 300 words just to describe a lion - Imagine that!

⟪ar-quote:أسد ، زرغام ، غزنفر ، زِیغام ، ھمزا ، عباس ، حیدر

فارس ، غادی ، هَصْوَرَة ، قَصوَرَۃ ، دِرْغَام ، خَبُور ، شُجَاع⟫

Every single word, describes a different shade of meaning about the lion. And what was the point of having so many words to describe the same thing? Precision! This way when they used the word **Haider**, there was no ambiguity about what the lion is doing. It's ripping through its preying - taking care of business! So it is through these words they made their language extremely precise.

In fact, you know what the word ⟪ar:عرب⟫means linguistically? Do you remember the term these people used for non-Arabs? They called the person ⟪ar:عجم⟫. And what that word means in a general sense, is someone who is a mute, or dumb.

[diagram: Two side-by-side cards: left card on parchment background labelled 'BITE' with the Arabic word عَجَمَۃ; right card on blue background labelled 'CUT' with the Arabic word عَرَبَۃ.]
  (see ../images/006.png)
  *Arabic labels in image:* ⟪ar:عَجَمَۃ · عَرَبَۃ⟫
  *Note:* Etymology lesson contrasting 'ajama (foreign/inarticulate, 'biting' on words) with 'araba (Arab/clearly-speaking, 'cutting' clean syllables) — basis for understanding why Arabic is called clear/cutting speech.

But if you actually look at the words ⟪ar:عرب⟫and ⟪ar:عجم⟫linguistically, the word ⟪ar:عجم⟫, comes from ⟪ar:عَجَمَۃ⟫, which does not mean "dumb". It actually means "to bite". And the word Arab, comes from the verb ⟪ar:عَرَبَۃ⟫, which means to cut. So ⟪ar:عجمۃ⟫means to bite, and ⟪ar:عربَۃ⟫means to cut. Now what's the difference between biting and cutting? The difference is that biting is not precise, whereas cutting is extremely precise. Biting results in jagged or rough edges; Cutting results in clean and smooth edges. And this is why they considered non-Arabs ⟪ar:عجمی⟫because they were rough around the edges when it came to language. So embedded with the word ⟪ar:عرب⟫itself, we find the meaning of extreme precision, because ⟪ar:عربی⟫is an extremely precise language, and in comparison to it every other language becomes ambiguous.

There are 8 words the ancient arabs used just for sleeping.

⟪ar-quote:نوم، سُبات، سکون، رقاد، کری، ھجوع، ضجع⟫

And they all mean different things. One is deep sleep; one is half asleep; one is for when your eyes are open but your mind is sleeping; one is for when you're sleeping but you can still hear people; one is is sleep when you're not lying down flat; one is for sleep with a dream in it, one is for sleep without a dream in it.

And this is something that the ancient Arab's ears were very attuned to when they heard people talk. If a word was placed in the wrong order, or if a better word could have been used, they would immediately notice it. Because in Arabic there is a word for every emotion, and every intensity of that emotion. Now the Quran comes to these people. I want you think about something. For a message to impress these people, shouldn't it have even more words for the same thing to describe something? Shouldn't it have new words that the Arabs never heard before?

You know how sometimes we listen to someone speak and they use words, like they just swollowed dictiionary for lunch? And we hear them speak and say, "Dude! That is so insanely profound what you just said! I have absolutely no clue what you just said to me, but it's so AWESOME!." So I would imagine the Quran would be something like that, right? Use tons of highly sophisticated words! Do you know how many words there are in the Quran in total? There are over 77,000 words in the Quran in total. Do you know how many unique words there are in the Quran based on tri-literal roots? Only 1600 words. That's it! All 77,000 words come from the same 1600 root words, and within those limited amount of words, it structures its AYATS with surgical precision.

Now let's come back to the idea of Quran being an unscripted oral tradition, and not a written one. See! It's very easey to judge and find flaws in an oral speech. You know why? because you have time process the information. Right now when I'm speaking to you, it's easy for you to detect the flaws in my speech, because you're not actively speaking, you're passively listening; so you get time to think about it. He said that word, he should have used that word instead! He said "hearing", he should have used "listening". That sentence was grammatically wrong! He didn't pronounce that word correctly. You can do this while you're listening, but I cannot do that as I'm speaking. Why? Because we as human beings, we cannot organize our "words" as we're speaking. Because when we're speaking, we're busy organizing our "thoughts", and the words just come out of us to articulate that thought. Our focus is thought not words, Isn't that true? This is why when we have to prepare a speech, we have to write it down first. Think about what you do when you have to write a speech, or submit a paper for school. You put down your thoughts on paper first, and then you go over it, again and again, and you organize your words. You rephrase your sentences; you remove redundancies; you look up better substitues for your words in a thesaurus. In other words, through this editorial process, you try to make your words precise. You strive for precision in the "order" of words, and in the "choice" of words - this is how you make your written speech eloquent. And we can do this in writing, but we cannot do this as we're speaking. Do you understand? And so this became the goal of the ancient Arab. To get this kind of precision and perfection in speech.

Now the Quran is revealed to them as an oral tradition. The WAHEE would come on Rasool Allah (Salallahu alayhi wa aalihee wa sallam), and he would immediately begin reciting these AYAATS in a flow. One AYAH after another until the entire passage was delivered. It's not like he would wait for the entire WAHEE to come upon him, then ask for a piece of paper; put his thoughts down, then organize his words, revise the material over and over again to make sure it's eloquent and the right words have been used, and then deliver that message to the people right? Historically, we find absolutely no evidence of any kind of an editorial process. He would just speak! And he would deliver entire passages of the Quran, not just one single sentence. And there was not even a scheduled time for revelation. Quran would get revealed any time during the day; under all sorts of emotions. So to be precise in the order of words, and the choice of words, for any human being in that position is absolutely impossible.  And then, once he spoke the AYAH, it's set in stone. Have you ever heard that he revealed an AYAH and then changed it? Did he ever say, You know what? that didn't sound right! Let me change that. Or that's not exactly what I meant to say, scratch that! Oh I could have said that one better, let me try again. No! We see none of that. Not one single instance where he ever said that. 23 years of Quranic revelation, without any kind of editorial process, and where the prophet never revokes an AYAH, unless Allah Himself revokes it by another AYAH! 23 years! We cannot do this for 23 minutes!

So now with that background in mind, I want you to look at these AYATS with me.

---

Precision in order of words

> ⟪ar:وَلَا تَقْتُلُوا أَوْلَدَكُم مِّنْ إِمْلَقٍ ۖ نَّحْنُ نَرْزُقُكُمْ وَإِيَّاهُمْ
وَلَا تَقْتُلُوا أَوْلَدَكُمْ خَشْيَةَ إِمْلَقٍ ۖ نَّحْنُ نَرْزُقُهُمْ وَإِيَّاكُمْ⟫
> *(6:151) Do not kill your children because of poverty — we provide for you all (parents) and them (children)
(17:31) Do not kill your children out of fear of poverty — we provide for them (children) and you all (parents)*
> — **Quran 6:151** *(from image; see _provenance.json for validation)*
  (image preserved at ../images/007.png)
  *Note:* Quran 6:151 vs 17:31 — classical exemplar of Quranic precision: when poverty is present (6:151) parents are mentioned first; when fear of future poverty is anticipated (17:31) children are mentioned first. Citation marks both verses.

In the days of ignorance, (⟪ar:دور جاھلیۃ⟫), and actually even today, parents would to kill their unborn children because of poverty. They didn't have enough food to feed themselves, and therefore could not afford to feed an additional mouth, so they would kill their children because of poverty. In both these ayaats, Allah talks to such parents, and commands them not to kill their children because of poverty, with a subtle difference...

In the first ayat He say: Do not kill your children **because**of poverty, we provide you all (parents) and them (children)

In the second ayat He say: Do not kill your children out of fear of poverty, we provide them (children) and you all (parents)

In the first ayah, who does Allah talk about providing first? Parents! And then who? children

In the second ayah, who does Allah talk about providing first? Children! And then about who? parents

Now what difference does it make right? parents first, children later, or children first, parents later. Isn't it the same thing? Now let's see why that is...

When Allah says, Do not kill your children because of poverty, does poverty already exist? Yes, it does! They don't have enough food to feed themselves, that's why they're killing the children. Cause they're worried about their own survival. So Allah addresses the parents first. He says to them, don't kill your children because of your present state. I will provide you first, and then I will also provide for your children.

In the second ayah, Allah talks about the "fear" of poverty! Does fear exist in the present or in the future? In the future! This means that the parents have their provision for the now, what they're worried about is the what? future! And who's going to join the family in the future? Children! So when he talks about "fear" of poverty, future provisions, related to future children, he talks about children first and then the parents. He says don't be fearful; or don't worry about the children that are coming in the future, we will provide them and not just them, but you as well. SubhanAllah!!!

Do you see how the words that are about to be said in the future, have an influence on how words are organized in the beginning, even before they are delivered. As humans, we do not have that ability when we speak. Because we can only organize our thoughts, not our words. To us, "I worked really hard",  and "I really worked hard", are the same thing. There is no difference. And these verses were not revealed in isolation. They were revealed as part of a passage, in one single extemporaneous flow. How do you organize words with this precision as you're speaking? It's impossible! Even when we write, we can't always be this sensitive! But Quran was not revealed as a written word; it was revealed as a spoken word! These AYATS had no editorial process, and yet we find this amazing perfection in the way words are organized in relation to what's coming ahead in the sentence. And this kind perfection, this kind of precision, exists consistently all across the Quran.

And the ancient Arabs noticed this precision as soon as they heard it, and they realized, that as human beings are simply not capable of this kind of perfection in oral speech; and this is where they experienced their miracle.

Let's look at another one...

---

> ⟪ar:قُلْ كَفَىٰ بِاللَّهِ شَهِيدًا بَيْنِي وَبَيْنَكُمْ ۚ إِنَّهُ كَانَ بِعِبَادِهِ خَبِيرًا بَصِيرًا
قُلْ كَفَىٰ بِاللَّهِ شَهِيدًا بَيْنِي وَبَيْنَكُمْ ۖ يَعْلَمُ مَا فِى السَّمَوَتِ وَالْأَرْضِ ۗ وَالَّذِينَ ءَامَنُوا بِالْبَطِلِ وَكَفَرُوا بِاللَّهِ أُولَئِكَ هُمُ الْخَسِرُونَ⟫
> *(17:96) Allah is enough as a witness between me and you / Allah has complete knowledge of his slaves
(29:52) Allah is enough between me and you as a witness / He knows what is in the heavens and earth. And they who have believed in falsehood and disbelieved in Allah - it is those who are the losers.*
> — **Quran 17:96** *(from image; see _provenance.json for validation)*
  (image preserved at ../images/008.png)
  *Note:* Quran 17:96 and 29:52 compared — classic exemplar of Quranic word-order precision. Citation marks 17:96 primarily.

The word  ⟪ar-quote:شَهِيدًۭا⟫! means "witness"! And it is also one of the 99 attributes of Allah. So keep that in mind. Now let's go over the red part first.

The first ayah says,
⟪ar-quote:قُلْ كَفَىٰ بِٱللَّهِ شَهِيدًۢا بَيْنِى وَبَيْنَكُمْ⟫

Say: "Allah is enough as a witness between me and you". Who is saying this AYAH? Rasul Allah! So the "ME" refers to who? RasulAllah and "YOU" refers to "us" or whoever is listening it. You understand?

In the second ayah, the red part says,
⟪ar-quote:قُلْ كَفَىٰ بِٱللَّهِ بَيْنِى وَبَيْنَكُمْ شَهِيدًۭا⟫

Say: Allah is enough between me and you as a witness. Again "ME" refers to Rasul Allah and "YOU" refers to us. Correct?

So the placement of which word is different in the two verses (Just the red parts). The word SHAHEEDAN.  If you take out this word, both ayahs would read the same, correct? So in the first AYAH, Rasul Allah uses the word SHAHEEDAN first, and then say "Me and You", but in the second ayah he says "Me and You" first and then uses the word "SHAHEEDAN".  Is that clear to everyone?

Now what difference does it make? They both mean the same thing right?

The thing is Quran is hyper-sensitive; it is super-sensitive to context. When Rasul Allah spoke, he organized the words like a beautiful architecture. You cannot move a single brick from its place, or its perfection will be lost forever. Now I want you to examine the latter part of these AYATS. The text after the red part.....

You'll see that in the first ayah Allah ends the AYAH by talking about himself. He says ⟪ar:إِنَّهُ كَانَ بِعِبَادِهِ خَبِيرًۢا بَصِيرًۭا⟫ . INNAHOO refers to Allah himself. He says Allah has complete knowledge of his slaves! Who has complete knowledge of his slaves? Allah!

But now if you look at the latter part of the second ayah, he ends the verse by talking about people⟪ar:أُو۟لَٓئِكَ هُمُ ٱلْخَسِرُونَ⟫.  He knows what is in the heavens and earth. And those who believed in falsehood and disbelieved in Allah - they are the losers. Who are the losers? the people.

So the first ayah ends by talking about Allah, and the second ayah ends by talking about people. And remember that SHAHEEDAN is an attribute of Allah(Subhanhu Wa Ta'ala). So the AYAH that ends by talking about Allah, Rasul Allah uses the attribute "SHAHEEDAN" first, and then refers to people. But in the second ayah that ends talking about people, Rasul ALlah refers to the people first and then uses Allah's attribute SHAHEEDAN! Subhan Allah!!!

Words that are about to be said in the future, have an influence on how words are organized in the beginning of the sentence. How do you do this in verbal speech? This kind of perfection is absolutely impossible to do in unscripted speech. Because we never get enough time to organize our words with this kind of precision, for something that we are going to say later in the conversation - with this surgical precision. And the entire Quran is filled with this kind of precision.

---

Precision in CHOICE of words

Now let's look at the precision in the CHOICE of words in a different ayah. We all know the difference between past tense and present tense. The Quran uses all three tenses. It uses the past tense, the present tense and of course the future tense. When I say "KILLED", which tense is that? When I say "KILLS" what tense is that? In Surah Nisa, in two consecutive AYATS, Allah says

4:92

⟪ar-quote:وَمَن قَتَلَ مُؤْمِنًا خَطَـًۭٔا فَتَحْرِيرُ رَقَبَةٍۢ مُّؤْمِنَةٍۢ وَدِيَةٌۭ مُّسَلَّمَةٌ إِلَىٰٓ أَهْلِهِ⟫

And whoever ****killed****a believer by mistake, then he should free another muslim as recompense and pay the blood money to the relatives of the deceased. Is "Killed" past tense or present tense? It is past tense. So **past tense** is used with mistake

4:93

⟪ar-quote:وَمَن يَقْتُلْ مُؤْمِنًۭا مُّتَعَمِّدًۭا فَجَزَآؤُهُۥ جَهَنَّمُ خَلِدًۭا فِيهَا⟫

And whoever ****kills****a believer on purpose, his recompense is hell fire. He will live in it forever. Is "Kills" past tense or present tense? It's present  tense. And so we see here that **present tense** is associated with intent, or deliberation. Past tense is associated with mistake and Present tense is associated with intent. You see that?

Now note that this is in the same passage (verses 92 and 93 from the same SURAH). You would think that Allah would stick to the same tense. After all what difference does it make?

⟪ar-quote:وَمَن قَتَلَ مُؤْمِنًا خَطَـًۭٔا

⟪ar-quote:وَمَن قَتَلَ مُؤْمِنًا ⟪ar-quote:مُّتَعَمِّدًۭا⟫⟫⟫

And whoever **killed**by mistake; and whoever **killed**on purpose. Same thing! But No! When he mentioned killing by mistake he uses the past tense, and when he mentions killing on purpose, he uses the present tense. You know why? Because the past tense only happened once.

I WENT to the seminar in NYC. What does that mean? One time!

I GO to the Microsoft Conference in NY. What does that mean? I go every year

So here in the first ayah, Allah talks about a man who killed by mistake and used the past tense. How many times do you kill by mistake? Just once! you only commit murder once. The second time you kill and say "Oh Mistake again" then.

In the second AYAH, Allah talks about some who kills with intent and uses present tense. He says, the the one who kills on purpose is a perpetrator, and he should be punished, because chances are what? he'll do it again, hence the present tense; hence the continuity. Past tense with murder because it is accidental, it does not have continuity. Present tense with murder, because it is on purpose, it has continuity. SubhanAllah!!

Quran is precise and perfect even in the tenses it uses. Not just the choice of words, not just the sequence of words, but even in the tenses of the words there is this such hyper sensitivity. And this is verbal speech. SubhanAllah!

---

The Arabic language has actually two words for giving counsel. The first word is ⟪ar:وَصَّی⟫;  and the other word is ⟪ar:أَوصا⟫.  You don't have to remember that  vocabulary. وَصَّی is when you give counsel that is of a spiritual nature, or when you give it over and over again. In Arabic, the only nuance to ⟪ar:وَصَّی -⟫ this council that is given over and over again, is ⟪ar:أَوصا⟫, which is a council that is given only one time.  I'll repeat that again. ⟪ar:وَصَّی⟫ - over and over again; ⟪ar:أَوصا -⟫one time. 

Remarkably in the quran, counsel is talked about several times. And if you take tally of all those times, where its mentioned like in BAQARAA, SHURA, NISAA, MARIAM, all these different places where counsel is talked about, every time Allah talks about "spiritual" counsel; counsel to do good, counsel to worship Allah, counsel to pray, he consistently uses the word ⟪ar:وَصَّی⟫, which is actually the word used for over and over again. And every time counsel is of a financial nature, like for example inheritance. Inheritance is called ⟪ar:وَصِیَّۃ⟫in Arabic and is also used in Urdu. Because ⟪ar:وَصِیَّۃ⟫- is the counsel that the deceased left regarding how his money should be distributed. In such cases Allah uses the word ⟪ar:أَوصا⟫.

So for spiritual matters he uses the word ⟪ar:وَصَّی⟫and for financial matters like that of inheritance he uses the word ⟪ar:أَوصا⟫, which is beautiful, because think about it! How many times will inheritance be distributed? One time. It's a one-time thing! So ⟪ar:أَوصا⟫is a better word to capture the one-time nature of inheritance; for that kind of counsel. However when it comes to spiritual counsel, to be mindful of Allah; to be truthful; to  be kind, to pray, this is not the kind of counsel you give somebody once. You have to give it over and over and over again. That's the nature of spiritual counsel. It must be repeated. So the Quran very beautifully and consistent in using the word ⟪ar:وَصَّی⟫every single time۔

Now think about this. In the Arabic language the word ⟪ar:وَصَّی⟫and ⟪ar:أَوصا⟫are interchangeable with a subtlety; one is repeated, the other is not. But the Quran is very precise about where it uses each one, with one amazing exception! EISA AS is born, and the Quran has a very unique narrative about the birth of EISA that the Bible doesn't have; That he spoke the day he was born. And as part of his speech he says:
⟪ar-quote:وَأَوْصَنِى بِٱلصَّلَوٰةِ وَٱلزَّكَوٰةِ مَا دُمْتُ حَيًّۭا⟫

Allah counseled me to pray and to give charity so long as I'm alive. Except the word he used for counsel this time is the word that Quran typically uses for financial matters. Why? This is a spiritual counsel - to pray, to give charity. Remember I told you that ⟪ar:أَوصا⟫is for one time, and ⟪ar:وَصَّی⟫is for over and over again? When EISA AS is speaking in this narrative how old is he? He's one day old. He couldn't have possibly been given counsel over and over again. He has only been given counsel to pray and give charity one time. So he says ⟪ar:أَوْصَنِى⟫.

23 years of an oral revelation, and the only time the pattern is broken is when the one-time advice is given. This is incredible precision for oral speech. Human beings can't be this consistent in their speech for a period of 23 years, where everytime the repeating spiritual consel is used one uses the word ⟪ar:وَصَّی⟫, and everytime the one-time financial counsel is used, one uses the word ⟪ar:أَوصا⟫, except the one time, when it is not possible to use the word.

---

They have so many words just to describe a farmer. A word for when he's planting the seed. a word when has planted the seed, A word when he's taking out the seed, when he's watering the plant. And all those words are used, just to say farmer.
⟪ar-quote:مزارع، کافر، فلاح، ملتزم⟫

All these words mean farmer... Yes a farmer is called "Kaafir" in Arabic because he hides the seed in the ground.. A seed was apparent, visible to the eye, but the farmer hides it in the ground.... just like a disbeliever hides the truth even though it's apparent... So the word for disbeliever (Kaafir) is actually the word used for "farmer."

When I'm speaking in a flow, I don't have enough time to process the next sentence that's coming out of my mouth. I don't have time to analyze my choice of words; the placement of my words. I can't do that. If I tried to do that I'll have to pause before each sentence, organize my words, and then speak. But I can't do all of that as I'm speaking, you understand? This is a human limitation.

Now the Quran is revealed to these Arabs, and one of the things that becomes miraculous to them, is the surgical precision in the choice of words and their placement within every single sentence. The prophet is speaking extemporaneously, without any planning or preparation; but the words he is choosing and the way he is structuring them within a sentence is just not humanly possible. So to them, even the most ordinary statements turn into miracles, just by the way in which it is being delivered to them - consistently. Because the Quran is extremely consistent in its choice of words. It's not like this order exists in just some AYATS. The more you study this book, the more consistency you find in it.

E.g. of Eisa AS

---

It's because when you and I speak, we organize our thoughts. When I came to this session, I organized my thoughts before hand. I said first I'm going to talk about this, then I'm going to talk about this and then I'm going to talk about that. I even have these points written before me. But you and I are incapable of organizing our words based on what we're going to say later.

<!-- section 7 (id=5788, raw_sort=7): Miracle of Conciseness -->
In the previous session, we looked at the criteria by which the ancient Arabs measured the eloquence of a speech. To them, eloquent speech meant two things: Speech must be "precise" and it must be "concise". They had this saying:

⟪ar-quote:الخیر الکلام مَن قَلَّ وَ دَلَّ⟫

The best speech is that, which is short and to-the-point.

So the first criterion was "precision", which meant two things: Precision in the "order or sequence of words", and precision in the "choice of words". The second criterion was that speech had to be concise; it had to be delivered using as few words as possible. So the idea was to challenge the imagination, using as few words as possible, while being extremely precise in the order and choice of those words; which is an extremely difficult thing to do. And the ancient Arabs were able to do this in writing, when they had their poetry slams, but they struglled to do this in conversations. And this is where the Quran  becomes a miracle to these people by its *style*. Because it comes to them as an unscripted speech, in their own language, demonstrating the kind of "precision and conciseness" that was beyond human capabilities. And they are defeated by it. They are incapacitated; they are rendered incapable of a response. And so their hearts and intellects are forced to believe that this cannot be the speech of a human being.

A miracle, once again, is something that incapacitates, or renders one incapable of a response. I keep repeating this definition of miracle because we need to move away from this visual concept of miracles that we have in our minds. Because Quran is not a miracle for the eyes; it is a miracle for the ears. Its an audible miracle, not a visual one.

In the previous session we looked at a few examples of precision in the order and choice of words. Today we're going to look at an example related to the miracle of conciseness in the Quran. Let me first give you the context of what concicse speech sounded like to the Ancient Arab. I explained to you earlier how these ancient Arabs developed this immense power of articulation through poetry. They didn't have any natural sceneries to enjoy; so they harnessed the power of language to paint these beautiful sceneries using picturesque words that were full of imagery. They would speak in riddles to challenge their imaginations.

To give you an example, there is this poet, who's penniless, and he's writing poetry about how generous he is, and how much he gives in charity. So his wife comes to him and says, Are you nuts? We don't even have food to feed ourselves; our children are starving, what are you talking about? We're bankrupt! and you're making poetry about how generous you are!? What's wrong with you? So he turns to her, and responds to her in poetry by saying:
⟪ar-quote:السَّیلُ حَربٌ عَلی مَکانٍ عَالِی⟫

Heavy rain does not get along with a house on top of a hill.

Now if he said that to us. We'd be like.... "say what?!!". What has rain on a house on top of a hill got to do with being charitable, or being generous, right? But do you know what he was talking about?

I want you to imagine this scene. There is a house on top of a steep hill, and there's heavy rain pouring down from the sky. When it rains, does the water stay on top of the hill? No! It flows down to the bottom of the hill, right? So he says, RIZQ, or provision comes from the sky. And there are two kinds of people in the world. The lofty ones and the lowly ones. People that are elevated and closer to God; and those that are low and worldly; people at the ground level. Now if your house is on top of the hill, aren't you closer to the sky? In other words, closer to God? So just like the water doesn't stay with a house at the top of a hill, and flows down to the earth; I am so generous that I don't keep any provisions for myself, I keep giving it to the lowly people. Because where does the water accumulate? Where does it create a puddle? On the ground! So I give all my provisions to these other people making *them* rich, because they're the debased ones on the ground, and I'm the noble one. This is how generous I am!! And he says all of this by saying what?
⟪ar-quote:السَّیلُ حَربٌ عَلی مَکانِ العَالِی⟫

Heavy rain does not get along with a house on top of a hill. 5 words! So this is what "concise" sounded like to them. They liked to hear the ocean in a shell! So this is how they spoke in these riddles. They loved challenging the imagination. They would never t just say what they really wanted to say.

***We married men can appreciate this, because of our wives, right? They have this ancient arab mentality LOL. They love to challenge our imaginations by never saying what they want to say. LOL.

Actually I shouldn't be making wife jokes. Women are in majority in this group, I'll get beaten up!***

Anyway, so you get the idea! This is how these guys spoke in riddles. And if you didn't get it, they would say... hah! ⟪ar:عجم⟫(mute - Al-Idiot)!!! But this was the kind of sensitivity to language, that these people enjoyed.

---

With this understanding of what concise sounded like to them, Today I want to present the 7 opening AYATS of Surah Al-MURSALAAT, as a miracle in the dimension of concise speech. A dimension in which impromtu speech literally rocks the imagination, with as few words as possible. But before we look at the verses, let's first understand the context and the background in which these AYATS were actually revealed.

You see! the Arabs of Quraish constantly contended and argued with Rasul Allah(Salallahu alayhi wa aalihee wa sallam) over the idea of an after life. They said, you keep talking to us about the sun and the moon colliding. You keep telling us about the mountains "moving swiftly" as if they were made of wool. You tell us people will be so scared on that day, that they will appear drunk out of fear. You tell us that the oceans are going to boil over. You keep warning us of these huge "cataclismic events" that are going to take place. We don't believe you! None of this is going to happen!! When is all this going to happen? None of this makes any sense to us! None of it is possible!

So they constantly disputed the threats of the Quran, saying they're just too cataclismic. They're too enormous to be possible. So in essence they made 3 arguments.

1. We don't need God for anything. We are the ones in control!

2. There is no purpose to creation. It is is just a random event

3. There is no hereafter or rising from the dead
⟪ar-quote:وَقَالُوٓا۟ إِنْ هِىَ إِلَّا حَيَاتُنَا ٱلدُّنْيَا وَمَا نَحْنُ بِمَبْعُوثِينَ⟫
They said, surely there is no life after this world, and we shall never be resurrected. Which means there is no reward or punishment.

Everything you're saying is simply nonsense! It's the crazy talk of a mad man (نعوذ باللہ). OK?

So these were their 3 arguments. I want you to keep these arguments in the back of your minds. Because Surah MURSALAAT is is revealed in rsponse to these arguments. And it begins by Allah(Azza Wa Jal) taking a few oaths.

**https://quran.com/77/1-7**

The SURAH, which is the 77th Surah of the Quran begins with the words:

⟪ar-quote:وَٱلْمُرْسَلَتِ عُرْفًۭا ‎⟫

The word ⟪ar:مرسلۃ⟫linguistically means, "that which has been released", or "that which has been sent". So Allah says: ⟪ar:وَٱلْمُرْسَلَتِ عُرْفًۭا ‎⟫, I swear by that which is released! What is he talking about? He's talking about the winds! The word ⟪ar:رُسُل⟫in Arabic is also used to describe a very fast horse. A horse that moves like the wind۔ The word ⟪ar:رسول⟫also describe a messenger; the one who is sent with a very powerful message. Angels are also described by the word ⟪ar:رسول⟫. So there are all these linguistic shades of meaning embedded in the word ⟪ar:مُرسَل⟫.

And so Allah(Subhanhu Wa Ta'ala), begins by taking an oath, or swearing by these winds. When do we take an oath? When do we swear by something? When we are not being believed! right? No I swear! I'm telling you the truth! I didn't push him down the stairs! I swear by his hamster! LOL! So one of the reasons we swear, is when we are not being believed! Now what is the context of revelation of these AYATS? Allah is not being believed! They are mocking his messenger about the existence of Allah, and the day of judgment. So Allah begins with an oath:⟪ar:وَٱلْمُرْسَلَتِ عُرْفًۭا⟫

The word ⟪ar:عُرف⟫in Arabic refers to the hair on the back of the neck of a wild horse. If you don't have reins, or ropes on a horse, what is the only thing you can use to slow it down? The hair on the back of its neck. So Allah gives the image of winds as though they are like these wild horses, that have been unleashed because its hair has been let go. Now what happens when you let go of the hair of a wild horse? It goes crazy! It goes out of control! It marches forward; full speed ahead. So what's being paralleled here is the image of a wild horse with winds. Meaning Allah(Subhanhu Wa Ta'ala) is telling the people of Quraish, that the winds are not something that randomly blow this way or that way. The reason you're feeling that soft breeze on your face, is because it's reigns are being held. Held by who? By Allah (AWJ)! But it is very easy for him to let go of that lock of hair. And if he let's go, what's going to happen? They're going to turn into this wild horse - this stallion which is going to crush through anything in its path. What happens when a hurricane decides to takes a stroll through a city? It destroys anything and everything in its path, right? So the first thing Allah is swearing by is the winds that have the potential to destroy when its reigns are let go. All of this imagery and an incredible warning is being delivered in just two words: ⟪ar:وَٱلْمُرْسَلَتِ عُرْفًۭا⟫

Then he says...

⟪ar-quote:‏فَٱلْعَصِفَتِ عَصْفًۭا ‎⟫

The word ⟪ar:عَصف⟫in Arabic is to move in an inconsiderate fashion. To move without a care for what comes in its path. So for exmaple, if the brakes of a truck, or a buldozer fail, they will just crush anything and everything that comes in its path. They're not going to care! They will just keep moving forward. So careless, inconsiderate movement is called ⟪ar:عصف⟫ in Arabic.

***Interestingly my name عاصف comes from the same root word! I'm going to have a word with my dad after this call! Thanks dad! I love you too!***

Anyway, so Allah continues with another oath: ⟪ar:‏فَٱلْعَصِفَتِ عَصْفًۭا ‎⟫. And I swear by the winds that when they get unleashed, they become violent; they become inconsiderate; they become ruthless. They don't care what's going to come in their way. They will just destroy as they move along.

So we see that in these first 2 AYATS, Allah swears by the potential power of destruction within these gentle winds. A few years ago there was a hurricane called "Katrina" in the US. If you look up the video of what it did in just 40 seconds! the destruction it caused! you'll have an idea of the power of these winds. In another place in the Quran Allah(Subhanhu Wa Ta'ala) actually talks about such winds that were unleased upon a nation of rebels, for 7 consecutive days.

⟪ar-quote:سَخَّرَهَا عَلَيْهِمْ سَبْعَ لَيَالٍۢ وَثَمَنِيَةَ أَيَّامٍ حُسُومًۭا فَتَرَى ٱلْقَوْمَ فِيهَا صَرْعَىٰ ؛ كَأَنَّهُمْ أَعْجَازُ نَخْلٍ خَاوِيَةٍۢ⟫

We sent them winds for 7 nights and 8 days continuously (⟪ar:حُسُومًۭا⟫) , continuously pounding them. 7 nights and 8 days! We turned their skulls into seedless dates. AllahuAkbar! Such powerful words!!!

Can you imagine the destruction it must have caused? If 40 seconds can do so much, what kind of destruction 7 consecutive days would have done?!

Now the wind is not some cataclysmic event, like the sun and moon coming together; or the sun increasing it's gravity pull. Its not a special event that needs to be prepared for. You know how we see in movies that special arragments are made for weapons of mass destruction. So many scientiest; So much money, resources; so much time goes into developing one such weapon. Isn't that true? What did Allah use to destroy these people? Just the wind! And the Quraish knew about this incident. So In other words, Allah is telling them, that I don't need to make any special arrangements to destroy you guys. All I need to do is release my hold on the lock of the winds, and they will do it for me. That's all I need to do. That's how weak you are! And this is how powerful I am! SubhanAllah!

But then, after describing the winds as the source of death and destruction, he immediately turns around and gives the aspect of winds. , he says...

⟪ar-quote:‏وَٱلنَّشِرَتِ نَشْرًۭا ‎⟫

And the winds that serve to spread. ⟪ar:نَشَرَ⟫is litereally when you take a bunch of seeds in your hand, and just fling it into the air, dispersing them on the ground. So Allah swears by the winds, that he uses to spread and disperse the clouds all over the world. Because what do clouds bring us? Rain! And rain is the source of life on this earth. No rain means no life! A drought brings death! So the same wind, that was the source of death and destruction in the first 2 AYAATS, they are now being described as a source of life in this third ayat. SubhanAllah!

And today we know even better! Winds don't just carry clouds around. What else do they carry? Pollen! The source of all vegetation. Pollen travels from one place to another through what? winds! Those of you who have bad allergies know that too well unfortunately. So these winds are actually a mercy of Allah. That's why we are reminded to say AlHamdulillah when we sneeze! Why does one sneeze? Because of a foreign particle is irritating the inside of the nose. How did the particle get there? Through breadth! What does one take in through breadthing? Air! Where did the air come from? Winds! And when we sneeze what pushes that foreign particule out? Our breadth, which is also a kind of forceful wind. SubhanAllah!

So Allah again swears by the winds that are also used to spreads these clouds around. Now when you think of Allah spreading these clouds through winds, you may think that it's all random! That the winds are in control. Science calls these, "the random acts of mother nature". But as Muslims we know there is no such thing as a random event. These are very precise, very calculated acts of Allah (AWJ). Then he says...

⟪ar-quote:‏فَٱلْفٰرِقٰتِ فَرْقًۭا ‎⟫

And I swears by those who make very precise decisions. Both words ⟪ar:فارقات⟫and ⟪ar:فرقاً⟫come from the same root word ⟪ar:فرق⟫, which we also use in Urdu. It means to "make different or distinct". It also means to separate two things clearly. So Allah is saying, I choose and decree where these clouds will reach and where they won't. I decide that water will fall here, and not there; this land will remain dry, and this land will get water. ⟪ar:‏فَٱلْفَرِقَتِ فَرْقًۭا ‎⟫.

So far, using just 8 concise words, with surgical precision, in choice and order of words, the Quraish are being warned through the same example of winds. They're told that these winds can bring death; and these same winds can bring life. I control which brings which, not you! And so Allah so he swears by these winds to enforce this idea, that "I'm the one in control! Not you!". SubhanAllah!

Then he says...

⟪ar-quote:‏فَٱلْمُلْقِيَتِ ذِكْرًا ‎⟫

These winds, they bring people in contact with reminders! ⟪ar:مُلْقِيَتِ⟫comes from the root word ⟪ar:لقی⟫which means to "meet someone" or "come in contact with someone". So Allah says, these winds bring people in contact with what? ⟪ar:ذِكْرًا ‎⟫Reminders. These winds are meant to serve as powerful reminders, through reflection. What are these reminders Allah is talking about? What were the 3 arguments of the Quraish? They said

1. We don't need God for anything. We are the ones in control!

2. There is no purpose to creation. It is is just a random event

3. There is no hereafter or rising from the dead

He addressed the first argument of control and power with the preceding 2 AYATS, now he begins addressing the argument of purpose. Now if you think about winds, they create a kind of cooperation, between the heaves and the earths. Winds are moving the clouds in the heavens, and the rain is falling on the earth. And the earth is then growing vegetation, which is feeding life on this planet. And all of this is happening to serve who? Us! The human beings. And the single entity that is responsible for this entire cordination is what? Winds!

Simply by using the winds as an example, Allah is emphasizing the fact, that there is one single chain of command; there is single leadership. There is only one entity that is in control, and that is Allah(Subhanhu Wa Ta'ala). And then using the same example he is now describing the purpose of creation. Because think about it! Who does everything in creation serve? The winds, the clouds, the rain that falls from the clouds, the vegetation it grows, the animals that eat the vegetation, the animals that we feed on; all of this is ultimately serving who? Mankind! Us!

So Allah says,⟪ar:فَٱلْمُلْقِيَتِ ذِكْرًا.⟫ These winds should remind you of your purpose! Because I created everything with one unified purpose! which is to serve you! Everything around you, minerals, plants, animals are in service to you; and you think you were created without a purpose? Aren't you one of my creations too? How does their purpose of creation for you, not remind you of your purpose of creation for me? Just look at how everything in the world comes in perfect cooperation and coordination with each other? How they work hand in hand through the means of cause and effect, to serve you! If they being a lower form have a purpose, how can you being a higher form (by means of intellectual awareness); how can you believe that you have no purpose!

He delivers all these reminders and reflections, just through the example of winds! Talk about challenging the imagination! SubhanAllah!

And then there's another reminder that the winds carry. Let me give you an example. Let's say if I have a pet; and I leave my pet without water all day (Why not! After all I am "Asif" right, the inconsiderate! LOL).  So if I have a pet, whose mercy is the animal at? At my mercy! I need to put some water in a dish or bowl and give it to the animal. But the animal is not capable of helping itself at all. It can't open the cupboard and prepare dinner for itself. It is completely at my mercy, right? Regardless of how this animal behaves; whether it damages my property, messes my stuff, breaks things, whether it obeys me or not, in the end; at the end of the day; it is completely at my mercy. Isnt' that true? As wild and as rebellious human beings can get, if Allah does not give us these sips of water to drink, what would you and I do? Where would we go? Just think about that for a second. We would have no place to go! We are more pathetic and more powerless than the pets that we think we own! Now who brings the water? the clouds! And who disperses the clouds? Winds. SubhanAllah! The winds are a reminder of the lordship, mastery and control of Allah(Subhanhu Wa Ta'ala) over all creation. That no matter who you think you are! Whether you're a poor farmer; or the king of nations, you are completely dependent on me! I am the one letting you have these sips of water that's keeping you alive! This water is not your product. You can walk as arrogantly as you want on the earth, but if I don't send this mercy from the sky, you are finished! Do you understand now, why we sit and drink water? Why we express our gratitude to Allah(Subhanhu Wa Ta'ala) by sitting down and showing respect to this blessing of water? Its a mindful reminder to us, that this water that is SO easily accessible to us, is actually one of the greatest blessings of Allah(Subhanhu Wa Ta'ala). Because without it, we'd be dead!

So using wind as an example, Allah responded to the argument of control and purpose. What was the third one? Coming back to life after death? Resurrection right?

What happens when water falls on a dry piece of land. A land that has gone dry because of the absence of rain, what happens to it when the clouds shower it with water again? It comes back to life! DEAD becomes LIVING! How did they come to life? Through water! Where did the water come from? Clouds! Who got the clouds over that exact spot? Winds! SubhanAllah! Now everytime rains bring life to the dead earth, we are reminded that we will also die one day; and we will also be placed in the earth; and just as the rain brings the dead earth back to life through vegetation, we too one day will be resurrected. The one who can bring the dead earth back to life right in front of our own eyes, he can't bring *us* back to life? Ofcourse he can! This same earth will be giving out human beings on the day of judgment. And then he says:

and BTW, the Arabs would just get all of this just as they heard it. Everything that I just explained to you in an hour, they processed it instantly. Because this was their thing! Their imaginations operated at a completely different level than ours. So they just extracted all of these meanings instantly from these verses. You understand?

So after talking about winds as reminders, he says:

⟪ar-quote:‏عُذْرًا أَوْ نُذْرًا ‎⟫

He says, there will be to kinds of responses from people when they feel the wind on their face. The first will be the people of true intellect. These will the people, who will reflect on these signs and reminders, and they will recognize the wisdom behind them. They will accept Allah's majesty! They will submit to his glory! For such people these winds will serve as a justification (⟪ar:‏عُذْرًا⟫). The winds will as the proof of the might of Allah(Subhanhu Wa Ta'ala). And then there are those who will shut their eyes and ears to these reminders, and they will reject them; and they will choose to disbelieve in Allah, and reject him. For such people these same winds have become a warner (⟪ar:نُذْرًا⟫). Because the prophets job is not to convince and forcefully make them believe, his job is to warn them!

⟪ar-quote:وَمَا عَلَيْنَآ إِلَّا ٱلْبَلَغُ ٱلْمُبِينُ⟫

And our duty is only to convey clearly.

So the messenger (Salallahu alayhi wa aalihee wa sallam) is fulfilling his duty by delivering the message. If they choose to disbelieve, they have to face the consequences of their choices on the day of judgment. Because they had plenty of reminders throughout their lives in the form of winds! Winds were constantly reminding them of these realities; but they sill chose to to reject it. ⟪ar:عُذْرًا أَوْ نُذْرًا⟫.

So Allah responds to all 3 arguments with just one example. Isn't this incredible? With the same example, in just 6 concise AYATS; using just 12 simple words, he responds to all 3 arguments, in a way that rocks the Arab imagination! Even though its one example across 6 concise AYATS, they contain within them an ocean of reminders! SubhanAllah!

Then after setting this stage; after all this explanation of warnings, threats and glad tidings, he finally comes to the point...

⟪ar-quote:‏إِنَّمَا تُوعَدُونَ لَوَقِعٌۭ⟫

⟪ar:انما⟫means Indeed! No doubt about it! ⟪ar:توعدون⟫come from ⟪ar:وعد⟫which means a promise (Urdu ⟪ar:وعدہ⟫), and ⟪ar:وقع⟫means and event (Urdu: ⟪ar:واقعہ⟫). So Allah says, Indeed! No doubt about it! Certainly! What you have been promised, is going to become an event! Because that was the essence of their arguments! "We don't believe you" they said to the messenger! Allah emphasizes, it's all going to happen. And the word he uses, for resurrection and day of judgment is "event". Because there is a difference between information about something, and the event itself. Just like the destructive and constructive power of the winds remains informational until the event of hurricane takes place! Then it's no longer just information! It's an actual event! Just like storms and hurricanes that destroyed Katrina. They all knew that winds can turn into hurricanes and be devestating. But when they actually witnessed it in action, it was no longer information. It became a reality! A painful event! And notice he didnt' use the word reality! Because realities can be subjective. But events are objective. A wedding is an event; a funeral is an event. There can't be any confusions about it. You can't confuse the two, right? So Allah says, the day of resurrection and accountabiltiy is information for you today, but no doubt about it, it will one day become an actual event. And that day will either be a day of blessing for you, or it will a day of torment. You will either receive the Allah's mercy, rewards and blessings on that day; or you will receive his wrath and anger. It is bound to happen! It is certainly going to happen!

Oaths in the Quran are an extremely proufound, literary master piece in and of themselves. Each one of them! Surahs that begin with oaths require special careful study. Just the study of why Allah chooses to take an oath of these things. It is incredible. And I'm right now only speaking of the outward meanings, the ⟪ar:ظاہر⟫. I'm not even talking about ⟪ar:باطن⟫, which is SO SO SO much more powerful!

So now if you measure these verses against the ancient arab criteria: that speech should be precise; it should be concise; it should rock the imagination; It should deliver an ocean of meanings with just a few words! Let's reveiw these AYATS again to compare them against these criteria.

Their first argument of the poeple of Quraish was, "We don't need God for anything. We are the ones in control". So in the first two AYATS : ⟪ar:وَٱلْمُرْسَلَتِ عُرْفًۭا۔۔۔ فَٱلْعَصِفَتِ عَصْفًۭا⟫, Allah(Azza Wa Jal) talks about death and destruction, and reminds them of who is in control, using the example of what? Winds! How many AYATS? 2! How many words in this AYAH? 2!

Their second argument was, "There is no purpose to creation. It is is just a random event". So in the following two AYAATS: ⟪ar:وَٱلنَّشِرَتِ نَشْرًۭا ; فَٱلْفَرِقَتِ فَرْقًۭا⟫, Allah talks about life and prosperity and control, using the example of what again? Winds! How many AYATS? 2! How many words in each AYAH? 2!

Their third argment was, "There is no hereafter or rising from the dead". So in the following 2 AYATS: ⟪ar:فَٱلْمُلْقِيَتِ ذِكْرًا۔۔۔عُذْرًا أَوْ نُذْرًا⟪ar-quote:‎⟫⟫, Allah reminds them, that he will bring them back to life, just as he brings the dead earth back to life through rain. He reminds them that there is a profound system of punishment and reward in place. There are certain things that begetts his wrath; and then there are other things that begett his mercy; and the winds are there to remind you of both. In how many AYATS again? 2! How many words in each AYAH? 2!

> ⟪ar:وَالْمُرْسَلَتِ عُرْفًا ﴿١﴾ فَالْعَصِفَتِ عَصْفًا ﴿٢﴾ وَالنَّشِرَتِ نَشْرًا ﴿٣﴾ فَالْفَرِقَتِ فَرْقًا ﴿٤﴾ فَالْمُلْقِيَتِ ذِكْرًا ﴿٥﴾ عُذْرًا أَوْ نُذْرًا ﴿٦﴾ إِنَّمَا تُوعَدُونَ لَوَقِعٌ ﴿٧﴾⟫
> *Don't need God | No purpose to creation | No resurrection
Death & Destruction | Life & Prosperity | Resurrection & Accountability
Indeed (without a doubt) — promise — event*
> — **Quran 77:7** *(from image; see _provenance.json for validation)*
  (image preserved at ../images/009.png)
  *Note:* Pedagogical exposition of Sura al-Mursalat (Q77) as a chiastic argument against three denials.

Now if you group these AYATS, based on their messages, you get exactly 3 sets of messages. The first set talks about death and destruction. The second set talks about life and prosperity. The third set talks about resurrection and accountability! Each set has 2 AYATS, and each AYAH uses 2 words. And then in the 7th verse, he comes to the point and makes a final definitive statement, saying what?  ‏⟪ar:إِنَّمَا تُوعَدُونَ لَوَقِعٌۭ⟫. Indeed everything promised, will become a true event! How many words did he use this time to make this statement? 3 words! 3 sets of oaths, revealing 3 distinct responses, to 3 distinct agruments; followed by a final definitive statement using exactly 3 words! SubhanAllah!

Now lets look at these three words used in the 7th verse, and compare them to the 3 sets of messages.

⟪ar:إِنَّمَا⟫

What was the first message about? Death and destruction! and what were the words used? ⟪ar:وَٱلْمُرْسَلَتِ⟫and ⟪ar:عَصْفًۭا⟫. Powerful winds that can be extremely violent! Extremely inconsiderate. This verse delivers the threat of death and destruction! If Allah lets go of the reins of these winds, targetting a particular group of people, is death and destruction certain? Absolutely! What's the first word used in the 7th Ayah? ⟪ar:إِنَّمَا⟫. And what does that word mean? Certainly!
⟪ar:تُوعَدُونَ⟫
What was the second message about? Life and prosperity! and what words were used? Spreading and dissemination (⟪ar:نشر⟫)  and separation, making clear and distinct (⟪ar:فرق⟫).  What's the second word used in the 7th Ayah? ⟪ar:تُوعَدُونَ⟫, which comes from ⟪ar:وعد⟫, meaning promise. Isn't this message that Rasul Allah(Salallahu alayhi wa aalihee wa sallam) is being asked to deliver a promise of "life and properity" in the after life? And is this message of Quran widely spread and disseminated to people? What's the word for that? ⟪ar:نشر⟫ .And does this message of Quran separate the truth from falsehood? Doesn't it make good distinct and clear from evil? What's the word for that? ⟪ar:فرق⟫- - SubhanAllah!

⟪ar:لَوَقِعٌۭ⟫

What was the third message about? Resurrection and accountability on the day of judgment? What is the day of judgment? Isn't it an event? What's the third word used in the 7th verse of the AYAH? ⟪ar:لَوَقِعٌۭ⟫, and what does that word mean? Event! SubhanAllah!

How do you do that? How do you get this kind of accuracy and precision, in an extempore, unscripted speech! It is absolutely impossible for human beings to do this!

If someone makes 3 arguments, can you instantly start responding, and just before the words come out of your mouth, you go... Hmmmm... OK so these guys are making all these arguments that I need to respond to. I hear exactly 3 main arguments, so I need to to have 3 sets of responses. I'm going to use two AYATS per message for my response, and each AYAH will contain eactly 2 words. I will make my final point after these 3 sets of AYATS, and I will use exactly 3 words, in which each word will have a direct correspondence to each of the three messages in the exact same order in which I deliver them; Addressing their 3 arguments in the exact same order they presented them to me. Can you do this? Can any of us do this even in writing? let alone spoken, unscripted, impromptu speech? Even if we did try to do this in writing, how long would it take for us to come up with something remotely decent? And the messenger of Allah (Salallahu alayhi wa aalihee wa sallam) is doing this instantly, extemporaneously in speech! AllahuAkbar! This is truly miraculous!

<!-- section 8 (id=5789, raw_sort=8): Perfection of AlHAMDULILLAHI -->
In the previous session we looked at the miracle of how perfectly concise the Quran is in its style of communication. Today I want to share with you another dimension of Quran's incredible perfection. This example is very close to my heart because when I first learnt this,  I remember I was completely floored by it. I remember being completely overwhelmed by it, to the point that I actually had to cry it out to feel better. So this was one of the dimensions that really took me, and by it I truly experienced the miracle of Quran.

Now this example is quite technical, because it involves a lot of Arabic grammar. But InshaAllah I'll try to make it as simple as I can for you guys. So what we're going to do today is, do an in-depth grammatical analysis of the 2nd verse of SURAH AL-FATEHA, which is
⟪ar-quote:الحمد للہ رب العالمین⟫

We're going to look at the linguistic depth and perfection of these words, and try to get a better understanding of why Allah said this, in the way that he did. And is it possible to say this verse a different way?! And what would we gain or lose if we switched the words around.

---

Let's begin with the first two words: ⟪ar:الحمد للہ⟫.Now what are some of the common translations of ⟪ar:الحمد للہ⟫ that you've heard? Praise belongs to Allah? Gratitude belongs to Allah? Thank you Allah? You're so awesome Allah? So this is our general understanding of what ⟪ar:الحمد للہ⟫ means.
