Now from a linguistic perspective, in ancient Arabic, the word ⟪ar:حمد⟫is actually a composite of two words. The first is ⟪ar:المدح⟫which mean "praise"; and the second word is ⟪ar:الشکر⟫which means "thanks or gratitude". So linguistically ⟪ar:حمد للہ⟫ means "praise and gratitude belongs to Allah". And when you add the AL before the HAMD, it makes it exclusive; it makes it specific. So then ⟪ar:الحمد⟫⟪ar:للہ⟫ means "ALL praise and gratitude belongs ONLY to Allah".

Why not use the words Al-MADH and Al-SHUKR to be more explicit?

Use FATERA

Now if that's the case, why did Allah not say:

⟪ar-quote:المدح و الشکر للہ رب العلمین⟫

Praise and gratitude belongs to Allah. It would have been more clear, isnt it? And it would have meant the same thing!

So lets begin by understanding the difference between these two words: Praise and Gratitude.

[diagram: Teaching diagram on the Arabic root ḥ-m-d: central box 'حمد' branches downward to 'شکر / GRATITUDE' (labelled 'Unconditional') on the left and 'مدح / PRAISE' (labelled 'Genuine') on the right.]
  (see ../images/010.png)
  *Arabic labels in image:* ⟪ar:حمد · شکر · مدح⟫
  *Note:* Pedagogical: hamd combines unconditional gratitude (shukr) and genuine praise (madh).

You're walking down the street and you see a beautiful car, What do you do? Do you thank it? Or do you praise it? Hopefully, you don't thank it! Hopefully you don't walk up to the car pat it on the hood and say "thank you so much BMW". The normal thing to do would be to what? To praise it! It's a beautiful car! If you go to someone's house who just had a baby, do you thank the baby? or do you praise the baby? You praise it! Oh what a cute baby! Such a beautiful baby, right? That's praise!

Thanks is something entirely different. Thanks is ONLY done when you are acknowledging a favor. Something was done for you, and in order to express your appreciation for that gesture, you thank the person. You had a flat tire. Someone came and helped you out. You say thank you! Thanks can only happen when you have a "reason" to thank. In other words, gratitude is a reaction. Is that clear to everybody? Gratitude is "always" a reaction. A "thank you" is not something you lead with. Ever!  You don't meet somebody passing down the street and say, Hey you! Thanks!! You never do that!

**Are praise and gratitude mutually inclusive?**

Another distinction between the two is that praise and gratitude are not mutually inclusive. The one you thank, may not necessarily be the one you priase also. Even thought you could! I can say: Thank you so much for doing this for me, you're SO awesome! In this case, I just thanked "and" praised together. So it can be done! But then it is also possible that I can thank someone, but not priase them. Let's think about that for a second, How do you thank someone without actually praising them? Let's look at an example from the Quran. You know Moosa AS was raised in a pretty interesting home. Where was he raised? He had a pretty famous address. He was adopted and raised by Firon. Years later, MOOSA AS is commanded by Allah to go to FIRON and deliver his message to him. When he does that, Firon basically says to him, "How dare you? How dare you talk to me this way?"

⟪ar-quote:قَالَ أَلَمْ نُرَبِّكَ فِينَا وَلِيدًۭا , وَلَبِثْتَ فِينَا مِنْ عُمُرِكَ سِنِينَ⟫

Did we not raise you as a newborn in this house? Did you not spend many years of your life here? How dare you talk to me like that? In other words, what is FIRON saying? Aren't you what? Aren't you grateful? And then Moosa responds:

⟪ar-quote:وَتِلْكَ نِعْمَةٌۭ تَمُنُّهَا عَلَىَّ⟫

That is the favor you did in fact do for me. Thanks! That is Moosa AS's way of expressing gratitude. So even though FIRON is a guy who will never be praised, especially not by a prophet; but when he does a favor, he will still be what? Thanked!

Now another thing about the word ⟪ar:مدح⟫, is that even though ⟪ar:مدح⟫means praise, it does not always have to be genuine. MADAH can be insincere praise. Let's say you come home with a really bad report card. You walk through the door, and as soon as you enter the house you say, Mom! OMG, Your cooking smells so delicious!! And she hasn't even started cooking yet. So you're praising her, but it's not genuine. You get it? Praise could be fake. There is fake praise done for kings, for bosses, for people in positions of power. It is done all the time! People praise physical appearances all the time, "You look so beautiful!", and people eat it up with a spoon!  "Oh thank you so much! Hehehe". But that's a false praise. Because you are not truly worthy of that praise. YOU did not make you look beautiful. It was Allah who made you look beautiful by giving you these features. That's why in Arabic when you praise someone's look, you don't say ⟪ar:حَمِدَ⟫. You would say, ⟪ar:مَدَحَ⟫, because even the ancient Arabs had this understanding that even though it's praise, it is a false praise.

Now it has been argued by some women, that you have no idea how much time and energy goes into putting on the kind of makeup that we have to to look beautiful. So we do deserve some praise! But that's a different topic. There was a lady in my office; she would put on SO MUCH makeup; so much powder; that when I look at her I always imagined, "What if I went over, and slapped her? It would form like a cloud of powder all around the office.... LOL

So what I want you to understand, is that the words,⟪ar:الشکر و المدح⟫, praise and gratitude, are two different things; and they are mututally exclusive. When something nice is done for you, as a "reaction" you express gratitude, and the word for that reactionary gratitude is "⟪ar:شکر⟫". When you say ⟪ar:شکر⟫, or SHUKRIYA, by definition, it is a reaction to a favor. Whereas when you see something beautiful, or impressive, you praise it, and the word for it is ⟪ar:مدح⟫. But then it is possible for that praise to be insincere. And sometimes you can have praise without gratitude; and then there are times where you can thank someone, but not praise them. You understand?

But the word ⟪ar:حمد⟫, linguistically, can only be used for genuine praise! So when Allah says, ⟪ar:الحمد للہ⟫ ; He is not just saying "all praise", what's implied in that word is "genuine" praise. "All genuine praise belongs to Allah". The second meaning embedded within the word HAMD is "unconditional" gratitude. This gratitude is not "reactionary". It is not because Allah did things for us! Had he not done anything for anyone of us, he would still be worthy of all gratitude! And he would still be worthy of all praise! And his praise can never be an insincere praise. It can never be fake, or manufactured. Because linguistically, the word HAMD cannot be used for false praise.

⟪ar:حمد⟫, is a praise that generates in the heart, by the awareness of the magnificence, and the glory of the one being praised. I'll say that again. ⟪ar:حمد⟫, the praise element of ⟪ar:حمد⟫, it occurs when the heart becomes aware of the magnificence, and the glory of the one being praised. It is generated through the knowledge one acquires, about the glory, the brilliance, the greatness of the one that is being praised. It can therefore never be false. All of this is captured in meaning by the usage of the single word HAMD. Therefore saying ⟪ar:الحمد للہ⟫, is more powerful than saying ⟪ar:المدح للہ⟫  and it is more powerful than saying ⟪ar:الشکر للہ⟫. It is more comprehensive than both of them combined. SubhanAllah!

Another reason for not using the two words is eloquence. What was the criteria for ancient Arab eloquence? Speech had to "precise" and it had to be "concise". And so by using one word, Allah made the meanings precise and concise at the same time. 

Another reason for not saying ⟪ar:المدح و الشکر للہ رب العلمین⟫ , is that in classical Arabic, when you put the word AND  in between two things, which is the letter ⟪ar:و⟫, it separates both words even in meaning. So when I say⟪ar:المدح و الشکر للہ⟫, linguistically what I'm saying, is that praise belongs to Allah for some things, and gratitude belongs to Allah for other things. They're not always combined. Because the words aren't combined. This is a cool feature of Arabic language. You don't say what you don't mean. So if we use the two words gratitude and praise, and combined them with an⟪ar:و⟫, in classical Arabic that means, that sometimes I am in the mood to praise him, but not thank them; and then there are other times when I'm in the mood to thank him, but not praise him, But when Allah says AlHamdulillah, that means for every act he does; and for every act he holds back; for every blessing he gives and for every blessing he holds back, for what he does or does not do, he is still worthy of genuine praise, and unconditional gratitude, both at the same time, You don't get to pick and choose which one.

So now if you buy a nice car, and you say ⟪ar:الحمد للہ⟫. What have you just done? You genuinely praised Allah for giving human beings the ability to create cars, to design and manufacture them, *and* you are grateful to Allah for letting you own one. So you are praising and thanking Allah both at the same time. But for any reason if you end up losing the car, it's still HAMDULILLAH, becuase HAMD is not reactionary. You were not grateful to him just because he gave you the car. So even when he takes it away, genuine praise and unconditional gratitude still belongs to him! All of this is captured in this beautiful word, HAMD.

And this is why, ⟪ar:الحمد للہ⟫is actually not just a statement, but an attitude of a true Muslim. Because ALHAMDULILLAH is optimistic in nature. You know sometimes a person is going through a difficult time, and somebody asks, "How are you doing", and he goes, "Oh you know! life sucks, but Alhamdulillah. That is not HAMD! Because that is insincere praise, and that is reactionary gratitude. And by definition, HAMD cannot be insincere praise or gratitude out of reaction. And so for a believer, ALHAMDULILLAH becomes an attitude! Because Allah is not interested in what comes out of our tongues. He's more interested in what comes out of our tongues, that is also connected to our hearts, So we have to mean what we say when we say ⟪ar:الحمد للہ⟫. We need to always be mentally prepared to have a genuine reasons to praise Allah; and then thank him on top of it; be grateful on top of it! So even when I'm going through difficult times, ⟪ar:الحمد للہ⟫! I am genuinely and unconditionally grateful to Allah! Because whatever I'm going through, it could always have been worse. Someone right now in the world is going through a much harsher version of what I'm going through. So I'm grateful to Allah that he chose to be linient with me! And ⟪ar:الحمد للہ⟫! I praise him, because it is only He who can, and will get me out of my painful situation. So a sincere ⟪ar:الحمد للہ⟫, is actually a believers optimistic attitude towards Allah. It contains within it the most fundamental element of human survival! HOPE! And this is why the Quran begins with this optimistic attitude of ⟪ar:الحمد للہ⟫

Nouns and Verbs

Use SAMYA

Now let's analyze this phrasegrammatically. In any language, you can use nouns and you can use verbs to describe things. Between nouns and verbs, which has tenses? You know present tense, future tense, past tense? Verbs have a tense. Nouns do not have a tense. There's no past tense noun or present tense noun or future tense noun, right?, Now when I say, I praise Allah, Did I use a noun or a verb? I used a verb. And what tenses is it?  It's the present tense. But when I say "Praise belongs to Allah!", is the word "praise" just by itself, a noun or a verb? It is noun!

Why did Allah use a noun instead of a verb? He could have said,  ⟪ar:احمدُ اللہ⟫, "I praise Allah"; or he could've said ⟪ar:نحمد اللہ⟫, "We praise Allah!". But Allah did not use a verb; instead he used a noun, Why? Now here is what makes this so beautiful. When I use a verb, obviously there is going to be a tense associated with it; and when I use a present tense to say, "I praise Allah", then I am only talking about the present. I am saying nothing about the past; and I'm saying nothing about the future. If I use the past tense, then I am not guaranteeing anything about the future or the present. Because a tense has to be one or the other. A verb is limited; it is temporary. And so Allah used a noun, because nouns are what? They are permanent! Allah's genuine praise and unconditional gratitude is described with permanence. You know what that means? It means I may be praising Allah right now, but the praise of Allah has always been there. I am not going to be in this world forever, but the praise and gratitude of Allah will always be around - forever. His praise and gratitude is not dependent on me. You know how people sometimes say, "Why does Allah need me to praise him? Why do "I" have to praise Allah?". The response to that person is that you clearly don't understand the Quran my friend! Because the Quran begins by declaring his independence, his autonomy, his self-sufficiency for praise and gratitude with the words ⟪ar:الحمد للہ⟫. This is a huge reality that exists within Alhamdulillah; that the genuine praise and sincere gratitude of Allah is permanent. It is not dependent on me; it is not because of me!

The second this is, when I say "Rashida ate her food", who is doing the eating? When I say "Amir is playing", who is doing the playing? When we use a verbs, somebody needs to DO the verb, It's called the subject, or the ⟪ar:فاعل⟫in Arabic. A verb always needs a doer. You cant just go into a conversation and say, "Failed the test!". Who failed the test? You cant just say, "Disappeared!". What disappeared?. Oh your book disappeared, You see?, When you use a verb you need somebody to do it; you need a subject. You cannot just have a verb all by itself or it won't make sense. But a noun doesn't need someone to do it. A noun does not need a subject. A noun is independent by itself. An apple is an apple! It can exist all by itself, independent of any doer. So when Allah used the word ⟪ar:الحمد,⟫ He made it a noun. He made it independent. Because he doesn't need anyone to praise him; and he does not have a need for anyone to be grateful to him. Had he used a verb, that would have meant, that he needed someone to praise him, and he needed someone to be grateful to him. You understand?

Even if Allah said "Everything and everyone praises, and is grateful to Allah", that too would have been limited, Why?, Because everything and everyone implies everyone and everything that exists *now*, in the present. It excludes everything and everyone in the past or the future. And that is why Allah used a noun for his praise and gratitude. He used the word Hamd as a noun. So that it is not confined in time and space. Because Allah does not need his creation to praise him and be grateful to Him. His HAMD was there before this universe was created; his HAMD exists for the duration of this universe; and his HAMD will exist ever after this universe is destroyed. Because his praise and gratitude does not require a doer. SubhanAllah! All of this is captured in just by using a noun instead of a verb.

Why not make it a command?

Use SAMYA

Now what if Allah said:
⟪ar-quote:أِحمدَ اللہِ رَبِّ العلمین⟫

What if he used a command? Praise Allah! The master of universes! Wouldn't that have been better? After all he is the creator of the universe! He is a master and we are slaves, so shouldn't a command make more sense? So why didn't Allah make it a command, I'll give you an example to help you understand. When I tell my daughter Erum to bring me a glass of water, by saying, "Erum! bring me a glass of water!". When I say that, I'm giving her a command! Once she hears me, she has two possible choices. She can either bring me the glass of water; OR, she can bring me the glass of water! (LOL). Those are the only two clear choices as far as she's concerned.

Now if Allah commanded us to praise him, What are the two things that could possibly happen?. Some would praise him; some would obey his command; and then there would be others who would disobey him. Some would be grateful to him; other would not. When you tell someone to do something, the ball is in their court! The obedience of that command depends on them. Maybe they'll choose to do it; maybe they won't. Allah did not talk about praise and gratitude in a way that depends on us. He did not put the ball in our court. He said whether you do it or not; whether you are grateful to me or not; whether you praise me are not, my praise and gratitude will always still be there. My Hamd is always there. It has been there forever, and it will be there forever. Human beings will come and go; nations will come and go; generations will come and go; THIS WORLD will come and go. But the HAMD of Allah will always be there. It is simply a matter of fact . SubhanAllah!

Why not emphasize his HAMD?

Now what if Allah said:
⟪ar-quote:انَّا الحمد للہ رب العلمین⟫

Certainly! For sure! No doubt about it! ABSOLUTELY, Hamd is for Allah. Now what sounds more powerful? Does, "All praise and gratitude belongs to Allah" sound more powerful? Or does saying, "Definitely, Certainly. Absolutely Hamd is for Allah!" sound more powerful? Obviously the latter one. So how come Allah didn't say, ⟪ar:انَّا الحمد للہ رب العلمین⟫, A Khateeb uses it all the time before he delivers a KHUTBA. I say it in the beginning of sessions all the time when I'm glorifying Allah. Remember?

⟪ar-quote:انا الحمد للہ نحمدہ و نستعینہ و نستغفر بہ و نؤمنُ بہ و تنکوکل علیہ⟫

So how come Allah didn't say it?

In order to understand this, you have to understand something about human communication. There are only 2 kinds of communications possible for the human being! Regardless of the billions and trillions - the uncountable number of words we say during our lifetime; all human communication eventually boils down to two categories. A communication can either be informative, or it can emotional. This in Arabic is called ⟪ar:جملۃ انشائیۃ⟫and ⟪ar:جملۃ خبریۃ⟫ . But who cares! The point is that when we speak, we are either expressing feelings and emotions; or we are delivering information about something. These are the only two kinds of speech that human beings are capable of. That's it! Let's look at an example. Right now, when I'm teaching you about ⟪ar:حمد⟫, am I delivering information, or am I expressing my emotions? I am giving you information. I'm teaching you about the Quran. This is informative speech. But when I'm talking to my friend, and I'm telling him how I feel about the sessions, what kind of communication is that? That is an emotional conversation. So those are the only two types of speech, that we as human beings are capable of. Either expressing emotion, or delivering information.

Now the thing about Arabic linguistics is, that when you use ⟪ar:إِنَّآ⟫, that statement can ONLY be informative. It can only be factual. It can NEVER be emotional!
⟪ar-quote:انا انزلناہ فی لیلۃ القدر⟫

We revealed the Quran in the night of power. Is that informative or emotional? It is informative! Allah is stating a fact, that the Quran was revealed in the night of power.
⟪ar-quote:إِنَّآ أَرْسَلْنَكَ بِٱلْحَقِّ بَشِيرًۭا وَنَذِيرًۭا⟫

We have sent you as a messenger to deliver glad tidings and to warn people? Information or emotion? Information!
⟪ar-quote:إِنَّآ أَعْطَيْنَكَ ٱلْكَوْثَرَ⟫

We have granted you KAUSAR. Information or emotion? Information!

So when a sentence in Arabic begins with ⟪ar:إِنَّآ⟫, it can only be informative. It can never be emotional. You understand? So by not using ⟪ar:إِنَّآ⟫, Allah made his Hamd, a "statement", that we can use to talk about Allah's praise and gratitude with others; to give them information about it. But he also made it a statement to express our own emotion, SubhanAllah!,  The beauty of it is that it can now be used to communicate the emotions of our heart, as well as a message that we want to give to somebody else. Right now when I'm saying ⟪ar:الحمد للہ رب العلمین ,⟫I'm giving you information about Allah's HAMD. A few hours later, when I recite these exact same words during my prayers; and I say ⟪ar:الحمد للہ رب العلمین⟫I will be expressing my emotions. I will be expressing my unconditional gratitude and genuince praise to Allah(Subhanhu Wa Ta'ala). We can now do both! If ⟪ar:انا الحمد⟫ was used, technically it could no longer be used to express emotion. So Allah said ⟪ar:الحمد للہ رب العلمین⟫so that it could be used for both.  SubhanAllah!!

Saying it strangely

Use FATERA

Now there are some verses in the Quran, these same words are used in a strange way. They begin with
⟪ar-quote:فَلِلَّهِ ٱلْحَمْدُ⟫

For Allah belongs all praise and gratitude. For example, in SURAH AL-JASIYA, Allah says:
⟪ar-quote:فَلِلَّهِ ٱلْحَمْدُ رَبِّ ٱلسَّمَوَتِ وَرَبِّ ٱلْأَرْضِ رَبِّ ٱلْعَلَمِينَ ‎⟫

For Allah belongs all HAMD - master of the heavens and master of the earth - master of the worlds. So then when not do the same thing with FATEHA? Instead of saying ⟪ar:الحمد للہ رب العلمین⟫, why not say ⟪ar:فَلِلَّهِ ٱلْحَمْدُ رب العلمین⟫? Why did he not do that?

To explain this, I'll say two sentences. You tell me which one sounds normal.
**I ate lunch. Lunch I ate**

Which one sounds normal to you?
**They went to school. To school they went.**

Which one sounds normal?

But if I say, "To school they went". Do you still get what I'm saying? OK! So one is normal, and the other one is strange; but they're both understandable.  I'm not telling you this to explain how YODA from speaksin StarWars. Strong the force is! or whatever!

In the arabic language sometimes the sequence of the words in a sentence are changed, and they are deliberately made strange. If you remember in the first session when I gave you the example of FIRON's wife (ASIYA), and the prayer she made to Allah regarding her residence problems. She said:

⟪ar-quote:إِذْ قَالَتْ رَبِّ ٱبْنِ لِى عِندَكَ بَيْتًۭا فِى ٱلْجَنَّةِ⟫

"My Lord, build for me near You a house in Paradise". Instead of saying, "My lord build me a house in paradise near you", which would have been the normal way to say it. But she said it in a strange way. Do you remember why? Because when you mess up the sequence, it makes it exclusive!

So instead of saying "I ate lunch", when I say, "Lunch I ate", I make that noun exclusive. So what I'm really saying is that I ONLY ate lunch. I did not eat anything else except lunch. It makes it exclusive. It adds the meaning of "only" to the sentence. But the ancient arabs did not have to use the word ONLY. They would just change the sequence of words, and the exclusivity clause would automatically apply. It would automatically communicate the word ONLY.

So let's say I'm teaching this session, and you and Samiya are chatting or texting. Because having a daughter, I learnt one thing about you girls. BOY you girls can talk!! So let's say I'm teaching and you both are yapping in the background. And I say Fatera What's going on?!! and you say, "I wasn't the ONLY one!". Now when yous say, I wasn't the only one, what are you "actually" saying? If I'm going to get in trouble Samiya better be in trouble as well. But you didn't have to use the other sentence. You just used the one word "ONLY" and strategically placed it in the sentence, to imply the same fate for SAMYA. Similarly in Arabic, when you strategically mess up the sequence of words, you're actually saying 2 things, and making it exclusive.

Now if you look at the context of the ayah in Surah Al-JASIYAH

⟪ar-quote:فَلِلَّهِ ٱلْحَمْدُ رَبِّ ٱلسَّمَوَتِ وَرَبِّ ٱلْأَرْضِ رَبِّ ٱلْعَلَمِينَ ‎⟫

in this entire SURAH, Allah is talking to the MUSHRIKEEN! The people who commit SHIRK. Who associate partners with Allah. Who praise and are grateful to people other than Allah. So Allah reverses the sequence of words and say. Hey! Watch it! HAMD ONLY belongs to me and nobody else! But in the context of SURAH AL-FATEHA, it was not revealed as a debate. SURAH AL-FATEHA is Allah introducing himself to us. He is not debating us; He's not settling an argument; He's not angry at us; and so he used a tone that is gentle about a fact that is inherintly known by all human beings. And so he does not need to apply the exclusivity clause, and so he says it the normal way: ⟪ar:الحمد للہ رب العالمین⟫.

And you know what this teaches us? It teaches us that the HAMD of Allah is already in everyone's heart. The disbeliever has simply lost his way; the polythiest has forgotten it; and so Allah gently, but powerfully reminds them about who he is in this SURAH. That's why he says ⟪ar:الحمد للہ⟫, is used instead of ⟪ar:فَلِلَّهِ ٱلْحَمْدُ⟫.

Why use Allah as well as Rabb?

Use SAMYA

Now the next question is, why use the words Allah as well as the word Rabb? Why say ⟪ar:الحمد للہ رب العلمین⟫? All HAMD is for Allah the master of the worlds. Why not just say:
⟪ar-quote:الحمدُ لِرَبِّ العلمین⟫

All praise and gratitude belongs to the master of the world. We would still get it, right? So why use both words? The reason for that is that the word "RABB" is an attribute of Allah. RUBUBIYYAH (which means mastery or lordship) is one of his many attributes. But "Allah" is his name. In the FATEHA, Allah is introducing himself to us! When you introduce someone you use your name, not your attributes. If I met you for the first time and said, "AsSalaamAlaykum I'm a teacher". You'll say "WalaykumAsSalaam Asif Chacha! You're also a weirdo!", right? Because you don't introduce yourself with your profession. Instead, if I said, "AsSalaamAlaykum, I'm Asif and I teach the Quran" that would make sense! And because Allah is introducing himself in the FATEHA, it is more appropriate to being with his name, than simply refer to himself through an attribute. So you have that perfection in there as well.

But there is something else in there that is so beautiful. When I look at a painting and I say "That is beautiful!". What am I praising them for? Their art! I am praising one particular skill. When I thank a teacher, what do I thank him for? For teaching me something. Thanks is specific. It is always for a particular favor that was done for me. In the same way "praise" is also very specific. You praise the beauty of a flower because its beautiful. You praise the freshness of the air because of how you feel. So if we said, ⟪ar:الحمد للخالق⟫ . HAMD belongs to the creator; then the only thing we are thanking Allah for, is creating this universe and everything within it. If we say ⟪ar:الحمد للحکیم⟫. Praise and gratitude belongs to the wise! Then the only thing we are appreciating about Allah is what? His wisdom! So how then do I appreciate "every single " thing about Allah(Subhanhu Wa Ta'ala) without missing anything? The things I can think of; as well as the things I can't think of; and also the things I will never be able to think of. How do I include everything in one concise statement, such that I truly get to thank Allah in the way he truly deserves to be thanked and praised? By saying ⟪ar:الحمد للہ⟫. When I associate the word HAMD with his name ALLAH, I am now genuiniely praising and unconditionally begin grateful to him for all of his attributes; for every single attribute that he possess. This is why we find the word HAMD associated with Allah and not RABB.

---

Another reason for explicitly mentioning the name Allah, is because the word RABB just by itself could be ambiguous.  People could have different concepts of ⟪ar:رب العلمین⟫ Praise the lord! To a Chirstian, "RABB", would mean something else. It could mean something else to a jew. It means something else to a Muslim. But Praise "Allah", the master of the worlds, leaves no room for confusion. I'll give you a perfect example of this from the Quran:

Which prophet was asked to face off against magicians? Moosa AS! Moosa AS faces off against these powerful magicians of FIRON. They throw their ropes and their rods and they turn into snakes. Then MOOSA AS throws down his staff, and it turns into a serpent that swallows up all the other snakes. What the magicians see that, what do they do?  They fall into sajda. Now I want you to picture this: FIRON is standing on stage, and the magicians are in SAJDA. And he's confused! "What's going on here? Are you guys getting ready for round 2, or what?? Or is this part of the act? what's going on?". So the magicians stand up from SAJDA and they say.
⟪ar-quote:قَالُوٓا۟ آمَنَّا بِرَبِّ ٱلْعَلَمِينَ⟫

We believe in the master of the worlds! They use the word "RABB".  But Firon is still confused! Why? Why is he confused? Because what had Firon declared?
⟪ar-quote:أنا ربکم الاعلی⟫

I am your greatest master! FIRON had already declared himself as RABB! And now the magicians are saying what?  ⟪ar:آمَنَّا بِرَبِّ ٱلْعَلَمِينَ⟫ We believe in the maser of the worlds. So FIRON is confused. Because he believes he is the Rabb they are doing SAJDA to. So the magicians are in SAJDA saying we believe in the master of the worlds, and FIRON is standing there going, AAAANNNNDDDD?? GOOO ONNNN???  LOL

And so they say, "No! you idiot! We're not talking about you"
⟪ar-quote:رَبِّ مُوسَىٰ وَهَرُونَ⟫

The rabb of Moosa and Haroon. The master of MOOSA and HAROON. They had to clarify. Because if they had just said ⟪ar:رَبِّ ٱلْعَلَمِينَ⟫, FIRON would have had no problems with that, you understand?. So the word Allah is absolutely critical in this verse.

---

Conclusion

So you see! Every verse in the Quran, starting with ⟪ar:الحمد للہ⟫, is *extremely* perfect in the way Allah says it. That no matter what variation you try to come up with; you try to use a verb; you try to use INNA; you try to change it into a command; you try to alternate the words of HAMD to words like Shukar and Madah; you try to leave out a name, you try to add a name; and you completely lose what Allah said and the beauty and the perfection of the way in which he said it. This Quran is like a beautiful architecture that you cannot move one brick from its place, or you'll lose the beauty of the structure. SubhanAllah!

Now this exercise that I just did with you guys, of just "kind of" exploring what ⟪ar:الحمد للہ⟫ is; and the alternatives are? And how come the alternatives are not good enough?. This exhaustive exercise exists for the entire quran! Verse by verse! Word by word by word. And I hope this gives you an apprecateion of the power of the Quran like nothing else you've experienced before. This is not just some book that we have in our houses to decorate our shelves. In todays day and age this book has been reduced to paper weight! But if you actually get engaged with the study of Quran, I swear to you, WALLAHI, there is no other book like this. How many times can you read the #1 best selling novel? How many times can you watch the #1 classic movie of all time? 2X, 3X, 4X. At some point you'll get bored. But the Quran is an ocean that has not bottom. The more you study it, the more you keep getting out of it, and there is no end to its unique treasures. SubhanAllah ALAZEEM!

How do you this in unscripted extemporaneous speech?

<!-- section 9 (id=5791, raw_sort=9): Science, preservation and rhyme scheme -->
Let's do a recap of what we've learnt so far. We established that Quran is an unscripted impromptu speech, delievered on the tongue of Rasul Allah(Salallahu alayhi wa aalihee wa sallam) before a live audience, made up all sorts of people - family, friends, arch enemies. We also know that this message was delievered while the prophet (Salallahu alayhi wa aalihee wa sallam) is going through a slew of emotions. And as human beings, we understand the effects that emotions can have on our speech. We struggle to find the proper words when our emotions are hightened. And yet this Quran is delivered in the most perfect and the most eloquent speech, consistently, regardless of the prophets state or the environment his is placed in.

And so the style of this message becomes a ⟪ar:معجزۃ⟫for the ancient Arabs. ⟪ar:معجزۃ⟫from the root word ⟪ar:عجز⟫means to completely defeat somone; to incapacitate somone; to render someone incapable of a response. And this is exactly what the Quran did to these ancient Arabs. They believed that they were the masters of their language. They believed that they had evolved it to the point where it is now humanly impossible to improve upon it any further. And here comes the Quran with a style, with an eloquence, with a perfection in its precision; in its conciseness; in its linguistic beauty, that completely blows them away. They are dumb founded by it. They cannot criticize it, they cannot challenge it, they cannot find a single flaw in it. And so it became clear as day to them, that this could not be the words of a human being; because it's not humanly possible to speak at this level of perfection. And so by their intellects, they are forced to surrender to it, and accept it as a divine message.

I also explained to you, and we've started experiencing this ourselves, that why Allah switched the style of his miracles from visual to audible. All previous miracles were for the eyes; but the Quran is a miracle for the ears. Because what the eye see is short lived. The people who saw EISA AS bring the dead back to life, they witnessed that event, at that particular moment, and then the miracle was over. But Quran is a miracle that is alive because of it audible nature. This is why I am able to recreate this experience of a "miracle" for you in these sessions. Everytime you learn something in these sessions, that makes you say SubhanAllah! WOW! This is incredible! This is truly amazing! That's you experiencing a miracle! That is the experience of ⟪ar:معجزۃ⟫. Every time I say SubhanAllah as I'm sharing this with you, that's me experiencing a miracle with you. So I urge you all to be mindful of that experience when it happens.

Today I'm going to share with you 3 more dimensions in which Quran provides a miraculous experience.

Scientific dimension

The first is its scientific dimension. As I said earlier, to science, there is no such thing as a miracle. Miracle is an extremely unscientific concept. There is no emperical evidence to prove the existence of heaven, hell, angels, jinn , everlasting life, and all this sort of stuff. If you think about it, we believe in JANNAH, in which we can eat anything we like, and we never need to go to the toilet; and we sweat perfume. All very unscientific for someone who doesn't believe. right? And there's an entire discussion of how these things can be proven rationally, which is outside the scope of these particular sessions.

But what's really interesting is that in recent times, this subject - science and Quran - has really picked up momentum. And the reason for that is because Allah speaks to his creation in the Quran, with one specific intention; with one precise goal. And that goal is to inspire reflection. To inspire reflection on the beauty of his creation.

⟪ar-quote:أَوَلَمْ يَتَفَكَّرُوا۟ ۗ مَا بِصَاحِبِهِم مِّن جِنَّةٍ ۚ إِنْ هُوَ إِلَّا نَذِيرٌۭ مُّبِينٌ⟫

⟪ar-quote:إِنَّ فِى ذَلِكَ لَآيَتٍۢ لِّقَوْمٍۢ يَتَفَكَّرُونَ⟫

Allah invites us to reflect! Reflect on what? The subtelties in the design of his creation. To reflect on the technology that he used in his creation. The symmetry that is involved in the desing of a single leaf. The advanced technology used in the creation of a single cell; in an atom. Allah wants us to reflect on it and see how advanced it is. And where science has reached today, even with such spectacular advancements, we cannot even create a fly, or a mosquito that is conscious of its own existence. And Allah created something as "man".

So one of the demands of the Quran, is of reflection. And where it becomes miraculous in its speech, is in how this message reveals facts about this universe; 1400 years ago; that are only now being proven scientifically, in recent times. So I want to quickly touch upon a few AYATS from this dimension.

[image 011: AI vision pending — see ../images/011.png]

One interesting example is Surah Al-Hadeed. The word HADEED in Arabic means "Iron". Allah says..

⟪ar-quote:وَأَنزَلْنَا ٱلْحَدِيدَ فِيهِ بَأْسٌۭ شَدِيدٌۭ وَمَنَفِعُ لِلنَّاسِ⟫

And we have sent down iron, which is very powerful, and contains many benefits for mankind

Now Allah talks a lot about His creation in the Quran. But when he does so, he uses the word  ⟪ar-quote:خلق⟫.
⟪ar-quote:يَٓأَيُّهَا ٱلنَّاسُ ٱعْبُدُوا۟ رَبَّكُمُ ٱلَّذِى خَلَقَكُمْ⟫

⟪ar-quote:هُوَ ٱلَّذِى خَلَقَ لَكُم مَّا فِى ٱلْأَرْضِ جَمِيعًۭا⟫

⟪ar-quote:إِنَّ فِى خَلْقِ ٱلسَّمَوَتِ وَٱلْأَرْضِ⟫

But when he speaks of iron, he did not use the word ⟪ar:خلق⟫. Instead what did he say? ⟪ar:وَأَنزَلْنَا⟫.We sent down!

Scholors of the past had been struggling with this concept. Because the words of the Quran are very precise. Muslims would argue that oh by sent it down he actually meant that he created it. And the argument to that would be, NO! If he wanted to say he created it, he would have used the word ⟪ar:خلق⟫. But He specifically used the word ⟪ar:أَنزَلْنَا⟫sent it down. So why did he use that word in particular?

In the 20th century, geologists come to an agreement about the beginnings of the earth. One of them being that iron is not part of the original earth's substance. It came to the earth in the form of meteor showers. And it got burried very deep into the core of the earth. Hence the word Allah uses in the Quran, specifically when it comes to "iron" is ⟪ar:أَنزَلْنَا⟫, and not ⟪ar:خلق⟫. "We sent down" becomes a very accurate depiction of the reality of iron coming into this world. Because it was literally sent down.

---

Another example is in surah Furqan, Allah say
⟪ar-quote:تَبَارَكَ ٱلَّذِى جَعَلَ فِى ٱلسَّمَآءِ بُرُوجًۭا وَجَعَلَ فِيهَا سِرَجًۭا وَقَمَرًۭا مُّنِيرًۭا⟫

Allah speaks about things in the heavens that are at his disposal.
⟪ar:تَبَارَكَ ٱلَّذِى جَعَلَ فِى ٱلسَّمَآءِ بُرُوجًۭا⟫Blessed is the one who placed stars in the sky. And then he says
⟪ar:وَجَعَلَ فِيهَا سِرَجًۭا⟫... in the sky he place for us a lamp. He calls the sun a lamp in this verse. And then he says ⟪ar:وَقَمَرًۭا مُّنِيرًۭا⟫. The word قمر means moon. But the word "⟪ar:منیر⟫" is what is so scientific. The word ⟪ar:منیر⟫means something that is "given" light. It doesn't have light of its own, it is given light from an external source. Something that is illuminated; something that does not give out light, but is lit by something else. For example the room you're sitting in is ⟪ar:منیر⟫, because of the light the bulbs are giving off. The bulb itself is ⟪ar:سراج⟫, but the room is ⟪ar:منیر⟫.

So when Allah spoke of the sun he called it a lamp. But when he spoke of the moon, he called it something that reflects light. So at a time when this is not a known phenomenon, Rasul Allah is speaking of a moon as a body in space that does not give off its own light, but is being lit by something else. Today for us, this is common knowlege. But 1400 years ago, this is not a very obvious concept. Because it looks like its giving off its own light. right? And so we find these precise discriptions in the Quran, that are only being proven today by scientists. SubhanAllah!

---

Then another amazingly scientific miracle is Allah says in Surah Al-Ambiya, describing the heavens and the earth, which is the arabic expression for the universe.

⟪ar-quote:أَوَلَمْ يَرَ ٱلَّذِينَ كَفَرُوٓا۟ أَنَّ ٱلسَّمَوَتِ وَٱلْأَرْضَ كَانَتَا رَتْقًۭا فَفَتَقْنَهُمَا⟫

Do the disbelievers not see that the heavens and the earth was a single fused material and we separated them.

The word ⟪ar:رتق⟫means something that is fused and inseparable. Fused and inseprable. The word ⟪ar:رتق⟫is used when a mother is carrying a child in her womb, because the mother and child are inseparable at that time. And when she would start delivering, the word used is ⟪ar:فتق⟫. Fataqa is the time for her to start parting. Literally her body is parting up and she is parting from her child.

So the AYAH says that the heavens and the earth used to be fused into one body, they were inseparable and then we caused them to come apart. Meaning the universe in its origin was a fused, united body. One single matter. And then it parted and spread out far and wide. What is this verse talking about? The Big Bang theory! About how the universe came into existence from a singularity with a big bang. And its explaining this 1400 years ago. And then he says:
⟪ar-quote:وَجَعَلْنَا مِنَ ٱلْمَآءِ كُلَّ شَىْءٍ حَىٍّ⟫

We made the water a source of life for all living things. And today we all know that our bodies are made up of about 60 to 80% of water  during a life span. Again, something stated way ahead of its time...

---

**https://quran.com/23/12**

In this verse from SURHA MUMINOON, Allah describes the exact process of how the fetus develops in a mothers womb.
⟪ar-quote:وَلَقَدْ خَلَقْنَا ٱلْإِنسَنَ مِن سُلَلَةٍۢ مِّن طِينٍۢ⟫

We created man from the purest kind of clay;
⟪ar-quote:ثُمَّ جَعَلْنَهُ نُطْفَةًۭ فِى قَرَارٍۢ مَّكِينٍۢ ‎⟫

then made him a drop in a secure receptacle;
⟪ar-quote:ثُمَّ خَلَقْنَا ٱلنُّطْفَةَ عَلَقَةًۭ فَخَلَقْنَا ٱلْعَلَقَةَ مُضْغَةًۭ فَخَلَقْنَا ٱلْمُضْغَةَ عِظَمًۭا فَكَسَوْنَا ٱلْعِظَمَ لَحْمًۭا ثُمَّ أَنشَأْنَهُ خَلْقًا آخَرَ ۚ فَتَبَارَكَ ٱللَّهُ أَحْسَنُ ٱلْخَلِقِينَ⟫

then formed the drop into a clot and formed the clot into a lump and formed the lump into bones and clothed the bones in flesh; and then brought him into being as another creature. Blessed be Allah, the Best of Creators!

These verses are revealing fundamental information from the field of embryology. Allah describes the womb as⟪ar:قَرَارٍۢ مَّكِينٍۢ⟫"a secure receptacle”. The word ⟪ar:مَّكِينٍۢ ‎⟫suggests meanings such as ‘unshakeable, sound, fixed; And the word "قَرَارٍۢ" means ‘a place of settlement. A place of safety’ Today we know that a mother’s womb provides insulation to the fetus, against external agents, such as light and sound; and protects it against shock and pressure. The womb is located in the pelvic cavity, and is well protected by thick and strong bones. And so the word ⟪ar:قَرَارٍۢ مَّكِينٍۢ⟫is an extremely accurate description of this process. And then he goes on to describe the stages of an embroys development in the perfect order. Doctors and scienties today attest to the perfection of this description. Just look up Quran and human embrylogy and you'll find all the evidence you need to prove the accuracy of this verse.

But what's incredible is that this description is being delivered 1400 years ago when the ancient Arabs didnt have access to this kind of technology. They didn't have XRay machines. There was absolutely no way for them to know this stuff. And yet the Quran explains these details with incredible perfection. SubhanAllah!

Miracle of Rememberance

The next dimension that I want to share with you today, is of Quran's preservation, and how it unites us as an nation. Allah says in the Quran:

⟪ar-quote:إِنَّا نَحْنُ نَزَّلْنَا ٱلذِّكْرَ وَإِنَّا لَهُۥ لَحَفِظُونَ ‎⟫

Indeed, we revealed this message, and indeed we will protect and preserve it. Allah takes on the responsibility of protecting and preserving his message. The word INNA which is used purely for informative speech; Allah says, Certainly, we have revealed this message; and certainly we will protect it. In other words, the safety and preservation of this message is not your responsibility, it's mine! So now let's see how he did that.

**Volunteer**

Is Quran an oral tradition or a written tradition? Oral! It is a spoken text. Now you tell me. Is it harder to preserve an oral tradition? Or is it harder to preserve a written tradition? Oral! It is exteremely difficult to preserve an oral tradition.

Do you know what chinese whisper is? Have you ever played it?

Let's say that we as a group, play this game of Chinese whisper. We all from a line, with you right next to me, and (let's say) Ali at the other end of the line. I begin with you. I whisper in your ear

"Aslam bumped into Faisal", OK?

Now you whisper it SAMIYA, she whispers it to Zain, he whispers it to Rida, she whispers it to Kashif, he whispers it to the next person, and we go on and on and on. What was the original sentence?

"Aslam bumped into Faisal"

By the time it reaches Ali - last member of this group - that statement has turned into "Aslam, burned Faisal's house down, destroyed his belongings, and killed his entire family". This is something that happens in oral tradition. Isn't that true? Nobody wanted to intentionally changed the original message. Somebody just decided to say the same sentence in their own way. They added or took away 1% of the sentence. Somebody else changed another half percent. Somebody else another 2%. Now 1 to 2% is not a major change. Is it? But when it passes through multiple people, the original message becomes completely unrecognizable. These kinds of experiments are done in communicaiton psychology all the time. Any kind of oral tradition is impossible to preserve. And the more it travels; the more people it passes through; the more it changes; and the more it varies. It's only logical.

Now by comparison, written tradition is safe. But it is not entirely safe. In the time of the prophet (Salallahu alayhi wa aalihee wa sallam), it's not like they had image scanners, or audio recorders, or back up hard drives. They used to write on camel hide. And so even if you have a written book, a line could get smudged, a paragraph could become illegible over time, it could get torn. So even if that written text reaches down generation, that could create skepticism about the integrity of the original content, right?

Now the Quran is an oral expression, that was compiled in the form of a book decades later. Originally, the way of recording or preserving the Quran was through memorization. Rasul Allah would recite a passage as the divine inspiration (wahi) would come to him. People would listen to it and immediately memorize it. Now you could ask, how is it humanly possible to memorize this message so accurately? So let's first try to understand that bit.

I'm going to say a sentence to you. I want you to listent to it very carefully, and then I want you to recite it back to me - verbatim - without missing a word. OK?  Ready?

My name is MARYAM. I am 11 years old. AND I am awesome!

Now repeat it! You see, you were able to repeat it back to me accurately. Was it hard? No! OK.  Next sentence. I want you to repeat this one to me as well, OK

⟪ar-quote:آمَنَ ٱلرَّسُولُ بِمَآ أُنزِلَ إِلَيْهِ مِن رَّبِّهِ⟫

Why couldn't you recite it back? Becuase I said it in a language that you're **not**very familiar with. That you do not have comamnd over. So you have to remember, that when we ask questions like, "how is it possible to memorize the Quran so accurately", we forget that the Quran was not revealed to us DESIS. It was revealed to ancient Arabs, who were masters of what? The arabic language! So memorizing Quran to us may be a very challenging task, but to them it was a piece of cake. you understand?

Anyway, so as the Quran is being revealed, people around the Rasool Allah, are listening to it, and memorizing it down to the last syllable. Then they would travel far and wide and recite the Quran to the Arabs of other cities. Then those people would listen to this message, memorize it and then they would teach others.

Now understand that once they left their land, they are completely cut off from the main land. It's not like they had phones or email. They couldn't call each other to confirm AYATS. Hey! Chapter 1 verse 2, Was it AlHamdu Lillahi or AlHamda Lillahi? They couldn't do that right? Once you've left the city, you're completely cut off from the source. And this how these people are memorizing the Quran and spreading it. So the logical assumption should be that within a year, there should have been a 100 versions of the Quran. Right? Uncountable variations of the original tradition. That's what should have happened.

Now fast forward to 2016. Today, almost every mosque in the world has a Quran memorization program. Hundreds of thousands of kids memorize the Quran each year. We all have also memormized atleast some surahs right?

Have you ever been to Indonesia? Do you speak Indonesean? OK! So let's say you travel to Indonesia which is a muslim country. You're among a bunch of local girls who don't speak English or Urdu. And you don't speak Indonesian. You start reciting Surah Al-Fateha. You say one syllable wrong - just one syllable. You say... AlHamda Lillahi... 3 girls will immediately stop you. They'll say no it's AlHamdu lillahi! Isn't that incredible? You don't know their language, they don't know yours, you've never met them before. But as soon as you recite the Quran, you're unified in one language.

If I'm at the airport, it's time for prayers, a man stands up and starts praying. Other muslims join him in prayer. He begins reciting the Quran. Every one is a stranger to every other person in that group. They've never met each other before this day. If he recites one word, one letter, one syllable of one word wrong, everyone will correct him with the right syllable. By the syllable - SubhanAllah!

---

Which city do you live in? Ok let's assume for a second, that all the Qurans of the world have been destroyed. Every book, every digital copy, every form of the Quran has been destroyed. It's no longer available anywhere. Not on the internet, not on computers, not on your phone, not in any book shelf. It's completely gone. Not just in your city but everywhere in the world. OK?

The only copy left is the original text that has been preserved in some library in Russia, let's say. There is no other form of Quran available any where in the entire world. You understand?

I can guarantee you that within 24 hours you will have the original Quran back, in just your city. Not even another city, just your city. How? Because of the kids in (city) who have memorized it. You give each kid a few pages to write and within 24 hours the entire book will be back. And when they reproduce it in writing, and you compare it to the libary copy of the Quran, guess what? Every word will match perfectly, down to the last syllable! SubhanAllah! Tell me of one book in the entire world, with which something like this is possible. SubhanAllah! This is how ingrained Quran is in the hearts of the Muslims. And this book is over 6000 verses. It's insane! This stuff really fascinates me! How can the world be so unified when it comes to this one single book? So many people are memorizing the Quran! Logically we should have so many versions of the Quran. And yet, we never find a discrepancy in an single word of this text, within our borders, or across our borders. AllahuAkbar! Another thing is that with time, documents become less and less viable. They become less valid. This is the only text that becomes more and more valid as time passes. SubhanAllah!

Rhyme Scheme

The last dimension for today is that of the Quran's rhyme scheme. This one is is SO SO amazing!

We all know that Quran has a rhyme scheme to it even though it is not poetry. First of all why is it not poetry? Let's first understand that.

For the ancient Arabs just because something rhymes, doesn't make it poetry. Arabic poetry has "very specific rules", rhyme being just one of them.

[diagram: Arabic prosody diagram of one bayt (verse) from al-Farazdaq's qasida. The bayt is split into a 'First Half' (6 words / 14 syllables) and a 'Second Half' (7 words / 14 syllables); a central wazn (meter) value of 15 separates them. Music-staff icons under each half evoke the meter analogy.]
  (see ../images/012.png)
  *Arabic labels in image:* ⟪ar:بَیت · هَذَا الَّذِي تَعْرِفُ الْبَطْحَاءُ وَطْأَتَهُ · وَالْبَيْتُ يَعْرِفُهُ وَالْحِلُّ وَالْحَرَمُ · وزن⟫
  *Note:* Prosodic analysis: the same al-Farazdaq line introduced in binder 34 ch153 used here to illustrate Arabic meter (15 syllables symmetric across the two hemistichs).

Without getting too technical, in Arabic poetry, each verse (which is called a bayt) is divided into two halves; and each half is made up of long and short syllables, which are called "meters" or ⟪ar:وزن⟫. There are 15 set metersfor Arabic poetry. Each meters has to do with the length of the syllables in a verse. Think of it like the beats of a drum in a song. You have hard and soft beats and they must be consistent across the song. It's the same with Arabic poetry.

The rule for Arabic poetry is that the number of syllabels must be consistent across a verse, and the pattern in which these syllables occur must also be consistent. The number of words in each pair does not matter. What matters is the count, and the pattern of the syllables used in the verse. . So if the first half in the verse has 10 syllables, the second half must also have 10 syllables. And if the first half has a syllable pattern of: SLSLSL, then the second half must also have the exact same pattern.

If you look at the image, you can see, that the first half has 6 words, and the second half has 7 words. But they both have exactly 14 syllables; and they both follow the exact same long-short pattern in each half.

Now even though the Quran has a rhyme scheme, the number of syllables; and the patterns in which these long and short syllables occur, differ between each AYATS. And this is is the reason Quran cannot be categorized as poetry; even though it sounds like poetry. So Quran, despite its rhyme scheme, is considered prose, and not poetry. It is prose in a poetic form.

---

Now each SURAHS of the quran has a certain rhyme scheme. But those of you who recite the Quran often, you must have noticed there are times when Allah suddenly changes the rhyme scheme in the middle of the surah. There's a certain rhyme going on, and then in some cases, suddenly the rhyme scheme changes for a few AYATS; and then it returns back to the previous rhyme scheme.

**https://quran.com/19/1

[image 013: AI vision pending — see ../images/013.png]
**

[image 014: AI vision pending — see ../images/014.png]

So for example, if you look at Surah Maryam, this SURAH has a certain rhyme scheme. It ends with words that rhyme
⟪ar-quote:ذِكْرُ رَحْمَتِ رَبِّكَ عَبْدَهُۥ زَكَرِيَّآ⟫

⟪ar-quote:‏إِذْ نَادَىٰ رَبَّهُۥ نِدَآءً خَفِيًّۭا⟫

⟪ar-quote:‏قَالَ رَبِّ إِنِّى وَهَنَ ٱلْعَظْمُ مِنِّى وَٱشْتَعَلَ ٱلرَّأْسُ شَيْبًۭا وَلَمْ أَكُنۢ بِدُعَآئِكَ رَبِّ شَقِيًّۭا⟫

So we see that the last words of these verses are following a particular rhyme scheme

⟪ar-quote:⟪ar-quote:زَكَرِيَّآ⟫، خَفِیَّا، شَقِیَّا، وَلِیَّا، ⟪ar-quote:رَضِيًّۭا⟫، ⟪ar-quote:⟪ar-quote:سَمِيًّۭا،⟫⟫ نَبِیَّا⟫

and the ayats go on and on and the words at the end of the ayaats keep rhyming and rhyming and rhyming until you reach ayah number 34

⟪ar-quote:ذَلِكَ عِيسَى ٱبْنُ مَرْيَمَ ۚ قَوْلَ ٱلْحَقِّ ٱلَّذِى فِيهِ يَمْتَرُونَ⟫

Everything was rhyming perfectly so far, and now from here the rhyme scheme changes. It's no longer⟪ar:زَكَرِيَّآ، خَفِیَّا، شَقِیَّا⟫.... it switches to

⟪ar-quote:فَيَكُونُ،⟫⟪ar-quote:مُّسْتَقِيمٌۭ⟫،⟪ar-quote:عَظِيمٍ⟫، ⟪ar-quote:مُّبِينٍۢ⟫، ⟪ar-quote:يُؤْمِنُونَ⟫، ⟪ar-quote:يُرْجَعُونَ⟫
So why is that? Is there any sort of logic behind this change or is it just random? As we know by now, Quran is perfect in its form. Everything is precisely in its place. Every word and its position in an AYAH has a specific purpose. So obviously it's not possible for the rhyme scheme to be just random.

What's so cool about this, is that when you read the translation of the verses that had the first rhyme scheme, you'll notice that Allah is narrating the stories of the prophets. So he uses a particular rhyme scheme for that. As soon as the subject changes, the rhyme scheme also changes.

You know how in literature, when you want to start a new thought, you start it in a new paragrpah, with an indentation. Quran does not have paragraphs in its SURAHS. The Quran's way of expressing a change in its subject, is by changing its rhyme scheme.

So in this Surah Maryam, Allah is talking about the prophets using the rhyme scheme of

⟪ar-quote:⟪ar-quote:زَكَرِيَّآ⟫، خَفِیَّا، شَقِیَّا، وَلِیَّا، ⟪ar-quote:رَضِيًّۭا⟫، نَبِیَّا، ⟪ar-quote:سَمِيًّۭا⟫⟫

Then Allah changes the subject and begins talking about himself. That he is the true master; and the only one worthy of worhsip; and how the disbelievers are in a state of great loss for not believing in him; and so he changes the rhyme scheme to

⟪ar-quote:يَمْتَرُونَ,   ⟪ar-quote:فَيَكُونُ,   ⟪ar-quote:مُّسْتَقِيمٌۭ⟫,  ⟪ar-quote:عَظِيمٍ⟫,  ⟪ar-quote:مُّبِينٍۢ⟫,   ⟪ar-quote:يُؤْمِنُونَ⟫,  ⟪ar-quote:يُرْجَعُونَ⟫⟫⟫

Do you see that? As soon as the subject changes, the rhyme scheme also changes. And this is so that the listner could know that now a new subject is being talked about. But whats SO interesting, SO  amazing, is that when Allah returns back to the previous subject; when he returns back to talking about the prophets again, he picks up the same old rhyme scheme again. And this is why when you get to verse 41, you get the original rhyme scheme back.

⟪ar-quote:وَٱذْكُرْ فِى ٱلْكِتَبِ إِبْرَهِيمَ ۚ إِنَّهُۥ كَانَ صِدِّيقًۭا نَّبِيًّا⟫

⟪ar-quote:إِذْ قَالَ لِأَبِيهِ يَٓأَبَتِ لِمَ تَعْبُدُ مَا لَا يَسْمَعُ وَلَا يُبْصِرُ وَلَا يُغْنِى عَنكَ شَيْـًۭٔا⟫

Back to the old rhyme scheme, because he's talking about prophets again.So he goes back to

⟪ar-quote:نَّبِيًّا⟫

⟪ar-quote:شَيْـًۭٔا ‎⟫

⟪ar-quote:سَوِيًّۭا ‎⟫

⟪ar-quote:عَصِيًّۭا ‎⟫

⟪ar-quote:وَلِيًّۭا ‎⟫

SubhanAllah!

A word that is not poetry. A message that is dealing with very very serious subjects. And yet for the listner who is carefully listening to the message, knows that the subject is one, because the rhyme scheme is one. And as soon as the rhyme scheme changes, the subject has advanced to something else. And when the rhyme returns, it was because that tangent was necessary to complete the original subject. SubhanAllah! Show me another impromptu speech! Show me another written document for crying out loud that does that! Show me a document that does that consistently through out its text. SubhanAllah!

For those of you who know surah AnNaba, it begins with Allah repremanding disbelievers. So he uses a particular rhyme scheme:

⟪ar-quote:عَم يَتَسَآءَلُونَ⟫

⟪ar-quote:‏عَنِ ٱلنَّبَإِ ٱلْعَظِيمِ⟫   ⟪ar-quote:‏ٱلَّذِى هُمْ فِيهِ مُخْتَلِفُونَ⟫

⟪ar-quote:‏كَلَّا سَيَعْلَمُونَ ‎⟫

⟪ar-quote:‏ثُمَّ كَلَّا سَيَعْلَمُونَ⟫

Subject changes, and Allah begins reminding them of his favors

⟪ar-quote:‏أَلَمْ نَجْعَلِ ٱلْأَرْضَ مِهَدًۭا⟫

⟪ar-quote:وَٱلْجِبَالَ أَوْتَادًۭا⟫

⟪ar-quote:‏وَخَلَقْنَكُمْ أَزْوَجًۭا⟫

⟪ar-quote:‏وَجَعَلْنَا نَوْمَكُمْ سُبَاتًۭا⟫

⟪ar-quote:‏وَجَعَلْنَا ٱلَّيْلَ لِبَاسًۭا⟫
SubhanAllah! One subject is done, the next one has its own rhyme scheme. And what's so miraculous is how consistent this is across the Quran.

And sometimes you will have long passages with the same exact rhyme scheme with something interjecting in between, that doesn't fit the rhyme scheme... You know why?  because that tangent is necessary for the rst of it and you have to pay intention.. Allah will say

⟪ar-quote:لَآ أُقْسِمُ بِيَوْمِ ٱلْقِيَمَةِ⟫
⟪ar-quote:‏وَلَآ أُقْسِمُ بِٱلنَّفْسِ ٱللَّوَّامَةِ⟫
⟪ar-quote:‏أَيَحْسَبُ ٱلْإِنسَنُ أَلَّن نَّجْمَعَ عِظَامَهُۥ⟫
⟪ar-quote:‏بَلَىٰ قَدِرِينَ عَلَىٰٓ أَن نُّسَوِّىَ بَنَانَهُۥ⟫
⟪ar-quote:‏بَلْ يُرِيدُ ٱلْإِنسَنُ لِيَفْجُرَ أَمَامَهُۥ⟫
⟪ar-quote:‏يَسْـَٔلُ أَيَّانَ يَوْمُ ٱلْقِيَمَةِ⟫

Subject changes....

⟪ar-quote:‏فَإِذَا بَرِقَ ٱلْبَصَرُ⟫
⟪ar-quote:‏وَخَسَفَ ٱلْقَمَرُ⟫
⟪ar-quote:‏وَجُمِعَ ٱلشَّمْسُ وَٱلْقَمَرُ⟫
⟪ar-quote:‏يَقُولُ ٱلْإِنسَنُ يَوْمَئِذٍ أَيْنَ ٱلْمَفَرُّ⟫
⟪ar-quote:‏كَلَّا لَا وَزَرَ⟫
⟪ar-quote:‏إِلَىٰ رَبِّكَ يَوْمَئِذٍ ٱلْمُسْتَقَرُّ⟫
⟪ar-quote:‏يُنَبَّؤُا۟ ٱلْإِنسَنُ يَوْمَئِذٍۭ بِمَا قَدَّمَ وَأَخَّر⟫

Subject changes

⟪ar-quote:‏بَلِ ٱلْإِنسَنُ عَلَىٰ نَفْسِهِۦ بَصِيرَةٌۭ⟫
⟪ar-quote:‏وَلَوْ أَلْقَىٰ مَعَاذِيرَهُۥ⟫

Then a small tangent, because Allah needs to tell us something which is important to understand what's coming ahead... So he changes the rhyme scheme for just one ayah...
⟪ar-quote:‏لَا تُحَرِّكْ بِهِۦ لِسَانَكَ لِتَعْجَلَ بِهِۦٓ⟫

And then returns back to the original subject at the beginning of the surah

⟪ar-quote:‏إِنَّ عَلَيْنَا جَمْعَهُۥ وَقُرْآنَهُ⟫
⟪ar-quote:‏فَإِذَا قَرَأْنَهُ فَٱتَّبِعْ قُرْآنَهُ⟫
⟪ar-quote:ثُمَّ إِنَّ عَلَيْنَا بَيَانَهُۥ⟫

SubhanAllah! It is SO incredible!! A rhyme scheme that tracks the subject matter. Explain to me how is this possible with spoken conversation. How do you use a rhyme scheme to track the subject matter? Consistently across a book that contains over 6000 verses! AllahuAkbar!
